# Unicorn Overlord Relationship Dialogue

## Main Relationships

### Adel

#### Adel and Alain - Tavern Praise

Adel: He's just... the best leader any of us could've ever asked for.

Clive: That's quite enough eulogizing for one evening, Adel. And perhaps you should consider laying off the ale as well.

Adel: But you agree with me, don't you? You gotta.

Adel: A guy like him's gonna be a great king. I'm sure of it.

Adel: Down with Zenoira. Long live the amazing King Alain!

Clive: Adel, please! There can be no telling what enemy soldiers might lie within earshot.

Alain: Oh, erm... 'Tis a fine evening we're having, is it not?

Adel: Your Highness! What are you doing here?

Berenice: Now this was worth coming to town for.

Alain: A word, Adel.

Adel: Please tell me you didn't hear all that. I mean... ahem.

Clive: It seems your penchant for drunken outbursts has finally caught up to you.

Adel: I'll not touch another drop of ale again, I promise.

Alain: In fact, I'm glad to hear how highly you think of me, if not a bit embarrassed by it.

Adel: Thank you for saying so, Your Highness.

Clive: You're lucky he's as generous a man as he is, Adel. Anyone else, and you would have been cast from our army entirely.

#### Adel and Alain - Apology

Adel: Your Highness?

Alain: What is it, Adel?

Adel: Well, I want to apologize for my actions at that tavern back in Cornia.

Alain: Do you mean that drunken evening you did nothing but sing my praises?

Adel: I do indeed.

Alain: Though perhaps you should consider keeping your voice down in the future.

Adel: I will, Your Highness.

Adel: I truly do believe you'll be one of the finest kings our land has ever seen.

Alain: Do you, now?

Adel: I would feel the same, even if you didn't belong to the royal family.

Adel: Your leadership and the kindness you show your soldiers come not from days in the castle, but those spent marching with our army.

Adel: To me, you're everything Cornia could ever hope for in a ruler.

Alain: Thank you for saying so, Adel.

Alain: Yet I wonder, where is this outpour of emotion even coming from?

Adel: I want you to know how I truly feel, and I want you to be certain it comes from me, not the alcohol.

Alain: I'm sorry to interrupt, Adel, but how long do you plan on flattering me for?

Adel: Are you all right, Your Highness? Your face is as red as mine after a long night of drinking.

#### Adel and Alain - Ring of the Maiden

Adel: You wanted to speak with me, Your Highness?

Alain: I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

Adel: Are you sure I'm worthy of it?

Alain: Yes, and so much beyond it as well. There's no man I trust more in this world than you, Adel.

Alain: But I won't force the matter. The decision to accept it or not lies solely on your shoulders.

Adel: Please, Your Highness, you needn't look so downcast.

Adel: This is an immense honor, and one I would be a fool to refuse.

Adel: It's merely... I've never received an offer from another man before. Natural it would paralyze me a little.

Alain: Apologies, Adel. I took our friendship for granted and failed to consider how you might feel.

Alain: So let me ask the question anew.

Adel: Ah. That's how you meant it.

Adel: But of course, Your Highness. I'll endure any task for the sake of our nation.

Alain: Our covenant is sworn.

Alain: Will you stand beside me through the trials ahead, my friend?

Adel: As if you even have to ask. I'll be at your side, Your Highness.

#### Adel and Alain - Final Battle

Galerius: End this, now.

Galerius: Hmph.

Galerius: Gah.

Alain: Mother!

Galerius: How does it feel, hm? Your dear mother, slain by your own hand?

Alain: What is happening to me?

Adel: Your Highness?

Galerius: What a poor fool he was, doomed to the same fate as the pitiful queen before him.

Galerius: His strength surpasses even Ilenia's. The might of the unicorn runs deep in his veins.

Galerius: The ring is mine to command, and a futile demise is all that awaits you now.

Galerius: None can ever hope to halt my designs. Bow to your emperor.

Galerius: This day is won by my hand.

Galerius: You will make a fine Zenoiran vessel once it is over.

Galerius: Enough. Can't you see it's over?

Galerius: The ring...

Galerius: But why does it hold such vast energy?

Adel: I know you're still in there, Your Highness.

Adel: Return to my side, I beg of you.

Galerius: It will take more than this to defeat me.

Adel: Your Highness!

Alain: Galerius. You saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire.

Alain: But as long as I live and breathe, you'll never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

Galerius: How do you know of that?

Galerius: You will not!

Galerius: Their emperor shall never know defeat.

Baltro: Your Majesty.

Galerius: How goes the rite?

Galerius: Then these insects shall be more than enough. Grant me your strength, and we'll stamp them out together.

Galerius: What do you think you're doing?

Baltro: If it wasn't clear, Your Majesty, the sigil seeks none other.

Galerius: Traitorous fool. Finally gone senile, hm?

Alain: Mother!

Ilenia: Ngh.

Adel: She's breathing.

Alain: Speak to me, please.

Alain: Josef, see my mother somewhere safe.

Josef: And you, Your Highness?

Alain: We end this long-drawn war now.

Adel: I'm ever with you, Your Highness.

Josef: Come home, both of you.

Baltro: What evil should I reanimate next? A monster capable of crushing you beneath its heel, perhaps.

Adel: You are the true monster here, sorcerer.

Alain: Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call.

Alain: Your emperor is no more, and in his place stands a tyrannical fiend who craves nothing but absolute control.

Alain: Tell me, is this what you truly desire? To sacrifice your very essence in service of this daemon?

Alain: Souls of the departed, if you have any humanity left within you, lend me your aid.

Alain: These souls are not a power one can wield, Baltro. They are human lives, human will in its purest form.

Alain: Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Adel and Alain - Ending

Adel: It almost brings a tear to my eye.

Adel: Back at the altar, when you called me your friend, did you mean to imply we stand as equals in your mind?

Adel: 'Cause, yeah, that's enough to make a guy blush.

Adel: Well, Clive? You gonna drink with me or what?

Clive: Easy, my friend.

Clive: What a shame it would be to forget the only coronation His Majesty will ever have.

Adel: Fine, fine. I guess I've had enough fun for one day.

### Amalia

#### Amalia and Alain - Ring of the Maiden

Alain: I would like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

Amalia: Sorry. I think there has been a mistake.

Alain: No mistake. I want you to have it.

Amalia: It would not even fit on my finger.

Alain: Does that mean you accept?

Amalia: Not yet. We are going to have some fun together, you and me.

Alain: A test of might. That explains why you asked me to bring a sword.

Alain: And should I win, I get to request anything I wish. That was the bargain, yes?

Amalia: If you are ready for rejection, I will take whatever you have got.

Alain: Very well. Then I will have to show you how I feel through martial prowess.

Alain: It seems I have won.

Amalia: The ring will not fit my finger, but I can wear it around my neck. No problem.

Alain: Amalia. Thank you.

Amalia: You are the strongest man I have ever met. strong enough to dethrone the champ.

Amalia: If you want me sticking around, I will stick around.

#### Amalia and Alain - Galerius

Alain: Galerius, Emperor of Zenoira.

Alain: Your ambitions are laid bare, and your empire in ruin.

Galerius: If you hope to speak, you will find me no willing participant. I have no words for you.

Galerius: End this, now.

Alain: strike him down. Emancipate his soul.

Alain: strike him down.

Galerius: Hmph?

Galerius: Gah.

Alain: What?

Josef: Alain! Your Majesty!

Alain: Mother!

Galerius: Hahahaha. How does it feel, hm? Your dear mother, slain by your own hand.

Alain: What is happening to me?

Amalia: Hey. Snap out of it!

Galerius: His strength surpasses even Ilenia's. The might of the unicorn runs deep in his veins.

Galerius: You would simply be volunteering your own body as my next vessel.

Galerius: The ring is mine to command, and a futile demise is all that awaits you now.

Amalia: Knew you were tougher than that, Alain. Now show me what you can do.

Galerius: It will take more than this to defeat me.

Amalia: I am just glad you are back.

Alain: You saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire.

Alain: But as long as I live and breathe, you will never inflict such callous devastation on the world.

Alain: Piteous ghost of an age long past, I shall grant your soul the freedom it desires.

Galerius: You will not!

Galerius: While the souls of Zenoira remain trapped, their emperor shall never know defeat.

#### Amalia and Alain - Baltro

Baltro: Your Majesty.

Galerius: How goes the rite?

Galerius: Then these insects shall be more than enough. Grant me your strength, and we will stamp them out together.

Amalia: Like we would roll over for you!

Galerius: What do you think you are doing?

Baltro: If it was not clear, Your Majesty, the sigil seeks none other...

Galerius: Traitorous fool. Finally gone senile, hm?

Galerius: Raagh!

Alain: Mother!

Ilenia: Ngh.

Alain: Speak to me, please.

Josef: I never imagined he possessed such frightful mastery over the bodies of others.

Ilenia: Alain. I cannot say how much time has passed since that day, but you have grown so much.

Ilenia: If only I could have been there to witness it.

Ilenia: It seems I owe Josef a great deal for raising you in my absence.

Alain: Josef, see my mother somewhere safe.

Josef: And you, Your Highness?

Alain: We end this long-drawn war here and now.

Josef: Come home, both of you.

Baltro: What evil should I reanimate next? A monster capable of crushing you beneath its heel, perhaps.

Amalia: Come on, Alain. Let us show him what he is up against.

Alain: Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call.

Alain: Your emperor is no more, and in his place stands a tyrannical fiend who craves nothing but absolute control.

Alain: Tell me, is this what you truly desire? To sacrifice your very essence in service of this daemon?

Alain: Souls of the departed, if you have any humanity left within you, lend me your aid.

Baltro: You ruined everything, accursed fool!

Alain: These souls are not a power one can wield, Baltro. They are human lives, human will in its purest form.

Alain: Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Amalia and Alain - Ending

Amalia: Before today, I could barely walk down the street without people cowering in fear at the sight of me.

Amalia: Guess that shows what swearing an oath can do.

Amalia: All I have ever cared about is strength, you know, but this is not so bad either.

Amalia: Though I am not sure I will ever get used to people calling me queen.

Amalia: Let us just forget I ever said that.

#### Amalia and Alain - A Remote Home

Alain: I take it the flames of this brutal war never reached your home?

Amalia: It was the kind of place you could spend years looking for and never come close to finding.

Alain: Why would you live in such a remote region?

Amalia: My father wanted to keep an heir hidden away. If anyone caught on, an heir would be the least of his worries.

Amalia: Bastard.

Alain: That only raises another question. Why did you leave?

Amalia: Because I started training. Learned all the techniques my proud ancestor was so eager to pass down.

Alain: You mean to say your skill is entirely self-taught?

Amalia: Sure is. And now I never have to worry about that again.

Alain: I suppose not.

Amalia: The coliseum was the only thing I was after when I left.

Alain: I imagine you rather enjoyed that part, given the powerful opponents you were able to face.

Amalia: You get me better than most do, Alain.

Amalia: Even without the old man pushing me to do it, I would have wound up chasing strength.

Alain: Then I am glad you decided to join us rather than our enemies. Thank you again, Amalia.

Amalia: Easy does it.

### Aramis

#### Aramis and Alain - Living as Aramis

Alain: I must know, Aramis. Do you still plan to continue on as a mercenary, even after the war?

Aramis: I'll not be returning to the royal family, if that's what you ask.

Alain: Has abandoning your lineage not proven difficult at times?

Aramis: Yet in order to conform to my surroundings, I cast those teachings aside and began to emulate the mercenaries around me.

Aramis: And as I did, I began to prove in a way that I needn't let my bloodline define who I am.

Alain: Ah.

Aramis: Yet death was not the answer I sought. Not while I knew that Gilbert was still alive.

Aramis: And now, he has finally reclaimed our lands from Zenoira's clutches, owing entirely to you.

Alain: Whether it be in his duty as your king, or simply as your loving brother.

Aramis: Then it would seem I've no choice but to live on, both for my nation and for Gilbert.

#### Aramis and Alain - After the War

Alain: If I may, Aramis, what do you intend to do once this war reaches its conclusion?

Aramis: Even once the fighting has ended, there shall be towns in need of aid, innocent people who seek to begin their lives anew.

Alain: Indeed there shall.

Aramis: Yet it's rather an interesting question. You speak as though you're certain we'll be victorious.

Alain: Certain may not be the correct word, though I assure you, I don't plan to let Zenoira defeat us.

Alain: Even should we claim victory in this conquest, much work shall remain to be done.

Aramis: And I'll not see you suffer as I had all those years.

Alain: Agonizing over your future, you mean?

Aramis: Precisely so.

Aramis: I dreamt of ascending the throne, of one day reshaping Drakenhold into the nation my father wished it could be.

Aramis: Yet when Zenoira struck, such dreams only served to cloud my vision, and the man known as Ludwig perished in the ensuing battle.

Aramis: To seize the disgraced Cornia as our own, thus prevailing in the centuries-long feud between our kingdoms.

Alain: Aramis.

Aramis: Yet I demand you save such kindness for those who deserve it more than I.

Alain: Listen to me, Aramis.

Alain: You wished that I not suffer the same mistakes as you, out of the compassion you bear for me as a friend.

Alain: And I must admit, I worry for you as well.

Aramis: Well, then. Not a soul in the world could remain callous in the face of such words.

Aramis: Pray, do not hesitate to do the same.

Alain: I won't.

#### Aramis and Alain - Ring of the Maiden

Alain: I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

Aramis: As I expected. Very well.

Alain: You aren't going to think about it first?

Aramis: What is there to think about? I know what must be done, and know we share a common purpose.

Aramis: Together, we will bring Zenoira down and restore a lasting peace to Fevrith. To our homes.

Aramis: I may be but a humble mercenary, yet I can offer a sharper sword and sturdier shield than almost any other.

Alain: And I'm ever grateful to have them, Aramis.

Aramis: Now then. I've heard the greater the trust between us, the grander the power our rings will bear.

Aramis: Thankfully, it goes without saying that our bond is stronger than any other.

Alain: Agreed.

Aramis: Even should the blade I wield crumble to dust, no impediment is too great with you at my side.

Aramis: I only ask that you never leave it. Not until I can prove I can avail my people.

Aramis: My nation and my brother need that assurance now more than ever.

#### Aramis and Alain - Final Battle

Galerius: End this, now.

Galerius: Hmph.

Galerius: Gah.

Alain: Mother!

Galerius: How does it feel, hm? Your dear mother, slain by your own hand?

Alain: What is happening to me?

Aramis: Alain!

Galerius: What a poor fool he was, doomed to the same fate as the pitiful queen before him.

Galerius: His strength surpasses even Ilenia's. The might of the unicorn runs deep in his veins.

Galerius: strike at this new body of mine, if you dare.

Galerius: You'd simply be volunteering your own as my next vessel.

Galerius: The ring is mine to command, and a futile demise is all that awaits you now.

Galerius: None can ever hope to halt my designs. Bow to your emperor.

Aramis: Ngh!

Galerius: This day is won.

Galerius: You will make a fine Zenoiran vessel once it is over.

Galerius: Enough. Can't you see it's over?

Galerius: The ring...

Galerius: But why does it hold such vast energy?

Galerius: It will take more than this to defeat me.

Aramis: Alain!

Alain: Galerius. You saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire.

Alain: But as long as I live and breathe, you'll never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

Galerius: You will not!

Galerius: Their emperor shall never know defeat.

Baltro: Your Majesty.

Galerius: How goes the rite?

Galerius: Then these insects shall be more than enough. Grant me your strength, and we'll stamp them out together.

Baltro: If it wasn't clear, Your Majesty, the sigil seeks none other.

Galerius: Traitorous fool. Finally gone senile, hm?

Alain: Mother!

Ilenia: Ngh.

Aramis: Worry not, Alain. She still lives.

Alain: Speak to me, please.

Josef: I never imagined he possessed such frightful mastery over the bodies of others.

Ilenia: Alain. I can't say how much time has passed since that day, but you've grown so much.

Ilenia: If only I could have been there to witness it.

Ilenia: It seems I owe Josef a great deal for raising you in my absence.

Alain: Josef, see my mother somewhere safe.

Josef: And you, Your Highness?

Alain: We end this long-drawn war now.

Aramis: Indeed, and pen a new future for all of Fevrith, the very peace we've always dreamed of.

Josef: Come home, both of you.

Baltro: What evil should I reanimate next? A monster capable of crushing you beneath its heel, perhaps.

Aramis: You'll do nothing of the sort. Your schemes shall end here, lost where you yourself deserve to be.

Alain: Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call.

Alain: Your emperor is no more, and in his place stands a tyrannical fiend who craves nothing but absolute control.

Alain: Tell me, is this what you truly desire? To sacrifice your very essence in service of this daemon?

Alain: Souls of the departed, if you have any humanity left within you, lend me your aid.

Alain: These souls are not a power one can wield, Baltro. They are human lives, human will in its purest form.

Alain: Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Aramis and Alain - Ending

Aramis: All I could do was become another man entirely, and struggle desperately against the tide of oppression.

Aramis: I shall always be grateful for that gift.

Aramis: Know that however far I may be, I shall never stop believing in your cause.

Aramis: By now, I fear simply praying for your success from the dark shadows of Drakenhold may no longer satisfy my desire to help.

Aramis: As a friend, that is.

Gilbert: Thus we stand not only as friends, but brethren in kingship of our respective nations.

Gilbert: In truth, I had once imagined the throne to be a cold place. A solitary prison formed of duty and formality.

Gilbert: I owe that in part to my subjects, of course, but none have nurtured that flame greater than you.

Gilbert: May our paths run ever in partnership, my friend.

Gloucester: In truth, I wasn't aware that Cornia was quite this beautiful in her full glory.

Gloucester: I only hope I can stimulate the growth of my own home in such a stark manner.

Gloucester: Have you found the occasion to speak with your brother, Ser Aramis?

Aramis: Briefly, yes. Best not to raise suspicions, if at all possible.

Gloucester: King Gilbert seemed rather overjoyed when I spoke to him earlier.

Leah: I have to say, Ser Aramis, I'm rather surprised to see you in attendance.

Aramis: I must take care to keep my identity concealed.

Leah: If nothing else, I hope you can be at ease amongst our friends.

Aramis: Thank you, Leah. I shall endeavor to do just that.

### Aubin

#### Aubin Recruited

Alain: Alone, are you?

Lex: What happened to your friends?

Aubin: Long gone by now, what with all the time I bought them. Never could have done it without you lot chasing me halfway to hell and back, though.

Chloe: The fort is empty. Not a soul in sight.

Lex: Guy laid out the bait, and we just had to take a nibble.

Alain: Strange. Few leaders would play the sacrificial lamb in such a predicament.

Aubin: Do not flatter yourselves. That is just part of the job. You are gambling with your life the second you take that coin.

Lex: Then you know how this ends.

Alain: Stay your blade, Lex. There is something I need to ask him.

Alain: What does Galerius want with Scarlett? I will take any scraps of information you may have.

Aubin: You do realize I am just hired steel, yeah? Sorry, but I am not a questions kind of guy, least not past my bottom line.

Lex: Well? What do we do with him?

Alain: Let us say I offered to fill those pockets instead. What then?

Aubin: First I would ask if you still had all your marbles. But I am not the discriminating type, long as the pay is right.

Lex: If this is supposed to be a joke, I am not laughing. We are trying to beat the enemy, not hire them.

Alain: It is not every day you come across a man willing to greet the heavens in order to see his allies safe.

Alain: Our aim is to liberate these lands from the oppressive clutches of Zenoira and its emperor.

Aubin: I had heard you were nothing more than the crumbs of some spineless resistance that got chewed up and spat back out.

Aubin: Never would have guessed you were really just a pack of reckless lunatics.

Chloe: This so-called lunatic is none other than Prince Alain, true-born heir to the Cornian throne. Our war is a righteous one.

Aubin: You are trotting around the crowned brat of a dead and gone kingdom, trying to flip a whole damn empire?

Aubin: Sorry, kids, but I do not like those odds.

Lex: Does not sound like he is interested.

Aubin: Hope you know I do not come cheap.

Alain: Does that mean you will join us?

Aubin: Granted you are willing to foot the bill. Kingmaking is not an everyday job for a merc.

Aubin: You have seen enough to know I am worth the gold and more.

#### Aubin and Alain - Different Kind of Boss

Aubin: I have got to say, I did not think people this damn nice were really out there.

Alain: Who are you speaking of?

Aubin: You, boss. Who has ever heard of a guy asking an enemy soldier to join up with him?

Aubin: Maybe that kind of mercy is what being king is all about.

Alain: I do not know about that.

Aubin: Good to see you staying humble about it.

Aubin: You really are different, boss. With you, we get the same kind of respect any knight would.

Alain: I look forward to fighting beside you.

Aubin: Looking forward to it.

#### Aubin and Alain - The Sea

Alain: What a gorgeous vista this is. I had no idea scenery like this existed within Cornia's borders.

Aubin: Sure, we got plenty o' ruins back home too, but nothin' beats this, if ya ask me.

Alain: It's interesting you say that. To me, both our lands have their own unique charm.

Aubin: Once I'd finally did it, that's when Zenoira showed up. Took the damn dream right outta my hands. Wish everyone back home could know this feelin'.

Alain: 'Tis a noble wish indeed, Aubin.

Aubin: We don't know when this war's gonna be over, either. But...

Alain: Let me help you, Aubin.

Aubin: You, huh? Not sure how I feel about askin' favors from a prince.

Alain: If anyone is capable of achieving such a dream, it's you. Think of the joy our people will know once you have.

Aubin: No arguin' with that. Well then, what're we waitin' for? We got ourselves a war to win!

Alain: And win it we shall. Both of us, together.

#### Aubin and Alain - Ring of the Maiden

Aubin: You were asking for me, boss?

Alain: I would like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

Aubin: Does not seem like you are pulling my leg, from the look of you. Mind if I ask why?

Alain: Swearing an oath with the person I trust most is the only way to draw out the ring's true power. That person is you.

Alain: That is more than enough reason for me.

Aubin: Here I was thinking I would pack up after the war, go home, and kick my feet up.

Aubin: But if you are offering a sweeter deal, I would be dumber than camel dung to say no.

Aubin: Looks like we have ourselves a deal. Nobody is stopping us, not now, not ever.

Alain: There is that confidence. I knew you were the right man for the task.

Aubin: Like anyone else could fill these boots. Now come on, we have got an emperor to topple.

#### Aubin and Alain - Final Battle

Galerius: End this, now.

Galerius: Hmph.

Galerius: Gah.

Alain: Mother!

Galerius: How does it feel, hm? Your dear mother, slain by your own hand.

Alain: What is happening to me?

Aubin: Eyes up, Alain.

Galerius: What a poor fool he was, doomed to the same fate as the pitiful queen before him.

Galerius: His strength surpasses even Ilenia's. The might of the unicorn runs deep in his veins.

Galerius: strike at this new body of mine, if you dare. You would simply be volunteering your own as my next vessel.

Galerius: The ring is mine to command, and a futile demise is all that awaits you now.

Galerius: None can ever hope to halt my designs. Bow to your emperor.

Aubin: Dammit.

Galerius: The ring... why does it hold such vast energy?

Aubin: I knew you would not give up that easy. Come on, let us send this ghost packing.

Galerius: It will take more than this to defeat me.

Aubin: Alain!

Alain: Galerius. You saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire.

Alain: But as long as I live and breathe, you will never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

Galerius: How do you know of that?

Galerius: You will not!

Galerius: Their emperor shall never know defeat.

Baltro: Your Majesty.

Galerius: How goes the rite?

Galerius: Then these insects shall be more than enough. Grant me your strength, and we will stamp them out together.

Baltro: If it was not clear, Your Majesty, the sigil seeks none other.

Galerius: Traitorous fool. Finally gone senile, hm?

Alain: Mother!

Ilenia: Ngh.

Aubin: It is all good, Alain. She is breathing, and steadily at that.

Alain: Speak to me, please.

Alain: Josef, see my mother somewhere safe.

Josef: And you, Your Highness?

Alain: We end this long-drawn war now.

Aubin: That sack of bones will not know what hit him.

Josef: Come home, both of you.

Baltro: What evil should I reanimate next? A monster capable of crushing you beneath its heel, perhaps.

Aubin: We only got one monster here. Name is Baltro. Now get ready.

Alain: Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call.

Alain: Your emperor is no more, and in his place stands a tyrannical fiend who craves nothing but absolute control.

Alain: Tell me, is this what you truly desire? To sacrifice your very essence in service of this daemon?

Alain: Souls of the departed, if you have any humanity left within you, lend me your aid.

Alain: These souls are not a power one can wield, Baltro. They are human lives, human will in its purest form.

Alain: Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Aubin and Alain - Ending

Aubin: About time you went and made yourself king.

Aubin: Feels pretty good, knowing the two of us are what made it happen.

Aubin: still, I could do worse than helping folks out for a living. Hell, I might even enjoy it.

Aubin: Did not really feel like it, but we were fighting a long time there.

Aubin: A real relief knowing our desert is still alive and kicking, too.

#### Aubin and Alain

Aubin: Gotta say, didn't think people this damn nice were really out there. Hahaha. I'm talkin' about you, boss. Who's ever heard of a guy askin' an enemy soldier to join up with 'em? Maybe that kinda mercy's what bein' king is all about.

Aubin: But ya really are different, boss. With you, we get given the same kinda respect that any knight would.

### Auch

#### Auch Recruited

Auch: All our endeavors, and not a scrap of progress to show for it.

Auch: Nothing to rival my brother's accomplishments. No hope to vie for Mother's affection.

Auch: Double our headcount. Find anyone willing to hold a spade. I'll handle their wages.

Soldier: Dire news, my lord. It's the rebels. They're coming our way.

Auch: Truly a fly in the ointment.

Soldier: That's not all, my lord. It seems Alain's the one leading them.

Auch: Then their feeble resistance should prove a simple task and earn me some deserved glory besides.

Auch: And Mother will have no choice but to be pleased with me.

Auch: Ah, the familiar taste of failure.

Auch: So this is how it ends. Pitifully, without a single word of praise in all my years. Was it really so much to ask?

Auch: Apparently so. My ashes will scatter like dust to the wind, and what little I amounted to in this life will go with them.

Josef: Alain. What do you wish to do with him, Your Highness?

Alain: Sorcerer Auch. I'd ask you to lend us your craft in the days ahead.

Auch: Come again?

Alain: Take arms with the Liberation.

Auch: You want me?

Auch: I've done no great deeds, even amongst my peers. And what little I can do is just a pale imitation.

Auch: It's sad, but true. Not even Mother could find it in her heart to praise a boy as miserable as me.

Alain: Your survey of these ruins is evidence enough that such scholarly prowess would surely aid our legion.

Alain: Our numbers grow stronger and larger with every passing day. Numbers I would like to count you among.

Auch: I'd be lying if I said it wasn't a curious thing, this marvel we call life.

Auch: My staff is yours to command, Your Highness.

Auch: And when you think about it, there can be no greater feat in the world than bringing Zenoira to its knees.

Auch: Perhaps that will be how I finally earn my mother's approval.

Auch: This wasn't an outcome I expected when I stepped out of my tent this morning, but it may be just the one I wanted.

Auch: I'm at your service, Your Highness. This land belongs to the Liberation now.

#### Auch and Alain - A Combat Theory

Auch: Could you spare a moment, Your Highness?

Alain: What is it, Auch?

Auch: I was hoping I might test a theory the next time Zenoira strikes. I will need more sorcerers if I am to do so.

Alain: In that case, I will have some transferred from another unit right away.

Auch: You would truly do that for me? It is still only an idea, and I have no guarantee it will prove effective.

Alain: Nor will you until you have the opportunity to assess its utility in genuine combat.

Alain: Should it fail, I have every faith you will see its flaws refined. And perhaps even more so should it succeed.

Auch: Well... yes. I suppose so.

Auch: You treat me not with the contempt I would expect from a royal prince, but with care and respect for your common man.

Alain: Seeing how little I know of the finer points of magick, it is of merit indeed to have you around.

Auch: I will do whatever I must to remain worthy of that praise.

Alain: I am certain you will.

#### Auch and Alain - The Sorcerers' Accident

Auch: This can't be happening. Not after I promised His Highness I would earn his praise.

Liberation Sorcerer: Ser Auch, it was a simple accident, and a wholly out of our control one at that. You can't blame yourself for such things.

Liberation Sorcerer: Besides, the rite itself was practically perfect. Take heart in that, if nothing else.

Auch: Fools. Your necks aren't the ones on the chopping block here.

Auch: I'm sorry. I... I didn't mean to.

Auch: It should be no surprise they'd think to abandon me.

Auch: But my search for glory goes on yet. Both for Mother and for Alain.

Alain: Good evening, Auch.

Auch: Your Highness? What are you doing here?

Alain: I've come to speak about what transpired between you and those sorcerers just now.

Auch: You saw that, did you? Go on, then. Scold me however you will.

Auch: I knew the day would come that you cast me from your army.

Alain: I'm not certain what you mean.

Auch: Don't lie to me. You must regret ever letting a failure such as I walk amongst you.

Alain: No, I-

Auch: Not another word. Just go. Abandon me like all the rest.

Alain: stop talking and listen for a moment, Auch. I'm only here because I worry for you.

Auch: You... what?

Alain: As do your fellow sorcerers, actually. They seemed convinced you wouldn't listen were it coming from them.

Liberation Sorcerer: Right you are, Your Highness. Yours is the sole voice that Auch has ears for.

Liberation Sorcerer: Though it did leave a fairly unsightly mark. Have you considered learning the art of fist-fighting instead?

Liberation Sorcerer: Hah! Could you imagine?

Alain: They're quite the pair, those two.

Auch: Hmph. Here I was positively wracked with guilt, and that's their response?

Alain: They haven't abandoned you, Auch. Nor shall I drive you out of the Liberation's ranks.

Alain: It's also why they never utter a word of complaint, no matter how unreasonable your demands may be.

Alain: That is the mark of a true leader, Auch. One I would be a fool to do away with.

Auch: Then... you're sure about this? Despite all of my failings in being of use?

Alain: The day shall never come that I regret enlisting your service.

Auch: Thank you, Your Highness.

Alain: Having said that, I suggest you pay more attention when others are speaking to you. Not only that, but-

Auch: Moved onto the scolding now, have you?

Auch: Though perhaps it's only fair I accept it today.

#### Auch and Alain - Ring of the Maiden

Auch: I know you've only asked me aside for a good cause.

Alain: I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

Auch: Sorry. You what?

Alain: 'Tis no legend, but truth.

Alain: In return, it will unleash the Unicorn's full power, thereby enabling us to smite Galerius once and for all.

Alain: And you, Auch, are the only one I can ask to accept it.

Auch: I can't believe this.

Auch: Have I finally found it, Mother? Finally discovered my purpose on this cruel earth?

Auch: Very well, Alain.

Auch: I've reason to believe that life represents my life's calling, yes.

Alain: I'll treasure this moment for as long as we live.

Auch: As will I, but... I do have one request.

Auch: Would you mind complimenting me every now and then? Maybe once a day? Or constantly, perhaps?

#### Auch and Alain - Final Battle

Galerius: End this, now.

Galerius: Hmph.

Galerius: Gah.

Alain: Mother!

Galerius: How does it feel, hm? Your dear mother, slain by your own hand.

Alain: What is happening to me?

Auch: Alain?

Galerius: What a poor fool he was, doomed to the same fate as the pitiful queen before him.

Galerius: His strength surpasses even Ilenia's. The might of the unicorn runs deep in his veins.

Galerius: You'd simply be volunteering your own as my next vessel.

Galerius: The ring is mine to command, and a futile demise is all that awaits you now.

Galerius: None can ever hope to halt my designs. Bow to your emperor.

Auch: How can I possibly do this on my own?

Galerius: This day is won.

Galerius: You will make a fine Zenoiran vessel once it is over.

Galerius: Enough. Can't you see it's over?

Galerius: The ring...

Galerius: But why does it hold such vast energy?

Auch: As you should. I'm not ready to lose you, Alain, nor will I ever be.

Galerius: It will take more than this to defeat me.

Auch: Alain!

Alain: Galerius. You saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire.

Alain: But as long as I live and breathe, you'll never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

Galerius: How do you know of that?

Galerius: You will not!

Galerius: Their emperor shall never know defeat.

Baltro: Your Majesty.

Galerius: How goes the rite?

Galerius: What do you think you're doing?

Baltro: If it wasn't clear, Your Majesty, the sigil seeks none other.

Galerius: Traitorous fool. Finally gone senile, hm?

Alain: Mother!

Ilenia: Ngh.

Alain: Speak to me, please.

Alain: Josef, see my mother somewhere safe.

Josef: And you, Your Highness?

Auch: Do you hear that, Mother? The prince shall save the world.

Josef: Come home, both of you.

Baltro: What evil should I reanimate next? A monster capable of crushing you beneath its heel, perhaps.

Auch: Your cruelty has plagued this land long enough, Baltro.

Alain: Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call.

Alain: Your emperor is no more, and in his place stands a tyrannical fiend who craves nothing but absolute control.

Alain: Tell me, is this what you truly desire? To sacrifice your very essence in service of this daemon?

Alain: Souls of the departed, if you have any humanity left within you, lend me your aid.

Alain: These souls are not a power one can wield, Baltro. They are human lives, human will in its purest form.

Alain: Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Auch and Alain - Ending

Auch: It's strange, you know.

Auch: Today was meant to be your coronation, but I found myself showered with praise almost as if it were my own.

Auch: You will be praising me after this, yes?

Auch: Do you think her words would be as kind as yours?

Auch: If anything, I had almost forgotten you were royalty during our time with the Liberation.

Auch: I'll always strive to maintain my use to you, no matter what times we're living in.

### Berengaria

#### Berengaria and Alain - Fear

Berengaria: The hell is your deal, Alain?

Alain: I'm sorry?

Berengaria: It's almost scary seeing how easy you make it look.

Berengaria: Why weren't you afraid of me, dammit?

Alain: My lack of experience chief among them.

Alain: In that moment, all I could see was the concern she bore for me. Not even a hint of fear.

Alain: No matter what terror I might feel, my army shall never know a trace of it.

Berengaria: Heh. Makes sense to me.

Berengaria: So, yeah. I'll be here if you ever need to talk.

Alain: You have my thanks, Berengaria.

#### Berengaria and Alain - Letting Guards Down

Berengaria: Well, if it isn't everyone's favorite little workhorse.

Alain: Please, Berengaria. You needn't patronize me.

Berengaria: If everyone keeps treating you like some kind of perfect commander, you'll always feel like you're stuck acting the part.

Alain: That would be rather stifling, yes.

Berengaria: Which means we're free to just breathe. Be ourselves, without giving a damn what anyone else thinks.

Alain: I suppose it would feel rather odd letting my guard down amidst my royal retainers.

Berengaria: Right? Wouldn't want to be caught dead talking to my men like this either.

Alain: You know, Berengaria, I believe that's the first time I've ever seen you laugh like that.

Berengaria: You got a problem with it?

Alain: Not at all. It's almost stunning, in a way.

Berengaria: Hmph. Make fun of me and it'll be the last thing you do.

Alain: Just a little "friendly teasing," as you put it. But I promise I meant every word.

Berengaria: And I don't think anyone's called me it either. But it feels pretty good, knowing you think so.

#### Berengaria and Alain - Countries and Trust

Berengaria: I don't get it. Why do you keep talking to me like this?

Alain: Well, perhaps because I enjoy your company, and the chance to let my guard down, of course.

Alain: But I'll be sure to keep my distance more often, if it troubles you so.

Berengaria: Listen to me, Alain.

Berengaria: You know how you said before it's a good thing we barely know each other? Well, there's a downside to that too.

Alain: Meaning what, precisely?

Berengaria: There's no telling when one of us might turn on the other.

Berengaria: That's how it goes when you're practically strangers.

Berengaria: But if Cornia and Drakenhold ever went to war again, you know which side I'd pick.

Berengaria: Nothing personal.

Alain: That you would betray my trust without the slightest hesitation?

Alain: Or perhaps I've always been a simple pawn in your grand schemes.

Berengaria: If that's what you want to believe, so be it.

Berengaria: Just know, I really have enjoyed our little chats.

Berengaria: Especially when you get all defensive about me deserting you.

Alain: Is this some manner of joke to you, Berengaria?

Berengaria: Sorry. I guess I'm just surprised to see you care so much.

Berengaria: But maybe that means we're not the strangers I thought we were.

Berengaria: Let's just hope our countries don't get in the way of that.

Alain: Yes, let's.

#### Berengaria and Alain - Ring of the Maiden

Berengaria: No thanks.

Alain: I haven't even said anything yet.

Alain: I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

Berengaria: And, uh... not interested, yeah.

Berengaria: There's no guarantee I won't turn on you, or you on me.

Alain: Then we'll face those consequences together.

Alain: We could live a hundred lives, and I would pick you every time.

Berengaria: That's some risk you're taking.

Berengaria: If what they say about your Unicorn and its tradition is true, this covenant represents the strongest bond imaginable.

Berengaria: The sacred kind, where severing it might just cost your life.

Alain: I'll bear any danger should it mean spending that life with you.

Alain: Marry me, Berengaria.

Alain: As stunning as you are now, you'll look even more so in the pure white of a wedding dress.

Berengaria: You're really something.

Alain: I love you. Now and always.

Berengaria: And I hope you're ready to put up with me for the rest of your life.

Berengaria: Your laughter, your tears, your pain, I'm here for all of it.

Berengaria: Once this war's done, I'll be back in Drakenhold where I belong.

Berengaria: And you know what my people think of Cornia. Things go sideways, we'll be at each other's throats before long.

Alain: I would never do that.

Berengaria: We'll see.

#### Berengaria and Alain - Final Battle

Alain: Galerius, Emperor of Zenoira.

Galerius: If you hope to speak, you'll find me no willing participant. I have no words for you.

Galerius: End this, now.

Galerius: Hmph.

Galerius: Gah.

Alain: Mother!

Galerius: How does it feel, hm? Your dear mother, slain by your own hand?

Alain: What is happening to me?

Berengaria: Hey. Stay with me.

Galerius: What a poor fool he was, doomed to the same fate as the pitiful queen before him.

Galerius: The coward steals the body of all who cuts him down.

Galerius: His strength surpasses even Ilenia's. The might of the unicorn runs deep in his veins.

Galerius: You'd simply be volunteering your own as my next vessel.

Galerius: The ring is mine to command, and a futile demise is all that awaits you now.

Galerius: None can ever hope to halt my designs. Bow to your emperor.

Berengaria: Rgh...

Galerius: This day is won.

Galerius: You will make a fine Zenoiran vessel once it is over.

Galerius: Enough. Can't you see it's over?

Galerius: The ring...

Galerius: But why does it hold such vast energy?

Berengaria: Come back to me, Alain. Please.

Galerius: It will take more than this to defeat me.

Berengaria: I'm here for you, Alain.

Alain: Galerius. You saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire.

Alain: But as long as I live and breathe, you'll never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

Galerius: You will not!

Galerius: Their emperor shall never know defeat.

Baltro: Your Majesty.

Galerius: How goes the rite?

Galerius: Then these insects shall be more than enough. Grant me your strength, and we'll stamp them out together.

Galerius: What do you think you're doing?

Baltro: If it wasn't clear, Your Majesty, the sigil seeks none other.

Galerius: Traitorous fool. Finally gone senile, hm?

Alain: Mother!

Ilenia: Ngh.

Berengaria: Alain, she's still breathing. It's okay.

Alain: Speak to me, please.

Josef: I never imagined he possessed such frightful mastery over the bodies of others.

Ilenia: Alain. I can't say how much time has passed since that day, but you've grown so much.

Ilenia: If only I could have been there to witness it.

Alain: Josef, see my mother somewhere safe.

Josef: And you, Your Highness?

Alain: We end this long-drawn war now.

Berengaria: Today's the day Baltro dies.

Baltro: The futile struggle of a rebel...

Alain: Many times you've tried, Baltro, but you shall never break our spirit. I promise you that.

Alain: Now prepare to be vanquished by the might of Fevrith.

Berengaria: Breathe your last, Baltro. I promise it'll be deep.

Baltro: What evil should I reanimate next? A monster capable of crushing you beneath its heel, perhaps.

Berengaria: Enough of your games.

Alain: Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call.

Alain: Your emperor is no more, and in his place stands a tyrannical fiend who craves nothing but absolute control.

Alain: Tell me, is this what you truly desire? To sacrifice your very essence in service of this daemon?

Alain: Souls of the departed, if you have any humanity left within you, lend me your aid.

#### Berengaria and Alain - Ending

Berengaria: You really never change, do you?

Berengaria: If anything, the more time we spend together, the more sure of your stupid decision you get.

Berengaria: And now you barely even leave me alone.

Berengaria: Though... I'm not complaining.

Berengaria: Don't mean to spring this on you two, but what do you say we get back to the old gang?

Travis: You mean rebuild the Tricorns?

Bruno: And with the both of ya back, I bet the rest o' the crew would come runnin' too.

Travis: I'm in if you are, Ren.

Berengaria: Good. Now come on, we've got work to do.

### Berenice

#### Berenice and Alain - The Right Weapon

Berenice: So? What do you think?

Alain: In all honesty, it feels rather different from what I am used to.

Berenice: If you have never trained with one, you will be worn out after just a swing or two. But that is nothing a bit of practice cannot solve.

Alain: Perhaps so, yet I believe I will be better off persisting with my current blade.

Berenice: Better to be a specialist than spread yourself too thin.

Alain: At times I have wondered whether I should learn a variety of weapons, to adapt to any situation we might come across.

Berenice: Not a bad thought, but one expert weapon can take you plenty far.

Alain: By an expert, do you happen to mean yourself?

Berenice: Sorry?

Alain: The confidence with which you cut down mounted opponents, despite your inherent difficulties against them, is remarkable.

Alain: I must admit, the skill you bear with that blade has seen you turn even dire situations in your favor.

Berenice: Easy there, Alain. I did not say all that just to fish for compliments.

Berenice: Any more of that and I might have started blushing.

Berenice: My point is, do not worry about how many weapons you can use. Focus on one and see where it takes you.

Alain: Thank you, Berenice.

Berenice: Any time. Now come on. We have training to get back to.

#### Berenice and Alain - A Rematch

Alain: Yet again your training proves a true test of mettle, Berenice.

Berenice: At least you've got the guts to keep coming back for more. Almost reminds me of myself when I was younger.

Berenice: You probably won't believe it, looking at me, but I got bullied all the time as a kid.

Berenice: And someday, I'm gonna change that.

Alain: I hope you do.

Berenice: You're fighting for the same reason, right? To make a better life for all our people.

Alain: I am. But we really should be getting back to our training now, Berenice.

Berenice: Think I need a little change of pace after all that depressing stuff.

Alain: What did you have in mind?

Berenice: A rematch. I still haven't gotten over losing to you the day we met.

Alain: I should have known you'd suggest another form of exercise.

Berenice: Hey, it's not like you're any better. You and I both know you'd rather be doing this than sewing or painting.

Alain: I won't deny that. And I suppose it would do us well to measure the results of our training.

Berenice: Just don't expect it to go as easy as last time, yeah?

#### Berenice and Alain - Ring of the Maiden

Berenice: Sorry, bad habit.

Alain: We've locked blades countless times of late, and have the scars to prove it.

Alain: And yet, I treasure each one as a symbol of our unity.

Alain: You're the finest partner I could ever ask for, Berenice. Both in sparring and in life.

Berenice: Ugh. I saw this coming from a mile away, but I had no idea it would feel so embarrassing.

Berenice: Just know that I'm not gonna stop training until I finally overtake you.

Berenice: So don't use this oath as an excuse to slack off, or I'll be at your heels the whole time.

Alain: Of course. I'll strive to remain strong and able as long as years allow it.

Berenice: Guess that's it, then.

Berenice: Now, I was thinking we could use a session or two to really get us ready for Galerius. What do you say?

Alain: It would be a pleasure. Wherever you lead, I'll gladly follow.

### Bertrand

#### Bertrand and Alain - A Father's Concern

**Bertrand:** Bastorias is a cold place indeed, but perhaps a pair of mittens can make it a little warmer for you.

**Alain:** I appreciate the thought, Bertrand. Thank you.

**Bertrand:** Ah, and this is some armor commonly used by the bear bloodline, though even a human should have no trouble wearing it.

**Alain:** 'Tis a kind gesture, yet I am not certain I will even be able to move under the weight of such heavy equipment.

**Bertrand:** I merely wish to prepare for any possibility, so I never again come to regret not doing so.

**Alain:** I value that input. But I promise you, all of us are doing everything we can to ensure we live to see another day.

**Bertrand:** My son gave the same assurance, moments before he marched to his death.

**Alain:** I am sorry for making you relive such a painful memory.

**Bertrand:** Do not apologize. To be honest, the reason I have been so insistent on helping you is because of how deeply you remind me of him. But it is clear now that my concern is unneeded.

**Alain:** If it brings you peace of mind, I would gladly accept any kindness you are willing to give.

**Bertrand:** It is a true honor to fight beside one as openhearted as you.

#### Ring of the Maiden

**Bertrand:** Prince Alain, I heard you required something.

**Alain:** Bertrand, I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden. The loss of a son is a fate I would not wish upon my worst enemy. And yet, you have not succumbed to your grief, but instead turned its fervency into strength for the Liberation.

**Alain:** That selflessness commands nothing but the deepest respect, and I would share this covenant with no other.

**Bertrand:** Impressive candor, as always, and a kind heart befitting a king.

**Alain:** Bertrand?

**Bertrand:** Apologies. The conviction in your eyes has more than convinced me. I will accept.

**Alain:** I am truly grateful for this, Bertrand.

**Bertrand:** Please, the honor is all mine. There is no finer man I could hope to stand beside.

#### Final Battle

**Bertrand:** What is wrong, Alain?

**Galerius:** The ring is mine to command. Now, bow to your emperor!

**Bertrand:** This is crueler than the darkest nightmare.

**Bertrand:** You are a coward, Galerius, and now you will meet a coward's end!

**Bertrand:** That is right. We never surrender. Come back to me, Alain!

**Bertrand:** It is good to see you again.

**Alain:** Galerius, you saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire. But as long as I live and breathe, you will never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

**Alain:** Piteous ghost of an age long past, I shall grant your soul the freedom it desires.

**Bertrand:** He still will not yield?

**Bertrand:** I would never allow it.

**Alain:** Mother!

**Bertrand:** There is nothing to fear, Alain. She is still alive.

**Alain:** Josef, see my mother somewhere safe. We end this long-drawn war, here and now.

**Bertrand:** Yes. We will make this madman regret every sin he has ever committed.

**Bertrand:** There is only one monster here: you, a cruel man who set the world ablaze with the flame of war.

**Alain:** Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call. Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Ending

**Bertrand:** Then I met you, joined your army, and eventually brought peace to a world which so desperately needed it. Thank you, Your Majesty, both for myself and for my son.

**Bertrand:** I can assure you of that, no matter what future may come to pass.

**Govil:** He just stood there, crying the whole time while everyone else was celebrating.

**Govil:** And to me, dammit, you did good, king. Oh, and make sure you stop by once it is back in business. I will give you the royal discount, promise.

### Bruno

#### Bruno and Alain - Travis Worrying

Bruno: Damn Travis... Who does he think he is anyway?

Alain: Has something happened between the two of you, Bruno?

Bruno: He keeps bringin' me things. 'Course, I'm happy to take 'em, but I dunno. He never used to do nothin' like this before.

Bruno: And really, you'd think he'd be fightin' me for the good stuff, not just givin' it away.

Alain: Either that, or he's merely happy to be sharing your company again, Bruno.

Bruno: That's enough standin' around talkin' about it. I'm gonna go bring all this back to him.

Alain: You aren't going to keep his gift?

Bruno: Wish he'd just stop tryin' to worry about me and go back to bein' the same old Travis.

Alain: Perhaps you could tell him that, then. I'm certain he'd be happy to hear you say it.

Bruno: Why's it always gotta be him gettin' his way?

#### Bruno and Alain - The Tricorns

Alain: Might you tell me more about your time with the Tricorns, Bruno?

Bruno: Be glad to. Ya prolly don't know this, but it was actually me who got the band up and runnin'.

Alain: Oh? Then how did Berengaria end up captain instead of you?

Bruno: We ended up gettin' beat real bad. Took everythin' I had to help my friends get away.

Bruno: And it wasn't long 'til the bandits caught up to me. Beat the livin' hell outta me to make sure I'd never mess with 'em again.

Alain: You mean to say you served as a decoy.

Bruno: That's what a captain does, yep. I wasn't gonna go lettin' my men get cornered.

Bruno: The door flung open, and before I knew it, some noblewoman was steppin' outta the thing.

Bruno: One swing of her axe, and the bastards were done for. I'm talkin' about Berengaria, if ya couldn't guess.

Bruno: And whaddya think she said when she pulled me up off the ground?

Alain: This is sounding more like a storybook with every word. I assume she wanted to know if you were okay?

Bruno: She gave me a big ol' smile and asked if I was willin' to let her join my band.

Alain: It seems she was still just as imposing then as she is now.

Bruno: And just like that, the Tricorns were off and runnin'.

Alain: Interesting. I never knew that was how you met them.

Bruno: Kinda seemed like fate, y'know? Same as it did when I met you.

Alain: Me?

Bruno: Yep. When I was comin' to after ya broke that spell, it felt like I was gettin' saved by the boss all over again.

Bruno: I owe ya big time for that.

Bruno: And I doubt this'll make up for it, but I'm gonna keep givin' everythin' I've got for the Liberation.

Alain: Not only for your strength in battle, but for your resolute and unwavering friendship.

Bruno: Hah! Well, there's plenty more where that came from.

#### Bruno and Alain - Ring of the Maiden

Bruno: You, uh, want me to grab someone for ya? I know it's not easy askin' yourself, so.

Alain: I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

Bruno: You a few horses short of a stable, boss? What part of me screams "maiden" to you?

Alain: None of it, actually.

Alain: The only requisite is that I trust its recipient above all others, which is why I'd like you to have it, Bruno.

Bruno: All this sappy stuff makes me wanna puke.

Alain: I'll hear whatever you have to tell me. And apologies for the nausea.

Bruno: Already said it once before. You saved my life, Alain.

Bruno: And I always pay off my debts, especially when they're the only reason I'm still breathin'.

Bruno: So it doesn't matter what's comin' for us. I'll be right here, ready to flatten any poor sap that tries to hurt ya.

Bruno: That's how much ya mean to me.

Bruno: Oh, and I'll be takin' that ring now. Gotta make it official and all.

Alain: Thank you for this, Bruno. I knew you were the right person to ask.

Alain: And with that, our covenant is sworn.

Bruno: And it feels damn good, too. I've got the strength of a thousand men.

#### Bruno and Alain - Final Battle

Galerius: End this, now.

Galerius: Hmph.

Galerius: Gah.

Alain: Mother!

Galerius: How does it feel, hm? Your dear mother, slain by your own hand?

Alain: What is happening to me?

Bruno: Alain!

Galerius: What a poor fool he was, doomed to the same fate as the pitiful queen before him.

Galerius: His strength surpasses even Ilenia's. The might of the unicorn runs deep in his veins.

Galerius: strike at this new body of mine, if you dare. You'd simply be volunteering your own as my next vessel.

Galerius: The ring is mine to command, and a futile demise is all that awaits you now.

Galerius: None can ever hope to halt my designs. Bow to your emperor.

Bruno: Nah. It can't be. It's not over yet.

Galerius: The ring... why does it hold such vast energy?

Bruno: The hell's happenin'? No time for messin' around. It's him. It's gotta be.

Galerius: It will take more than this to defeat me.

Bruno: Alain!

Alain: Galerius. You saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire.

Alain: But as long as I live and breathe, you'll never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

Galerius: How do you know of that?

Galerius: You will not!

Galerius: Their emperor shall never know defeat.

Baltro: Your Majesty.

Galerius: How goes the rite?

Galerius: Then these insects shall be more than enough. Grant me your strength, and we'll stamp them out together.

Bruno: Heh. Try it if ya want. We're happy to smack ya around.

Galerius: What do you think you're doing?

Baltro: If it wasn't clear, Your Majesty, the sigil seeks none other.

Galerius: Traitorous fool. Finally gone senile, hm?

Alain: Mother!

Ilenia: Ngh.

Bruno: She's still breathin', Alain?

Alain: Speak to me, please.

Alain: Josef, see my mother somewhere safe.

Josef: And you, Your Highness?

Alain: We end this long-drawn war here and now.

Bruno: Finally. Let's hit this guy with everything we got.

Josef: Come home, both of you.

Baltro: What evil should I reanimate next? A monster capable of crushing you beneath its heel, perhaps.

Bruno: Keep dreamin'. You're not leavin', pal.

Alain: Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call.

Alain: Your emperor is no more, and in his place stands a tyrannical fiend who craves nothing but absolute control.

Alain: Tell me, is this what you truly desire? To sacrifice your very essence in service of this daemon?

Alain: Souls of the departed, if you have any humanity left within you, lend me your aid.

Alain: These souls are not a power one can wield, Baltro. They are human lives, human will in its purest form.

Alain: Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Bruno and Alain - Ending

Bruno: So as long as I'm still breathin', this axe'll be yours.

Bruno: Just lemme know if ya ever need me to swing it at someone.

Bruno: Hell of a place ya got here, Alain. Though it was hell gettin' it cleaned up, too.

Travis: But I'm glad we got it looking good as new in time for the big day.

Bruno: After all he's done for us, Alain deserves a bit o' royal comfort.

#### Bruno and Alain - Travis Worrying

Bruno: Travis keeps bringing me things. Food, mostly. Sometimes supplies.

Alain: Perhaps he is happy to share your company again.

Bruno: Hmph. We used to fight over the good stuff. Now he just hands it over like I am made of glass.

Alain: He is worried about you.

Bruno: I know that. I just want him to stop worrying and go back to being Travis.

Alain: Then tell him so.

Bruno: Guess I will have to.

#### Bruno and Alain - The Tricorns

Alain: You were the one who first gathered the Tricorns, were you not?

Bruno: Aye. I got the band running, but Berengaria became captain after.

Alain: How did that happen?

Bruno: I was acting as a decoy when bandits caught me and beat me senseless. Ren came charging in with an axe and saved my hide. Then she asked to join.

Alain: That must have been quite a sight.

Bruno: Felt like fate. Same feeling I had when you broke that spell on me. I owe you, Prince. I will give everything I have to the Liberation.

Alain: Your strength is formidable, Bruno, but your friendship is the greater gift.

Bruno: Careful. Keep talking like that and I might blush.

### Bryce

#### Bryce Recruited

Rock Rat Grunt: It's Alain, and he's got his whole damn army with him. They could be breaking down our door any second.

Bryce: Didn't think unicorns came this far north.

Kurt: You wanna make a run for it, boss?

Bryce: And hand them the city without even a fight?

Bryce: Nah. This place is ours, and we're gonna prove it.

Bryce: Then it's time we finally make our stand.

Bryce: More than that. Let's show them how strong a cornered rat can bite.

Nina: I'm certain you remember, Your Highness, but I used to stand with the Rock Rats myself. Might I have a word with their captain before the battle?

Bryce: Been a while, Nina. Didn't realize you were rubbing shoulders with the crown now.

Nina: Now please, Captain. Run away or surrender, but don't try to fight us. You will not win.

Bryce: And dammit, that's what we're gonna do.

Nina: But Captain...

Bryce: Oh, and don't hold back on account of us, okay? It's time your friends learn how strong we are.

Bryce: Easy, kid. Treat me like some sort of thief and it'll be the last thing you do.

Alain: The pride in your eyes tells me much the same.

Nina: Captain.

Bryce: Heh. Don't think we've had a spar before. Hope you don't disappoint.

Bryce: Looks like we're done for.

Bryce: No more running, huh?

Nina: Your Highness! I beg you, show mercy to this man.

Alain: The Rock Rats are thieves, there's no denying that. Yet...

Bryce: Not interested.

Bryce: You talk a good talk, I'll give you that. But you're still royal filth, and you'll steal from us just like all the rest.

Bryce: So, no thanks.

Nina: Captain, please. Alain is different.

Nina: When he first fled Palevia, he had six men to his name.

Nina: Yet now he stands with an army at his back, an impenetrable force.

Nina: Much like the Rock Rats, His Highness has faced the same struggle.

Bryce: People change, Nina.

Bryce: And there's no crueler man than the bottom-dweller turned baron.

Bryce: They get desperate to cling to their newfound power. Forget how to trust. Turn on those they once called friends.

Alain: Then why not watch over me yourself?

Alain: If I ever prove unworthy of the crown, you're free to run me through with that spear.

Bryce: Huh?

Alain: I only ask that you fight beside us all the while.

Alain: It will take all manner of strength and experience to slay Galerius and restore peace to this chaotic land.

Bryce: But it'll only be me joining you.

Bryce: After everything I've put them through, my men deserve to finally settle down. Get some rest, start a family.

Alain: Not to mention that this city will need protection. Very well. I'll grant that request.

Bryce: Ugh. Father almighty...

#### Bryce and Alain - Trust

Bryce: Well, speak of the devil. I've got a question I want to ask you.

Bryce: But the second people find out I'm keeping an eye on you, they come running over to me.

Bryce: The whole damn army won't shut up about it.

Bryce: They trust you, kid. More than most people trust their own reflections.

Alain: Hm. 'Tis a nice thing to hear, despite the inconvenience it seems to be causing you.

Bryce: The way they talk, I figured it was just a matter of time till you got all smug over it.

Bryce: But how do you stay so damn grounded when everyone else keeps trying to lift you up?

Alain: Because there's only one reason I'm even here: to restore my home to its rightful rulers.

Alain: Any trust I've gained, any soldier I recruit, is ultimately for that purpose, and that alone.

Bryce: Heh. And here you are, winning that home for the whole damn continent.

Bryce: But now, I'm actually looking forward to the day you finally are king.

Alain: Then perhaps you'd consider simply trusting me, rather than always holding that spear at my back.

Bryce: Keep it up, commander.

#### Bryce and Alain - Ring of the Maiden

Bryce: Hey there, commander. Something on your mind?

Alain: I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

Bryce: Heard enough about it to know what that means.

Bryce: Doesn't make it any less of a surprise, though.

Bryce: I said I'd run you through if you betrayed the people. You remember that, right?

Alain: I have to admit, the cost of breaking such a promise has kept me standing even taller than I otherwise would.

Alain: I could have a thousand armies, and there'd still be none other like you.

Bryce: Hm. Can't exactly refuse that.

Bryce: But remember, there's always a price to betraying a contract.

Bryce: So no turning back on championing the common man over your moneyed ones.

Bryce: Well, you know what? Anyway, I'm done talking.

Alain: I'll be looking forward to more of these lectures in the years to come.

Bryce: But maybe that's just what it takes to change the world.

#### Bryce and Alain - Final Battle

Galerius: End this, now.

Galerius: Hmph.

Galerius: Gah.

Galerius: None can ever hope to halt my designs. Bow to your emperor.

Bryce: Is this really it, kid?

Galerius: This day is won.

Galerius: You will make a fine Zenoiran vessel once it is over.

Galerius: Enough. Can't you see it's over?

Galerius: The ring...

Galerius: But why does it hold such vast energy?

Bryce: Heh. There you are.

Bryce: You sure kept me waiting, kid. Now come on out already.

Galerius: It will take more than this to defeat me.

Bryce: Alain!

Alain: Galerius. You saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire.

Alain: But as long as I live and breathe, you'll never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

Galerius: How do you know of that?

Galerius: You will not!

Galerius: Traitorous fool. Finally gone senile, hm?

Alain: Mother!

Ilenia: Ngh.

Josef: I never imagined he possessed such frightful mastery over the bodies of others.

Bryce: Evil bastard doesn't deserve sympathy. Finish it, kid.

Alain: Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call.

Alain: Your emperor is no more, and in his place stands a tyrannical fiend who craves nothing but absolute control.

Alain: Tell me, is this what you truly desire? To sacrifice your very essence in service of this daemon?
