### Celeste

#### Celeste Joins the Liberation Army

**Celeste:** What has become of him, Gammel?

**Gammel:** He got away. Bastard's slipperier than a damn eel. Really put my heart into tryin' to get him to see reason, too. But some people never listen.

**Gammel:** And that is all I got. Think you had somethin' to ask the boss here, too?

**Celeste:** Right, I almost forgot. Alain, ser. If it would not be too much bother, would you mind granting me a position in your army?

**Alain:** Not at all. I would welcome it, in fact.

**Celeste:** Oh, thank the Father!

**Gammel:** Hope ya got room for another pair of boots, then. I owe Celeste here my life. I would never be able to look my sister in the eye if anything happened to her.

**Celeste:** I will remain ever faithful to you, Alain, till death do us part.

#### Celeste and Alain - The Banquet

**Alain:** Might I ask you something, Celeste? It pertains to the banquet that was thrown for us after we liberated the nearby town.

**Celeste:** What about it?

**Alain:** I noticed you putting a rather exorbitant amount of salt and pepper on your food.

**Celeste:** I remember doing so, yes.

**Alain:** You mean to say it was intentional, then? I thought the ale had gotten the better of you. Do you always eat in such a manner?

**Celeste:** Not generally, no. But I was sitting next to you, so nervous that I could barely taste a thing. I did not want to let the feast go to waste, though, so I poured on as much seasoning as I could to try and enhance the flavor.

**Alain:** Forgive me, Celeste. I failed to realize the hardship my presence caused you.

**Celeste:** It is not your fault, my prince. I am just too shy for my own good sometimes.

**Alain:** Let us try shaking hands, to begin with.

**Celeste:** I... um. Yes, let us.

**Alain:** Celeste? Wait here whilst I summon a healer!

**Celeste:** I am fine, really. It is only the nerves getting to me a little.

**Alain:** Hm. This may prove more difficult than expected.

#### Celeste and Alain - Princess

**Alain:** Your temperature seems rather normal today, Celeste. Perhaps you have finally grown somewhat used to my presence?

**Celeste:** I believe I have, after all these mornings we have spent shaking hands.

**Alain:** Even if it meant being teased by Lex every time he walked by.

**Celeste:** Heheh.

**Alain:** Is something funny?

**Celeste:** Every time I do, it feels like I have become a princess, just for a moment.

**Alain:** One with neither castle nor crown, I should remind you. It is strange to think that without this war, we likely would never have even met each other.

**Celeste:** Ah! Sorry, I seem to have let myself get carried away for a second there.

**Alain:** I do not say that to reprimand you, Celeste. I merely find it beautiful, how even the most terrible of situations can give rise to so many fine friendships. So should it bring you joy to think of yourself as a princess, I will not tell you to do otherwise.

**Celeste:** Alain... To hear you speak such kind words to me, I am starting to wonder if I truly am.

**Alain:** 'Tis a fine thought, yes.

**Celeste:** Then come. We have a song to sing with the animals of the forest.

**Alain:** Perhaps we needn't go that far into the fantasy.

**Celeste:** Oh, this is going to be so much fun!

**Alain:** Well, I suppose I would not mind humoring her for at least a little while.

#### Ring of the Maiden

**Celeste:** I was told you were asking for me.

**Alain:** Celeste, I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

**Celeste:** It is beautiful. Almost like something out of a faerie tale.

**Alain:** It may as well be. This ring has been in the royal family for generations.

**Celeste:** And you believe me worthy of such an honor?

**Alain:** I do. Both as a warrior maiden, spurred onward by her bounteous sense of justice, and as a gentle princess able to tread this path ever at my side.

**Celeste:** I always dreamed of a day like this, but I never thought it would actually come. Not for me.

**Alain:** I take it you accept, then?

**Celeste:** Of course. I would not trade your affection for all the riches in the world. I may not be well versed in the ways of the court, but I swear I will always stand faithful to you, Alain, till death do us part.

**Alain:** Those words came as quite a shock the first time, but now they are the finest poem I have ever heard.

**Celeste:** This truly is a marvelous ring. I have to make sure my gryphon does not mistake it for a snack instead.

**Alain:** Please do that. Um, yes.

#### Final Battle

**Celeste:** Alain!

**Galerius:** The ring is mine to command. Now, bow to your emperor!

**Celeste:** You put your trust in me when you gave me this ring, and now it is time to return the favor.

**Alain:** Celeste!

**Alain:** Galerius, you saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire. But as long as I live and breathe, you will never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

**Alain:** Mother!

**Celeste:** Her breathing is steady, Alain. She is alive!

**Alain:** We end this long-drawn war now.

**Celeste:** I am not going anywhere until the final blow is struck.

**Celeste:** Come, Alain. Let us bring their pain to an end.

**Alain:** Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call. Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Ending

**Celeste:** Either way, I am still pinching myself that I am your queen.

**Celeste:** I wonder what he is doing hiding behind that rock.

### Chloe

#### Chloe and Alain - Speaking Like a Prince

Alain: Urgh.

Chloe: Why the sigh, Your Majesty?

Alain: Forgive me, Chloe. It was nothing important, I assure you.

Chloe: It certainly didn't sound like nothing.

Alain: All those years spent learning under Josef, and I still feel like I barely have anything to show for it.

Chloe: You always talked like anyone else does. I used to find it endearing, to be honest.

Alain: But now I feel like I'm constantly forcing myself to be someone I'm not.

Chloe: Maybe you just need a bit of practice, then.

Alain: That would be great, assuming you're offering.

Chloe: We can start right now. Say that again, but like a prince would.

Alain: Ahem. Should you truly wish to grant me such kindness, I would be honored to accept.

Chloe: That's better!

Alain: Phew. I was worried for a second there.

Chloe: Don't be. I thought it all sounded quite elegant, actually. I know you're leading an army now, but I hope we can still talk to each other like friends, at least when it's just the two of us.

Alain: As do I. Thank you again, Chloe.

#### Chloe and Alain - Family

Alain: Isn't it a little early to be out training, Chloe?

Chloe: I'm the only one of us who was ever interested in becoming a soldier. My dad hardly knew what to do with me. That's why he sent me off to train under Ser Josef.

Alain: Why did you never mention it to me?

Chloe: I'm sorry for not bringing it up sooner.

Alain: Please. We all have things we seek to defend, and your father was no different.

Chloe: I plan to go back once the war is over, to find my sisters and do what I can to help them start anew.

Alain: It seems you care quite deeply for them.

Chloe: I do. still, I suppose I should figure out how to be a little more refined before I see them again.

Alain: I'm not sure there's any need for that. You're plenty ladylike as it is, Chloe.

Chloe: I appreciate you saying so, even if you don't really mean it.

Alain: In all truth, though, 'tis I who yet struggles to grasp the affairs of nobility.

Chloe: If you really want to be king, you need to know how to engage with that part of society.

Alain: I guess in that case, let's keep practicing, same as before.

Chloe: It seems we have a lot of ground to make up before you're ready for that crown.

#### Chloe and Alain - Dance Practice

Chloe: Yes! That's perfect, Your Majesty.

Alain: Ah... I feel as though I might stumble at any moment.

Chloe: Ow!

Alain: Forgive me, Chloe! Are you okay?

Chloe: I'm fine, thank you.

Alain: I have to wonder, is learning to dance truly a necessary part of being a noble?

Chloe: It's strange hearing you complain about it. I always thought you were good at these kinds of things.

Alain: If only. I've never been particularly proud of my dexterity. In fact, I was so clumsy with a blade at first, Josef nearly put a stop to our lessons entirely.

Chloe: But praising your skill is practically all that Ser Josef does.

Alain: Now, perhaps. I was lucky I had Lex and Scarlett there to support me after even the most minor of missteps. And you, Chloe.

Chloe: Am I truly as important to him as they are?

Alain: What was that?

Chloe: Oh, speaking of Scarlett, she recently asked me to teach her how to cook.

Alain: And did you?

Chloe: Of course. She works hard, you know, though I can't say she's especially good at it. Frankly, it was frustrating to think I'd never do the same. Anyway, it's not like me to get all upset like this. I'll see you later, Your Majesty.

Alain: Wait! If only you could see what I see, Chloe. Perhaps then you would realize just how much you do for us.

#### Chloe and Alain - Ring of the Maiden

Chloe: Is there something I can help with, Your Majesty?

Alain: I would like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

Chloe: I had a feeling that might be why you asked me here, but there must be someone else who deserves it more than I do.

Alain: I am meant to give this ring to whomever I trust most.

Chloe: Really?

Alain: You can tell me if you are not interested.

Alain: Apologies. That is not how I meant to phrase it.

Alain: What I truly wish to say is that your presence is what gives me the strength to march on day after day.

Chloe: You would be doing this whether I am here or not, and you know it.

Alain: But...

Chloe: I am sick of seeing you like this, Alain.

Chloe: I have watched you grow all these years, more and more into the ideal prince. But I know that is not who you really are.

Chloe: So cut the act, at least when you are with me.

Chloe: I will do it. I will swear the oath.

Chloe: But only if I can spend more time with the real you.

Chloe: I am serious.

Alain: That means the world to me. Truly.

Chloe: You will have to prove it, then. Let us see how good you are at dropping that princely mask of yours.

Alain: I shall endeavor to do so in all that I am.

Chloe: That is what I am talking about.

#### Chloe and Alain - Final Battle

Alain: Galerius, Emperor of Zenoira.

Galerius: If you hope to speak, you will find me no willing participant. I have no words for you.

Galerius: End this, now.

Galerius: Hmph.

Galerius: Gah.

Alain: Mother!

Galerius: How does it feel, hm? Your dear mother, slain by your own hand.

Alain: What is happening to me?

Chloe: Alain, look out!

Galerius: What a poor fool he was, doomed to the same fate as the pitiful queen before him.

Galerius: His strength surpasses even Ilenia's. The might of the unicorn runs deep in his veins.

Galerius: The ring is mine to command, and a futile demise is all that awaits you now.

Galerius: None can ever hope to halt my designs. Bow to your emperor.

Galerius: You will make a fine Zenoiran vessel once it is over.

Galerius: The ring... why does it hold such vast energy?

Chloe: He is still in there, fighting Galerius with everything he has left.

Galerius: It will take more than this to defeat me.

Chloe: Alain!

Alain: Galerius. You saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire.

Galerius: You will not!

Galerius: Their emperor shall never know defeat.

Baltro: Your Majesty.

Galerius: How goes the rite?

Galerius: Then these insects shall be more than enough. Grant me your strength, and we will stamp them out together.

Galerius: What do you think you are doing?

Baltro: If it was not clear, Your Majesty, the sigil seeks none other.

Galerius: Traitorous fool. Finally gone senile, hm?

Alain: Mother!

Ilenia: Ngh.

Chloe: She is alive. Queen Ilenia...

Alain: Speak to me, please.

Josef: I never imagined he possessed such frightful mastery over the bodies of others.

Ilenia: Alain. I cannot say how much time has passed since that day, but you have grown so much.

Ilenia: If only I could have been there to witness it.

Ilenia: It seems I owe Josef a great deal for raising you in my absence.

Alain: Josef, see my mother somewhere safe.

Josef: And you, Your Highness?

Alain: We end this long-drawn war now.

Chloe: You will have my spear as long as you need it. Let us finish this.

Josef: Come home, both of you.

Baltro: Do you not understand, boy? Your end has already been written.

Alain: I will not hear another word of Baltro's madness. Come, the final battle is upon us.

Alain: Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call.

Alain: Your emperor is no more, and in his place stands a tyrannical fiend who craves nothing but absolute control.

Alain: Tell me, is this what you truly desire? To sacrifice your very essence in service of this daemon?

Alain: Souls of the departed, if you have any humanity left within you, lend me your aid.

Alain: These souls are not a power one can wield, Baltro. They are human lives, human will in its purest form.

Alain: Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Chloe and Alain - Ending

Chloe: I am sure you are exhausted from all the festivities, Alain, but thank you for remembering our promise.

Chloe: I am glad to see you are out enjoying yourself, no matter what face you show the world while you do it. I really am.

Chloe: Maybe lean on my shoulder for a minute or two?

Chloe: Sorry. That might be my own wish rather than yours.

Chloe: Well, Ridiel? What do you think of Gran Corrine?

Ridiel: I cannot help but smile a bit, realizing we are the ones responsible for this.

Chloe: Looks like peace is getting the better of you.

### Clive

#### Clive and Alain - Royal Guard

Alain: If I may, Clive. How would you feel about joining my royal guard, after peace is restored to our land?

Alain: Such strength of will would prove invaluable in my service. I'm certain of that.

Clive: Your Highness, I...

Clive: And as you may know, I've little left to call my own in this world. No family to speak of, and no retainers to my name.

Clive: Yet that is precisely why I must return home at the conclusion of this war.

Clive: My mother and sister would surely have wanted the same, had they only lived to see the day.

Alain: All I ask is that you continue to march beside us until that day comes.

Clive: 'Tis a badge I shall wear with pride for the rest of my days.

#### Clive and Alain - Ashen Blue

Boy: When I grow up, I want to be a knight just like you.

Boy: Oh, wait until my friends hear about this!

Clive: Hello there, Your Highness.

Alain: That was kind of you to do, Clive.

Alain: Though you and Adel are both of noble line, you never let such matters hinder your relations with the common man.

Clive: As is our duty as knights of the Ashen Blue. Status and station are nigh meaningless here in our province.

Clive: To join our order, all one needs is the talent to hold a blade and the ambition to see their journey through.

Clive: But of course, so long as he truly wishes to become a knight.

Clive: Think of Berenice and her lack of horse.

Clive: Being born to commoner parents, she couldn't afford a steed of her own.

Clive: And while she claims it's due to her dislike of the beasts, she simply never had the opportunity to learn.

Clive: Yet while she stood with our order, she was every ounce our equal.

Alain: Point well made. In truth, I always believed a knight had to come from noble birth.

Clive: Cornia is a nation of great history, Your Highness.

Clive: Of great noble families who have endured for centuries, while those beneath them are resigned to subsist off their land.

Clive: Most knights, on the other hand, belong to the lower nobility, a class fully subservient to those more illustrious houses.

Clive: And while you might expect such vassalage to be a positive thing, it is often rife with abuse and exploitation.

Clive: As has been its purpose ever since King Gerard granted our order the land we stand upon.

Alain: My grandfather, the Sacred Blade of Cornia. I only knew him from portraits I've seen on the castle walls myself.

Clive: Why did he deserve to lead the nation, simply because of the lineage into which he was born?

Clive: It was that doubt which led him to frequently roam the land, enlisting to his service any able subject he came across, no matter their birth.

Clive: We swore allegiance to only one sovereign: the great Gerard, who bestowed this province upon us.

Clive: And thus, our territory has served as a deterrent to the nobility's influence, and the cornerstone of a lasting peace in the region.

Alain: It was out of pride for your homeland, and the will to see its ideals carried through to the next generation of knights.

Clive: I only hope I didn't bore you with the tale, Your Highness.

Alain: 'Tis clear to me now that I know almost nothing about my own kingdom.

Clive: Please. You mustn't speak so ill of yourself.

Clive: I would be most honored to tell you more.

#### Clive and Alain - Loss and the Future

Clive: My father, my family, and my retainers all stood firm against the Zenoiran onset, and all of them perished in the process.

Clive: Perhaps my sister and mother might yet live.

Clive: For a knight, such actions are the mark of a coward, not a leader.

Alain: And were we not here to fight it, Cornia would surely be lost to Galerius for the rest of time.

Alain: We must never forget that. No matter what.

Clive: Thank you for saying so, Your Highness.

Clive: Even should we defeat Galerius, I imagine it will be difficult to return to the days of innocence which came before.

Alain: All this time, I've thought only of restoring Cornia to my family's rule.

Alain: Yet I've no knowledge of what the kingdom I fight for even used to look like.

Alain: After all this time, I fear I've no attachment to the home I lost.

Alain: 'Tis thoughts such as these that instill in me the same doubts which likely once plagued my grandfather.

Clive: To summon the winds of change 'cross Cornia's fields, just as King Gerard did before you.

Clive: And I, for one, am eager to see what manner of kingdom you create in the decades to come.

Alain: And I shall do whatever I must to honor their conviction.

#### Clive and Alain - Ring of the Maiden

Alain: I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

Clive: I understand.

Clive: Do you recall your request from before, Your Highness?

Alain: Of course. I also recall you rejecting the offer.

Alain: Yet I would ask this of you now, even still.

Alain: Even should you reject my overtures once more.

Clive: In truth, Your Highness...

Clive: I've come to regret the denial with which I met you that day.

Clive: I realize now, for your aim of bringing a good and prosperous Cornia will be much the same to my own home.

Clive: Would that I could have arrived at this revelation sooner.

Clive: Though we may leave the past in the past. In the present moment, I desire nothing more than to serve at your side.

Alain: Your words are most heartening, Clive. And I'm glad you've changed your mind.

Clive: I can imagine no greater honor than this, Your Highness.

Alain: Yet you're the only one I could ever have hoped to ask.

Clive: Please. Such generous words upon this humble knight.

Clive: Now come. Together, we shall see Zenoira's ambitions defeated.

#### Clive and Alain - Final Battle

Galerius: End this, now.

Galerius: Hmph.

Galerius: Gah.

Alain: Mother!

Galerius: How does it feel, hm? Your dear mother, slain by your own hand?

Alain: What is happening to me?

Clive: Your Highness?

Galerius: What a poor fool he was, doomed to the same fate as the pitiful queen before him.

Galerius: His strength surpasses even Ilenia's. The might of the unicorn runs deep in his veins.

Galerius: You'd simply be volunteering your own as my next vessel.

Galerius: The ring is mine to command, and a futile demise is all that awaits you now.

Galerius: None can ever hope to halt my designs. Bow to your emperor.

Galerius: This day is won.

Galerius: You will make a fine Zenoiran vessel once it is over.

Galerius: Enough. Can't you see it's over?

Galerius: The ring...

Galerius: But why does it hold such vast energy?

Clive: End this foul nightmare and return to me.

Galerius: It will take more than this to defeat me.

Clive: Alain!

Alain: Galerius. You saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire.

Alain: But as long as I live and breathe, you'll never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

Galerius: How do you know of that?

Galerius: You will not!

Galerius: Their emperor shall never know defeat.

Baltro: Your Majesty.

Galerius: How goes the rite?

Galerius: Then these insects shall be more than enough. Grant me your strength, and we'll stamp them out together.

Baltro: If it wasn't clear, Your Majesty, the sigil seeks none other.

Galerius: Traitorous fool. Finally gone senile, hm?

Alain: Mother!

Ilenia: Ngh.

Clive: She still lives, Your Highness.

Josef: I never imagined he possessed such frightful mastery over the bodies of others.

Ilenia: Alain. I can't say how much time has passed since that day, but you've grown so much.

Ilenia: If only I could have been there to witness it.

Ilenia: It seems I owe Josef a great deal for raising you in my absence.

Alain: Josef, see my mother somewhere safe.

Josef: And you, Your Highness?

Alain: We end this long-drawn war now.

Clive: That vile sigil will fall by our hand.

Josef: Come home, both of you.

Baltro: What evil should I reanimate next? A monster capable of crushing you beneath its heel, perhaps.

Clive: You've desecrated their memory, wicked sorcerer.

Alain: Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call.

Alain: Your emperor is no more, and in his place stands a tyrannical fiend who craves nothing but absolute control.

Alain: Tell me, is this what you truly desire? To sacrifice your very essence in service of this daemon?

Alain: Souls of the departed, if you have any humanity left within you, lend me your aid.

Alain: These souls are not a power one can wield, Baltro. They are human lives, human will in its purest form.

Alain: Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Clive and Alain - Ending

Clive: Allow me to offer my heartfelt congratulations, Your Majesty.

Clive: As well as my humblest gratitude as an appointed member of your royal guard.

Clive: Long have I waited in darkness. Ten agonizing years, hoping the light of the heavens would one day shine on our lands once more.

Clive: Never again shall the tragedies of war torment our innocents and raze our homes.

Clive: I pledge my life in service of that aim, Your Majesty.

Monica: My sincerest congratulations on your ascendance, Your Majesty.

Berenice: While you're chained to a desk in your stuffy old castle, I'll be training, same as always.

Berenice: Just don't get too weighed down by that crown, Alain.

Adel: Today, raise your glasses to King Alain. We drink in his name.

Adel: Ahem. Congratulations again on your rise to the throne.

Adel: I believe that with every ounce of my soul.

Adel: Well, Clive? You gonna drink with me or what?

Clive: Easy.

Clive: What a shame it would be to forget the only coronation His Majesty will ever have.

Adel: Fine, fine. I guess I've had enough fun for one day.

### Colm

#### Colm and Alain - Care for Melisandre

Colm: Allow me to thank you once more for granting us refuge in your army, my prince.

Alain: It is nothing that demands gratitude, Colm. Your aid is a most welcome boon in these difficult times.

Colm: And what of Lady Melisandre? I pray she has not given you too much trouble.

Alain: Not particularly, no.

Colm: That is a relief to hear.

Colm: Is it concern for the prince which stays her hand, or perhaps an uncharacteristic bout of shyness?

Alain: Colm?

Colm: Whatever the case, it is best not to interfere in the affairs of her heart.

Colm: Pardon me for saying, ser, but I trust you will treat my lady with all the love and kindness she deserves.

Alain: You do mean in my role as her commander, yes?

Alain: You are a fine attendant indeed, Colm. It is plain to see just how deeply you care for her.

Alain: Such loyalty must provide great comfort in her times of need, much as Josef does for me.

Colm: And it demands every ounce of effort I have to ensure my counsel does not come across as intrusive or overbearing.

Alain: Thank you, Colm. I shall speak with Josef tonight and allay whatever concerns he may be carrying.

Colm: A wonderful idea, my prince. I am certain he will be pleased to know how you feel.

Colm: Perhaps it is that shared kindness which makes her and the prince such an ideal match for one another.

#### Colm and Alain - Ring of the Maiden

Colm: You know, I may be the lady's attendant, but you needn't call upon me if you wish to call upon her.

Alain: I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

Colm: Pardon, ser? You don't want Melisandre, but me?

Alain: I fear I've given the wrong impression in calling you here.

Colm: Not at all, ser. I'm merely seeking to comprehend.

Alain: I'm to give the ring to the person I trust most in this world.

Alain: And together, we will strike Zenoira down and restore a great and lasting peace to all of Fevrith.

Colm: I understand now.

Colm: I would gladly accept.

Colm: Everything I do, I do for the well-being of our people, and for that of Lady Melisandre, of course.

Colm: If you're certain the talents of a lowly servant can be of use, I will readily offer them to your cause.

Alain: With one of your skill at my side, we are all but guaranteed to emerge victorious.

Colm: High praise indeed. But I assure you, the reality of our righteous war will soar even higher.

#### Colm and Alain - Final Battle

Galerius: It will take more than this to defeat me.

Galerius: You will not!

Galerius: Their emperor shall never know defeat.

Baltro: Your Majesty.

Galerius: Then these insects shall be more than enough. Grant me your strength, and we'll stamp them out together.

Galerius: Traitorous fool. Finally gone senile, hm?

Ilenia: Ngh.

Alain: We end this long-drawn war now.

Colm: Though I admit, bearing witness to it did raise doubts as to whether I stand worthy of your ring.

Colm: Doubts which were soon quelled by a firm scolding from Lady Melisandre.

Colm: Excessive as the honor may be, I've nothing but joy to have sworn this covenant with you.

Colm: I merely ask for your patience in the days ahead, to forgive my failings should I ever stumble.

Melisandre: My fondness for you is the same as ever, and I expect it always will be.

### Dinah

#### Dinah and Alain - Protect Yunifi

**Alain:** I would be glad to do so, Dinah, but where exactly is this coming from?

**Dinah:** Any fight she sees, she will go jumping in to break it up. When a friend gets hurt, she is always the first one rushing to help. And when you have got something to celebrate, she will be right there celebrating with you till the sun goes down. If anyone deserves the best that life has to offer, it is her.

**Alain:** If such a situation ever arose, I would do what it took to protect you both.

#### Dinah and Alain - A Wound

**Alain:** Thank you both for keeping patrol this evening. I am certain it was...

**Yunifi:** Agh!

**Dinah:** Dammit! I could not pick up his scent in all this snow. You are bleeding pretty badly there. Everything okay?

**Alain:** I have also spoken to Josef about fortifying our perimeter, at least for the time being.

**Dinah:** That is not what I am asking about. I wanna know how you are doing, Alain.

**Alain:** I shall gladly bear any wound to keep the both of you safe, just as I said I would.

**Dinah:** Maybe you should reconsider. I would have been just fine without you getting yourself hurt for me.

**Alain:** I made you a promise, and I fully intend to keep it, no matter the cost.

**Alain:** Ngh...

**Dinah:** Now go back to your tent and get some sleep, Alain. That is an order.

**Alain:** It is late, Dinah. You should really head in and get some rest.

**Dinah:** It is only natural a commander cares about what his soldiers are getting up to.

**Alain:** Of course, Dinah. You are far more to me than just that.

**Dinah:** You are gonna wake up the whole camp if you keep shouting like that.

**Alain:** Indeed. I should not have spoken to you in such a manner.

**Dinah:** Maybe I should not have been so harsh on you, but you really do care too much. It is not worth dying over. There are a lot of people out there who could not stand to see you get hurt. Including me.

**Alain:** I cannot promise the same if someone I care about is in danger. Someone like you.

**Dinah:** I will be there soon enough, so do not go worrying about me while I am gone.

**Alain:** As you wish. Good night, Dinah.

#### Ring of the Maiden

**Dinah:** Need something?

**Alain:** Dinah, I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

**Dinah:** I know how deeply you care for those who fight for you, Alain. Better than most, I would say. But I thought that sentiment applied to all of us equally.

**Alain:** I realized something when I saw you in danger. Among all others, you are the one I hold most dear.

**Dinah:** What am I supposed to say to that? Knowing you, you mean every word of it. Not to mention the way you look at me. It is just not fair.

**Dinah:** I showed up planning to turn you down, you know.

**Alain:** I am sorry.

**Dinah:** See, this is exactly what I am talking about. What business do you have apologizing?

**Dinah:** Fine. I will stand by you to the very end.

**Alain:** Thank you, Dinah, for saying yes despite yourself.

**Dinah:** One more thing. Remember what I said before? How I do not wanna see you hurt? It is even more true now. So no dying on me. I want you to promise, okay?

**Alain:** I promise. I will never let you experience that pain again.

#### Final Battle

**Dinah:** Alain!

**Galerius:** The ring is mine to command. Now, bow to your emperor!

**Alain:** Dinah!

**Alain:** Galerius, you saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire. But as long as I live and breathe, you will never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

**Alain:** Mother!

**Dinah:** Her breathing is steady, Alain. She is alive.

**Alain:** We end this long-drawn war now.

**Dinah:** That sigil does not stand a chance against us.

**Alain:** Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call. Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Ending

**Dinah:** I wish they would just give it a rest already. Oh, Alain. Something wrong?

**Dinah:** I thought maybe you would be so busy rubbing elbows in there that you would not make it over to me.

**Dinah:** Hmph. Go do what you have to do, but do not worry. I will still be here when you are done.

**Dinah:** They just never agree on anything, huh?

**Dinah:** Keep this between us, but I have never really enjoyed fighting in the first place. I only did it because I had to.

### Eltolinde

#### Eltolinde and Alain - First Impressions

**Eltolinde:** I have to know, Alain. What was your first impression upon arriving in Elheim?

**Alain:** It would have to be the greenery, of course. At times of solitude, it has even felt as though the trees themselves were likely to pick me up and carry me off to unknown shores.

**Eltolinde:** I cannot deny the possibility. I am certain they were ever vigilant in studying your actions, and presumably still are.

**Alain:** Let us presume, then, that the forest were restored to its natural state. Would a mere word from your lips be enough to make me vanish for the rest of time?

**Eltolinde:** Yet I cannot imagine that ever being the case. Not for the man who was so brave in delivering me from Zenoira's grasp. My faith in you shall not waver, Alain, no matter what events may lie ahead.

#### Eltolinde and Alain - Distance

**Alain:** 'Tis a fine morning, Eltolinde.

**Eltolinde:** Indeed it is, my prince. I pray the day ahead shall prove a fruitful one.

**Alain:** I was thinking of the moment you and the others came upon a rare poisonous herb here in Cornia.

**Eltolinde:** What a delightful moment it was. Yet such outbursts are wholly inappropriate for one of my standing. There are rules the Turenos must uphold as leaders of Elheim, a ban on consorting with foreign dignitaries chief among them, no matter where my own personal feelings may lie on the subject.

**Alain:** While at others, you simply let yourself exist as a mere elf among friends and nothing more. Anyone should be free to do the same, no matter what nation they come from. Erm, Eltolinde?

**Eltolinde:** I suppose the issue here is my wishing to be your friend. But rather, the emotions I have begun to bear for you.

**Alain:** Eltolinde...

**Eltolinde:** Forgive me. I did not mean to grab your hands like this.

**Eltolinde:** Let this be proof of the relationship I wish to foster with you.

**Alain:** I would not mind, were that the case.

#### Eltolinde and Alain - An Embrace

**Alain:** Eltolinde?

**Eltolinde:** What is it, Alain?

**Alain:** Forgive me the outburst, but I cannot say I much expected you to embrace me like this.

**Eltolinde:** According to them, the best way to show deep affection for someone is by holding them close and not letting go.

**Alain:** That is not entirely incorrect, and yet...

**Eltolinde:** It is a difficult matter indeed to accurately study customs not found within Elheim's borders.

**Alain:** Ah. That explains why you seemed so uncomfortable in doing so.

**Eltolinde:** You are blushing, Alain. Perhaps I should have known this would be a struggle.

**Alain:** How do you mean?

**Eltolinde:** I am meant to be the leader of my nation, but these feelings only make it more difficult to maintain the distance such a role requires. Should our association prove a hindrance to the war effort...

**Alain:** Eltolinde.

**Eltolinde:** Alain?

**Alain:** The more our roles demand we stay at arm's length, the more I want to pull you close to me.

**Eltolinde:** I admit, I am happy to know I am not the only one struggling with this. 'Tis simply the reality of our differing lifespans.

**Alain:** Then that is all the more reason to spend as much time together now as we possibly can.

**Eltolinde:** You may just be right, Alain.

#### Ring of the Maiden

**Eltolinde:** I hear you have need of me, Prince.

**Alain:** Eltolinde, I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

**Eltolinde:** Allow me to ask you something before I offer my response. The limits of our mortality differ greatly. I will live on long after your flesh has returned to the earth. My grief is all but inevitable if we continue down this path. What do you make of that?

**Alain:** I am well aware that agreeing to this will subject you to years of solitude and sorrow. But I share in that sentiment myself. The mere thought of leaving this world without you at my side fills me with the coldest melancholy, and fear.

**Alain:** Even still, I wish to spend what little time I have with none but you. I ask that you forgive me this request all the same.

**Eltolinde:** Thank you, Alain. I can tell you truly mean what you said. And you are right. Grief visits more than just the one left behind.

**Eltolinde:** I accept your proposal, your melancholy, your fear, and your selfishness. We shall remain as one until Death himself tears us apart.

**Alain:** There could be no greater honor. So long as we have time to share in this life, I promise to share it with you. I love you, Eltolinde.

**Eltolinde:** And I the same.

#### Final Battle

**Eltolinde:** Alain!

**Galerius:** The ring is mine to command. Now, bow to your emperor!

**Eltolinde:** Alain, this ring is the only thing keeping you tied to our world.

**Alain:** I will return.

**Eltolinde:** Thank the stars you're...

**Alain:** Galerius, you saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire. But as long as I live and breathe, you will never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

**Alain:** Mother!

**Eltolinde:** She still lives, Alain.

**Alain:** We end this long-drawn war now.

**Eltolinde:** Today, we restore peace to all of Fevrith. Today, this horror shall reach its conclusion!

**Rosalinde:** This time, no harm will come to you.

**Eltolinde:** Have you no heart? No compassion for those you once called brother?

**Alain:** Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call. Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Ending

**Eltolinde:** We have spent so much time with our friends during the war, yet now our company will mostly consist of each other. I am more certain now than ever that you are the one I wish to spend my days beside.

**Eltolinde:** I love this ring, Alain, and you.

**Eltolinde:** Have you any plans for what comes next, Umerus?

**Umerus:** Once matters have settled down a bit, I was thinking it might be nice to plant a garden near my home.

**Eltolinde:** That is a lovely idea. Perhaps I could pay you a visit once it is finished, assuming you would not refuse the company.

**Umerus:** I hope that by then, it will have grown into a tranquil refuge worthy of your presence.

**Galadmir:** That has been evident since the moment that crown was placed on your head. I may have tested you once, but you have more than proven yourself worthy of my trust. Our entire kingdom will have nothing but praise for the greatest hero Fevrith has ever known.

**Galadmir:** It has been quite the novel experience, witnessing another land's coronation.

**Eltolinde:** Yes. With delegations hailing from every land of Fevrith, it feels as though the entire world has joined hands in harmony.

**Galadmir:** A harmony which will surely see more visitors grace Elheim's forests soon enough. And with any luck, everyone present at today's coronation will continue to strive toward deepening it further.

**Eltolinde:** I pray you are right.

### Fodoquia

#### Fodoquia and Alain - Peyston Under Zenoira

**Fodoquia:** Hold. Your banners do not fly Zenoiran colors. But it appears there has been a misunderstanding. Albion has ceded its lands to our new emperor, Galerius. You stand on Zenoiran territory now, and not a soul among us desires liberation.

**Fodoquia:** Ser Alain, if you truly seek no quarrel with us, then leave this place. I will claim I saw nothing. But know this: when next your gauntlets rap at our gates, you will find neither mercy nor hesitation. Now begone.

**Alain:** A convincing show of strength, Ser Fodoquia.

**Fodoquia:** When the Empire came forth and began violating our land, I fought back with every ounce of my being. I was prepared to oppose their rule until our final soldier fell.

**Fodoquia:** As were my people. They stood by me and risked their very lives in defending this sacred ground. But six months passed, then a year. The pain of citizenry besieged grew fiercer and fiercer until at last there came the breaking point.

**Fodoquia:** That day, my own subjects kidnapped my son and demanded we lay down our arms. By Zenoiran orders, they massacred my child and offered his corpse as a sacrifice to our new masters.

**Fodoquia:** They chose to leave me in power, to exploit my rage and my despair for their own nefarious purposes. So I bent to the will of my people, and the path they chose to walk was that of subjugation.

#### Ring of the Maiden

**Fodoquia:** Prince Alain, I was informed you had words for me.

**Alain:** Fodoquia, I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

**Fodoquia:** Hm. I assume such an offer is symbolic of the trust you have placed upon my shoulders. While I cannot truly deny the joy I feel in this moment...

**Alain:** I know well the sacrifices you are willing to make for the well-being of others, and that you possess an unbreaking spirit, dauntless in the face of even the deepest despair. I am certain a covenant with you would bring these rings immeasurable power.

**Fodoquia:** You know, Prince, our battle at Peyston forever altered my life. Not only were you able to liberate the city, but my heart as well.

**Fodoquia:** To refuse a gesture this righteous would be tantamount to divine treason. I accept.

**Alain:** You have done me a great honor, Fodoquia. Thank you, truly.

**Fodoquia:** All that I am is ever in your service.

#### Final Battle

**Fodoquia:** My prince!

**Galerius:** The ring is mine to command. Now, bow to your emperor!

**Alain:** Fodoquia!

**Alain:** Galerius, you saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire. But as long as I live and breathe, you will never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

**Fodoquia:** How does he yet possess such strength?

**Alain:** Mother!

**Fodoquia:** Your mother still lives, my prince.

**Alain:** We end this long-drawn war now.

**Fodoquia:** Today, the countless years of despair shall be cast into the depths of oblivion.

**Fodoquia:** Words shall not return this tyrant to the heavens.

**Alain:** Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call. Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Ending

**Fodoquia:** Having vanquished evil and restored the joy of peace to your citizens, I feel much the same again. Whatever challenge may lie before me, I shall trust myself to overcome it, just as you trusted me not long ago.

**Fodoquia:** Meandering through your capital has raised my spirits rather dramatically. Yet I shall never surrender hope, neither for myself nor for them.

### Fran

#### Fran and Alain - The Gryphon Trial

Alain: Is everyone in your family able to ride gryphons, Fran?

Fran: Actually, just me.

Fran: Every couple of years, the house holds a trial to determine who that is.

Alain: 'Tis an intriguing method indeed, a test of skill to prove yourselves ready.

Fran: But it turned out I was the only suitable candidate.

Alain: Because the others all failed to command their gryphons?

Fran: You could barely call it a proper trial at all.

Alain: No, I suppose not.

Fran: But I knew the shame it would bring our family if I failed to gain admission into the Knights of the Rose.

Fran: So I trained tirelessly, day after day, until I was able to prove my merit and join the order in true.

Alain: 'Tis surely that dedication which sees you thriving now for the Liberation as well.

Fran: But I appreciate you saying so, even if it's not entirely true.

#### Fran and Alain - A Gryphon Ride

Alain: Might I ask you a favor, Fran?

Fran: Anything, Your Highness. What can I help you with?

Alain: If it is all right with you, I wish to ride your gryphon.

Fran: You? That would be far too dangerous.

Alain: I cannot say I expected such a deafening refusal.

Fran: I worry my gryphon would throw you off if you tried.

Alain: It appears I was gravely mistaken.

Fran: Hold on a minute. Were you suggesting we go together?

Alain: I could hardly presume myself capable of taming a beast of war alone.

Fran: In that case, I think it should be okay.

Alain: Do you truly mean that?

Fran: I would not want you falling to your death on account of me.

Alain: Then I will do just as you say. Thank you, Fran.

Fran: What did you think, Your Highness?

Alain: It was unlike anything I could ever have imagined, in the best way possible.

Alain: I did not expect the wind rushing across my face to feel so different from how it does on the ground.

Fran: I am glad you enjoyed it.

Alain: Tell your gryphon I say thank you as well, for granting an unknown passenger such a wonderful voyage.

#### Fran and Alain - Ring of the Maiden

Alain: Hm? And where is your rider, gryphon?

Fran: I'm sorry, Your Highness.

Fran: Well... I guess I'm having trouble believing any of this is real. It is real, isn't it?

Alain: I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

Fran: You... you would?

Alain: Erm, Fran?

Fran: Forgive me, my prince. I'm just struggling to take this all in.

Alain: The blame lies with me for surprising you so.

Alain: The truth is, I've been enchanted ever since we took to the sky together.

Alain: Not by the thrill of riding atop a gryphon, but by how I felt doing so with you.

Alain: Should you accept this ring, we shall fly together for the rest of our lives and attempt to surmount our fates in the process.

Alain: So tell me, Fran. Would you be willing to make another dream of mine a reality?

Fran: To be honest, when I first heard of rings and oaths, I secretly hoped you would be the one who ended up picking me.

Fran: All that to say, I would be honored.

Alain: I'm glad to hear it.

Fran: Looks like both our dreams came true today.

Alain: Indeed. Perhaps I could have saved us some worry if I had only mentioned it sooner.

#### Fran and Alain - Final Battle

Galerius: End this, now.

Galerius: Hmph.

Galerius: Gah.

Alain: Mother!

Galerius: How does it feel, hm? Your dear mother, slain by your own hand?

Alain: What is happening to me?

Fran: Your Highness!

Galerius: What a poor fool he was, doomed to the same fate as the pitiful queen before him.

Galerius: His strength surpasses even Ilenia's. The might of the unicorn runs deep in his veins.

Galerius: strike at this new body of mine, if you dare.

Galerius: You'd simply be volunteering your own as my next vessel.

Galerius: The ring is mine to command, and a futile demise is all that awaits you now.

Galerius: None can ever hope to halt my designs. Bow to your emperor.

Galerius: This day is won.

Galerius: You will make a fine Zenoiran vessel once it is over.

Galerius: Enough. Can't you see it's over?

Galerius: The ring...

Galerius: But why does it hold such vast energy?

Fran: Your people need you now more than ever. I need you.

Galerius: It will take more than this to defeat me.

Fran: Alain!

Alain: Galerius. You saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire.

Alain: But as long as I live and breathe, you'll never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

Galerius: How do you know of that?

Galerius: You will not!

Galerius: Their emperor shall never know defeat.

Baltro: Your Majesty.

Galerius: How goes the rite?

Galerius: Then these insects shall be more than enough. Grant me your strength, and we'll stamp them out together.

Galerius: What do you think you're doing?

Baltro: If it wasn't clear, Your Majesty, the sigil seeks none other.

Galerius: Traitorous fool. Finally gone senile, hm?

Alain: Mother!

Ilenia: Ngh.

Fran: Oh, thank the Father. She's still breathing.

Alain: Speak to me, please.

Josef: I never imagined he possessed such frightful mastery over the bodies of others.

Ilenia: Alain. I can't say how much time has passed since that day, but you've grown so much.

Ilenia: If only I could have been there to witness it.

Ilenia: It seems I owe Josef a great deal for raising you in my absence.

Alain: Josef, see my mother somewhere safe.

Josef: And you, Your Highness?

Alain: We end this long-drawn war now.

Fran: The sigil will fall by our hands.

Josef: Come home, both of you.

Baltro: What evil should I reanimate next? A monster capable of crushing you beneath its heel, perhaps.

Fran: Enough. Behind the guise of a man, you are nothing but evil.

Alain: Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call.

Alain: Your emperor is no more, and in his place stands a tyrannical fiend who craves nothing but absolute control.

Alain: Tell me, is this what you truly desire? To sacrifice your very essence in service of this daemon?

Alain: Souls of the departed, if you have any humanity left within you, lend me your aid.

Alain: These souls are not a power one can wield, Baltro. They are human lives, human will in its purest form.

Alain: Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Fran and Alain - Ending

Fran: Oh, Alain! I trust you haven't been tiring yourself out talking to everyone?

Fran: I'll take you far above the clouds, where no one else can find you.

Fran: It would mean we have a few minutes alone together, too.

Miriam: I hope you find the occasion to speak with them as well.

Miriam: Queen Ilenia shall be safe 'neath my watchful eye. I assure you of that.

### Galadmir

#### Galadmir and Alain - Training

**Galadmir:** Now if only you were better suited to fighting beside Ter Eltolinde, you might just earn a passing grade.

**Alain:** I still have much to learn, then.

**Galadmir:** You and Lex have spent a great many years training for this war together. You must learn how to adapt with a new partner, one like me, if you are willing.

**Galadmir:** The stronger you grow, the more assured I can be in Ter Eltolinde's safety under your command.

**Alain:** I look forward to learning what an attendant to the Turenos is capable of.

**Galadmir:** Just the answer I was hoping to hear.

**Alain:** What incredible strength...

**Galadmir:** On your feet, Alain. It is much too early for you to be giving up now.

**Alain:** But of course. I shall press ever onward, if I must.

**Eltolinde:** What is going on here, Galadmir? Alain looks as though he is about to faint.

#### Ring of the Maiden

**Galadmir:** You have picked an interesting setting for a discussion. I presume it is a matter of some importance?

**Alain:** I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

**Galadmir:** The truth, then?

**Alain:** The truth is, I trust you above all others. Not only for your strength, but for your loyalty, your cautious demeanor, everything about you, really.

**Galadmir:** Hence, you would have me wear it?

**Alain:** That is the request I would make of you, yes. Though perhaps I have failed to earn the trust required for such an oath.

**Galadmir:** If anything, I would say your lack of confidence betrays your trust in me.

**Alain:** That was not my intent.

**Galadmir:** Heheh. Apologies for teasing you, Alain. You still have much to learn about me, but I will gladly give you all the time you need. I accept.

**Galadmir:** I have watched you hold the entire Liberation together with your bare hands and sacrifice your own well-being for that of your people. How could I not be certain about such an incredible man? Now, the ring, if you will.

**Alain:** I should have known you would have me beaten in a war of words.

**Galadmir:** This covenant is a profound one, Alain. So do not think you can go before your task is finished.

#### Final Battle

**Galadmir:** Alain!

**Galerius:** The ring is mine to command. Now, bow to your emperor!

**Galadmir:** Is this how your journey ends? A tragic death, possessed by the very evil you sought to unmake? Think of all those you would leave behind. Think of me!

**Alain:** Galadmir...

**Galadmir:** It is all thanks to you.

**Alain:** Galerius, you saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire. But as long as I live and breathe, you will never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

**Alain:** Mother!

**Galadmir:** She is all right. Just a bit shaken up, I imagine.

**Alain:** We end this long-drawn war now.

**Galadmir:** Defeat the man and shatter his cursed sigil, and this will finally be over.

**Galadmir:** Enough of your deranged ambitions.

**Alain:** Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call. Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Ending

**Galadmir:** I certainly never would have accepted your proposal had I doubted you. One look at you here and now, and I have every answer I could ever possibly need.

**Galadmir:** I do wonder if I have outlived my use to you, seeing as the duty of our covenant has been fulfilled. It changes nothing for me, though. I will always be at your side whenever you need it.

**Galadmir:** It has been quite the novel experience, witnessing another land's coronation.

**Eltolinde:** With delegations hailing from every land of Fevrith, it feels as though the entire world has joined hands in harmony.

**Galadmir:** A harmony which will surely see more visitors grace Elheim's forests soon enough. And with any luck, everyone present at today's coronation will continue to strive toward deepening it further.

**Eltolinde:** I pray you are right. Myself among them, of course. May its splendid radiance never fade from this land.

### Gammel

#### Gammel and Alain - Atonement

**Gammel:** So, yeah. Ya ever need someone to go dirtyin' their hands for ya, I'm your guy.

**Alain:** Gammel, I could never ask that of you. Not after you promised me you would be living an honest life now. I will not have you abandon that pursuit in my name.

**Gammel:** still trustin' that I'm a new man, free of all this thievin' business?

**Alain:** I do. And given the matter of your sister, I do not suspect you could do something so foolish.

**Gammel:** Got nothin' to say to that. Maybe it is just my conscience gettin' the better of me. Don't give a damn how dangerous it is, neither. Far as I'm concerned, I shoulda been dead that day back in Coquillage.

**Alain:** That is enough, Gammel. If you truly wish to atone for the sins of your past, you need merely carry their lessons into your future, both for your own sake and for your sister's.

**Gammel:** You're a real piece of work, Alain. But when you're right, you're right. I won't go bringin' this up again.

**Alain:** I pray you do not.

#### Ring of the Maiden

**Gammel:** This supposed to be a joke, boss? You wouldn't catch a damn fool laughin' at it.

**Alain:** I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

**Gammel:** Me, a maiden?

**Alain:** It belongs to the one I trust most, and that would be you, Gammel. Please.

**Gammel:** Always knew ya were naive, but this is somethin' else. You're the only reason I'm not bones and dust right now, so whatever ya say, boss.

**Gammel:** That it?

**Alain:** Indeed. We should now be able to draw on the rings' full power.

**Gammel:** Then what are we waitin' for? It is time we teach Galerius who's king around here.

#### Final Battle

**Gammel:** Boss!

**Galerius:** The ring is mine to command. Now, bow to your emperor!

**Alain:** Gammel!

**Alain:** Galerius, you saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire. But as long as I live and breathe, you will never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

**Gammel:** Boss?

**Alain:** Mother!

**Gammel:** It's okay, boss. She's breathin' just fine.

**Alain:** We end this long-drawn war now.

**Gammel:** Old snake's the lowest of the low.

**Alain:** Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call. Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Ending

**Gammel:** still, ya never know which of 'em might try and stab ya in the back. Can't thank ya enough, boss.

**Gammel:** Any idea what ya wanna do now, Mandrin? Me, I'm gonna travel the world, help people get their lives back together.

**Mandrin:** Like you even have to ask. I'm coming with you.

**Gammel:** Heh. Looks like the Talons are back in business, then.

**Mandrin:** I mean, look at us. Whatever new horizon you're looking at over there, that is the one I wanna see.

**Mandrin:** Never seen you smile that big, Gammel. You gonna tell me what it is for, or what?

**Gammel:** Ain't it obvious? I'm just real excited about the boss here gettin' crowned king.

**Mandrin:** Now tell me the truth or I'll smack it outta you.

**Celeste:** Wow. Gran Corrine is even more magnificent than I had imagined. Her streets are filled to the brim with adoring citizens, and the city's bounds stretch far wider than any book has ever described.

**Celeste:** I would love a tour sometime, if you ever have a moment to spare.

### Gilbert

#### Gilbert and Alain - The War Ahead

**Alain:** Tell me, Gilbert. Are you satisfied with your decision to join our ranks?

**Gilbert:** Hermann and my other retainers are more than capable of guiding Drakenhold forth in my absence. In other words, yes. There is no place I would rather be.

**Alain:** Please, you mustn't speak of debt between us. At times, I wonder if that is merely a lie I tell myself to mask my insatiable thirst for revenge.

**Gilbert:** Your deeds have saved countless lives, Alain. Granted hope to so many who had lost it, including myself.

**Alain:** Even still, I fear there was but one reason for my rushing to your aid. 'Twas not some grand design to see your nation restored, Gilbert, but the selfish desire to add your strength to our own.

**Gilbert:** Rather than press forth into foreign lands, your sole aim would be striking at Galerius as swiftly as possible.

**Alain:** And at the conclusion of this war, a difficult restoration shall await your people.

**Gilbert:** To live in peace as neighbors, as we rightly should. Pardon the lecture, Alain. I should know better than to patronize a future king.

**Alain:** When the scourge of Zenoira is at last no more, what future awaits these lands?

**Gilbert:** Let us begin, Alain.

#### Gilbert and Alain - A Sparring Match

**Gilbert:** Hmph!

**Alain:** Ah! 'Tis an impressive art, one which took all my effort to avoid, even with the knowledge it was coming.

**Gilbert:** Ready thyself.

**Alain:** It would be my honor.

**Gilbert:** What is the meaning of this?

**Alain:** Are you all right, Gilbert? Ah, 'tis but a flamebug.

**Gilbert:** What are you doing to my leg?

**Alain:** If you fail to quickly tend to their bite, it will swell in size and begin to assail you with searing pain. Now, this may hurt, Gilbert, but I ask that you suffer through it.

**Gilbert:** You needn't do any such thing, I assure you. Nrgh.

**Alain:** There. That should be all.

**Gilbert:** It appears you have a wealth of experience in the matter.

**Alain:** Do you fear them in much the same way Virginia does?

**Gilbert:** You truly are an unusual prince, Alain. Though I understand now why Virginia approved of you.

**Alain:** What do you mean?

**Gilbert:** She didn't mention? Had she deemed you unworthy of the throne when you first set foot into Drakenhold, she planned to cut you down where you stood.

**Alain:** That seems rather harsh.

**Gilbert:** It seemed, at times, that she wished to follow directly in Queen Ilenia's regal footsteps. Yet be warned, Alain. She will not accept your failure kindly.

**Alain:** A chilling notion indeed. Can you walk, Gilbert? We should get you to a healer with all haste.

**Gilbert:** Then let us be off.

#### Gilbert and Alain - Drakenhold

**Alain:** I see now why Drakenhold is often said to be the birthplace of dragonkind.

**Gilbert:** Indeed. Marvels such as these are the grandest treasure our kingdom has to offer.

**Alain:** 'Tis nothing at all like the scenery one might see at home in Cornia.

**Gilbert:** Nor is the fact that this nation exists in Cornia's shadow.

**Alain:** I cannot say I have heard that history.

**Gilbert:** Perhaps Josef never saw fit to mention it. Centuries past, your kin came to these lands, and 'twas then that he formed a nation of his own: the nation we now know as Drakenhold.

**Alain:** I never knew of such history, Gilbert.

**Gilbert:** Yet for all its flaws, the people of Drakenhold shall always cling fast to the only home they have ever known. And the fire which burns within their breast is a flame of rebellion against the comfortable lives our neighbors are blessed with.

**Alain:** But Gilbert...

**Gilbert:** From that day forth, I struggled to trust anyone who hailed from Cornian shores. Until I met you, that is. Yet such inequity can breed hatred, a truth often unnoticed by those more fortunate.

**Gilbert:** Heavy weigh the burdens of this long-standing imbalance, on no head more so than the king of Cornia himself. Hold true to your ideals, Alain, for he is a friend I admire quite dearly.

**Alain:** Then I shall ever strive to be a man you can admire, now and for the rest of my days.

#### Ring of the Maiden

**Gilbert:** I feel as though I know why you summoned me here. Speak your part, please.

**Alain:** I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

**Gilbert:** As I suspected. Yet I believe your reason for choosing me lies not with drawing out the ring's power. No, I expect the intent instead falls upon the relation between Cornia and Drakenhold. Am I wrong?

**Alain:** I admit this rite does bring certain advantages. 'Tis a bond of mutual trust, after all.

**Gilbert:** Though the two of us may finally bring this long war to its end, you and I already share deep friendship, with little and less need for covenants to prove it. Hence, I suggest the ring rather go to the one you care for most.

**Alain:** You are a leader as clever as you are careful, Gilbert. But it seems you have miscalculated.

**Gilbert:** Why do you laugh?

**Alain:** The one I care for most is you.

**Gilbert:** I cannot say I ever considered such a notion.

**Alain:** I have to say, it is rather endearing to see you at a loss like this. Quite a stark difference from your normal stateliness.

**Gilbert:** I concede this round. It seems I have no choice but to accept.

**Alain:** Thank you, Gilbert.

**Gilbert:** Indeed, and my nation's future with Cornia appears all the brighter knowing you shall stand at its helm. Now let us expunge Galerius from this world, and usher in a new age through every corner of Fevrith.

#### Final Battle

**Gilbert:** Alain...

**Galerius:** The ring is mine to command. Now, bow to your emperor!

**Gilbert:** You never were the yielding type. Return before me, noble king of Cornia!

**Alain:** Gilbert!

**Alain:** Mother!

**Gilbert:** Rest easy, Alain. She appears to be very much safe.

**Alain:** Thank you.

**Gilbert:** The sigil shall fall, I assure you of it.

**Alain:** Now prepare to be vanquished by the might of Fevrith!

**Gilbert:** Now come. Let prince and king strike together!

#### Ending

**Gilbert:** Though... hm. I shall rather regret returning home without finding the opportunity to do so.

**Virginia:** Well, Gilbert, where shall we be off to next?

**Gilbert:** We shall hold a grand feast to celebrate, from the orange hues of the setting sun till the very first light of dawn.

**Virginia:** Hm. There's a tavern nearby I think you would love. The perfect place for a little drinking contest.

**Gilbert:** Always a competition with you, is it?

**Virginia:** I'll never renounce the thrill of victory, and today I'm feeling even luckier than normal.

**Hermann:** I only pray that this newly discovered bond between our nations never fades into obscurity.

**Gilbert:** Now that it has come to pass, I find it almost as moving as my own coronation.

**Hermann:** I can only assume it is due to your bond of friendship, forged beyond breaking in the furious flames of war. And I believe the relations between Cornia and Drakenhold mirror the ironclad strength of that bond.

**Gilbert:** Indeed. I do pray that our amity remains as such for the rest of our days.

### Gloucester

#### Gloucester Joins the Liberation Army

**Gloucester:** That is not so easy to hear. I have committed horrible crimes toward these people.

**Alain:** Their suffering is yours as well.

**Aubin:** Folks'll realize that if you give 'em time.

**Alain:** Gloucester, will you join us? We mean to reclaim all of Fevrith from Zenoira.

**Gloucester:** I cannot abandon my post as royal guard. Now that I have reclaimed control of my mind, I must watch over the desert. Those were my master's orders.

**Aramis:** A moment, if I may. I would have a word with this royal guard.

**Gloucester:** You...

**Alain:** Aubin, let us give them room.

**Aubin:** Fine by me.

**Gloucester:** Assuming you would accept me, that is.

**Alain:** Gladly. Your strength will be most welcome.

#### Gloucester and Alain - The Desert

**Alain:** I heard that, as Prince Ludwig's retainer, you saw to the well-being of Drakenhold's desert. The distance from Soldraga to the southern reaches is great. Why agree to such a task?

**Gloucester:** A debt grew when my sister married a man from the region. A nation must celebrate all lives, not merely those of its nobles. My nieces and nephews deserve peace without prejudice.

**Alain:** An admirable dream.

**Gloucester:** Then help me, my prince. Together, we can build a brighter future.

**Alain:** My blade is ever yours.

#### Ring of the Maiden

**Gloucester:** I hear you've need of me?

**Alain:** Gloucester, I want you to have this ring.

**Gloucester:** Who are you speaking to exactly? I fail to see any eligible damsels in the vicinity.

**Alain:** I am speaking to you. My partner need not be a maiden. This ring is for the person I trust most to help me end Zenoira. That person is you.

**Gloucester:** If accepting it means saving the desert, the kingdom, and the world, then I would gladly accept any role you deem me fit for.

**Alain:** Then remember this as well: both of us must return alive. Drakenhold will thrive with you there.

**Gloucester:** I will do everything in my power to live on. If not only for myself, then for my home as well.

#### Final Battle

**Gloucester:** My prince!

**Galerius:** The Unicorn's power is mine.

**Gloucester:** No.

**Alain:** I will not be broken.

**Gloucester:** You vowed that both of us would return from this final clash alive.

**Alain:** And I mean to keep that vow.

**Alain:** Mother!

**Gloucester:** Her condition appears stable. You've nothing to worry about.

**Alain:** Thank you.

**Gloucester:** Together, we shall put an end to this vile man and his abhorrent deeds.

**Baltro:** You still defy me?

**Gloucester:** Such single-minded evil...

**Alain:** It ends now.

#### Ending

**Gloucester:** I only pray I can repay the favor over the course of my remaining years.

**Alain:** You already have, many times over.

**Gloucester:** Aramis, did you find occasion to speak with your brother?

**Aramis:** Briefly. Best not to raise suspicions.

**Gloucester:** King Gilbert seemed overjoyed.

**Aramis:** There is no hiding the truth from one as observant as you.

**Gloucester:** Then may that truth guide Drakenhold toward a gentler future.

### Govil

#### Govil and Alain - Not a Pet

**Alain:** Does your tail always move like that?

**Govil:** Not really, no. It just kinda does that sometimes, like when I see a friend come home safe.

**Govil:** You know, I am not a pet. How would you feel if I said you reminded me of a damn monkey?

**Alain:** I meant no offense.

**Govil:** I could get used to "majestic," though. Not that I blame you for thinking a puppy is cute. You just cannot help going over to ruffle their hair, you know? Would not dream of treating an adult like that, though, and I suggest you start thinking the same.

**Govil:** You tell any bestral they remind you of a pet, and they might just try and rip your throat out.

#### Ring of the Maiden

**Alain:** Govil, I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

**Govil:** Whoa there. You sure about this? Guess I am not too surprised, but that thing is made for human fingers. Why give it to me?

**Alain:** Despite your outwardly gruff demeanor, I possess few friends more affectionate and courageous than you.

**Govil:** Fine, then. If that is what you really want, I am your guy. And hey, palling around with the king who saved Fevrith might just make people think different about us bestrals. With you, it feels like that is actually possible.

**Alain:** Thank you, Govil. I promise I will do all I can to make that dream a reality.

**Govil:** The king's right hand, huh? I like the sound of that. Now let us make sure you get that crown back.

#### Final Battle

**Govil:** Alain!

**Galerius:** The ring is mine to command. Now, bow to your emperor!

**Govil:** What kinda sick joke is this? Give him back, or I will take him back!

**Govil:** No giving up, old man!

**Govil:** Not happening. Alain will be back. He has gotta be.

**Govil:** See? I knew you would not go down that easy. Not when we have still got dreams to chase.

**Alain:** Govil!

**Alain:** Galerius, you saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire. But as long as I live and breathe, you will never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

**Govil:** Not if we beat you before that.

**Alain:** Mother!

**Govil:** Hey, she has still got a pulse!

**Alain:** We end this long-drawn war now.

**Govil:** The future of the world's hanging on this, so no messing up, yeah?

**Govil:** Sorry, but we have already had enough nightmares to last a lifetime.

**Alain:** Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call. Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Ending

**Govil:** Not that I am complaining. Oh, and I am ready to start whenever you need me. Never know what might offend someone, you know? So I was hoping you could maybe teach me some etiquette first. Seems only right if I wanna act the part.

**Govil:** Oh, and do not worry. You are coming with me. They are gonna love meeting a king!

**Bertrand:** Ah, though I cannot say I feel any different. Let us enjoy ourselves, hm?

**Bertrand:** After all, my people have been quite fascinated with Cornian culture ever since they first met you.

### Hilda

#### Hilda and Alain - Wyvern Comfort

Alain: I mean not to complain, Hilda, but it appears your wyvern has mistaken me for...

Alain: He's been biting at my hair for some time now, rather forcefully, I might add.

Hilda: It seems he likes you, Alain.

Hilda: He simply wishes to hearten you through all the hardships you endure, day after difficult day.

Hilda: Really, it should come as an honor.

Alain: And it does, most certainly. Yet I fear my life is at risk.

Hilda: In truth, he often does this for me as well, whenever I find myself in a fit of melancholy.

Hilda: Could it be that you're feeling uneasy about something, Alain?

Alain: I hadn't thought it would be that obvious.

Alain: Yet losing a soldier under my command never grows any less painful.

Hilda: I should expect no less from the man who seeks to be king.

Primm: Alain? Is that blood on your forehead?

Alain: Remind me to never be consoled by a wyvern again.

#### Hilda and Alain - Ring of the Maiden

Hilda: I heard mutterings around camp about the rite of covenant. Is that why you've called me here?

Alain: I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

Hilda: You seem quite set on it.

Hilda: In our time together, I've come to know you as a kind man, well deserving of his soldiers' trust and loyalty.

Hilda: But you're still much too naive.

Hilda: That innocence will see your head roll someday, especially if you mean to rule a kingdom.

Hilda: Which is why I would ask you this.

Hilda: You've spoken time and again of your wish to restore order to this land.

Hilda: But are you prepared to deal with the consequences of doing so? To make decisions that mean the life and death of your people?

Alain: Indeed I am.

Alain: Though, I've made a promise to myself.

Hilda: Which is?

Alain: I will never let the luster of the crown wash away my humanity.

Alain: Those who forget the very citizens they claim to serve are unfit to lead, and unfit to rule.

Hilda: There's the Alain I know.

Hilda: But you've changed too. Those eyes burn with the fire of true conviction, just like you say.

Hilda: I'll support you however I'm able, both in leadership and in life.

Alain: I'd like nothing more, Hilda.

Hilda: That's that, then.

Hilda: You may have much to learn, Alain, but being a warm, gentle soul isn't one of those things.

Hilda: Never lose that.

Alain: With you at my side, I never could.

#### Hilda and Alain - Final Battle

Galerius: End this, now.

Galerius: Hmph.

Galerius: Gah.

Alain: Mother!

Galerius: How does it feel, hm? Your dear mother, slain by your own hand?

Alain: What is happening to me?

Hilda: Alain!

Galerius: What a poor fool he was, doomed to the same fate as the pitiful queen before him.

Galerius: His strength surpasses even Ilenia's. The might of the unicorn runs deep in his veins.

Galerius: You'd simply be volunteering your own as my next vessel.

Galerius: The ring is mine to command, and a futile demise is all that awaits you now.

Galerius: None can ever hope to halt my designs. Bow to your emperor.

Hilda: This can't be it... can it?

Galerius: This day is won.

Galerius: You will make a fine Zenoiran vessel once it is over.

Galerius: Enough. Can't you see it's over?

Galerius: The ring...

Galerius: But why does it hold such vast energy?

Hilda: It's really you.

Hilda: Let's see what this ring can do, then.

Galerius: It will take more than this to defeat me.

Hilda: Alain!

Alain: Galerius. You saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire.

Alain: But as long as I live and breathe, you'll never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

Galerius: How do you know of that?

Galerius: You will not!

Galerius: Their emperor shall never know defeat.

Baltro: Your Majesty.

Galerius: Then these insects shall be more than enough. Grant me your strength, and we'll stamp them out together.

Galerius: What do you think you're doing?

Baltro: If it wasn't clear, Your Majesty, the sigil seeks none other.

Galerius: Traitorous fool. Finally gone senile, hm?

Alain: Mother!

Ilenia: Ngh.

Hilda: 'Tis surely some manner of miracle, but the queen still breathes.

Alain: Speak to me, please.

Josef: I never imagined he possessed such frightful mastery over the bodies of others.

Ilenia: Alain. I can't say how much time has passed since that day, but you've grown so much.

Ilenia: If only I could have been there to witness it.

Ilenia: It seems I owe Josef a great deal for raising you in my absence.

Alain: Josef, see my mother somewhere safe.

Josef: And you, Your Highness?

Alain: We end this long-drawn war now.

Hilda: This infernal chapter in Fevrith's history shall finally come to a close.

Josef: Come home, both of you.

Baltro: What evil should I reanimate next? A monster capable of crushing you beneath its heel, perhaps.

Hilda: There's no reasoning with a man given over to delusion. Prepare yourself.

Alain: Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call.

Alain: Your emperor is no more, and in his place stands a tyrannical fiend who craves nothing but absolute control.

Alain: Tell me, is this what you truly desire? To sacrifice your very essence in service of this daemon?

Alain: Souls of the departed, if you have any humanity left within you, lend me your aid.

Alain: These souls are not a power one can wield, Baltro. They are human lives, human will in its purest form.

Alain: Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Hilda and Alain - Ending

Hilda: I can't remember the last time I saw this many people in one place, and I'm not exactly a fan of it myself.

Hilda: And as always, just tell me if there's anything I can do to help. I'll be at your side before the words even cross your lips.

Hilda: Did you enjoy the banquet, Primm?

Primm: More than I even thought possible, yes. But...

Hilda: But what?

Primm: I was so invested in the feast before me that I forgot to search out one of those coins celebrating Alain's coronation.

Primm: Events like these only happen once in a lifetime, and I was too tempted by the allure of sustenance to realize it.

Hilda: Don't worry. Alain handed me two of them just a few moments ago.

Primm: He did?

Primm: I didn't realize my vices were that obvious.

Primm: I have to say, a nation with you as its king does sound appealing.

Primm: Not that there's anything wrong with my own, of course.

Primm: I'm practically certain of it.

### Hodrick

#### Hodrick Freed from Galerius's Spell

Hodrick: What foolishness is this? One such as I, brought low by the Cornian prince.

Josef: You have fallen far indeed, Hodrick.

Josef: How many times did you stare death in the face at Her Majesty's side? Now look what you have become.

Josef: Your Highness?

Alain: I refuse to cut down a friend without first knowing how we have reached this grim conclusion.

Alain: A simple reason is all I ask.

Scarlett: Alain!

Alain: The ring. What sorcery is this?

Hodrick: Ngh. My head...

Alain: A spell to shackle the hearts of men.

Hodrick: That is the only way I can think to describe it, my prince.

Hodrick: That ill-fated day, all the lords closest to your mother turned upon her without so much as a moment's notice.

Hodrick: Unfortunately, my memories end there as well.

Josef: A frightful power, if what you say is true. A spell of control, it could be called.

Josef: Such magick would go far in explaining how Galerius so swiftly brought Fevrith to its knees.

Hodrick: I shudder to think what unspeakable evil I have wrought upon our world these last ten years.

Hodrick: Though there is no greater misdeed than turning my spear upon you, Prince Alain.

Alain: That is enough. You must not blame yourself any further.

Alain: But I do wonder how this ring is capable of unmaking the spell.

Josef: In truth, I had believed it to be a mere symbol of your birthright and regalia, and nothing more.

Josef: To think the power of cleansing truly exists.

Josef: Legend speaks of your ancestors wielding it to purify evil, but I had believed such tales mere fiction.

Scarlett: It is entirely possible that the ring which bears its image is somehow capable of that same power.

Alain: If Galerius's rule is built upon foul sorcery that fetters our people, then this ring is the ray of light that will pierce its wicked heart.

Hodrick: True words, my prince.

Josef: Indeed. Were we able to free those bound by his cruel magicks...

Alain: All told, I have often found myself plagued with doubt. Is it justice that guides our march, or paltry vendetta?

Alain: Yet the answer is clear now. The path before us is laid bare, and all that remains is to walk it.

Alain: Walk it I will, Mother. It may take days, months, or even years, but I shall see the duties of my bloodline fulfilled and slay Galerius like the beast he is.

#### Hodrick and Alain - Castle Balcony

Hodrick: A fine evening, Your Highness.

Alain: It is indeed. The kind of peaceful atmosphere which calls to mind memories of my childhood.

Alain: Do you remember the day you lifted me upon your shoulders, to let me see above the castle balcony?

Hodrick: I would not soon forget it.

Alain: I can almost picture it now, gazing out at the endless lights lying tranquil in the city below.

Hodrick: As can I. Of course, I was still but a young man at the time, and took quite a scolding from Ser Josef for exposing you to such danger.

Alain: I often prayed that I would one day stand as tall as you, that I would bear the strength to support another just as you did for me.

Alain: It is a prayer I continue to offer the heavens even now.

Hodrick: I am certain Queen Ilenia would be pleased to see the fine man you have become.

Alain: I hope you are right.

#### Hodrick and Alain - Pritzlasse

Hodrick: I must say, I never expected to look upon Pritzlasse from within Drakenhold's borders.

Alain: Tell me, did you ever mount an attack on its ramparts while my mother ruled as queen?

Hodrick: Hers was not a reign marked by invasions or offensives, Your Highness.

Hodrick: Yet as this stronghold stands between Cornia and Drakenhold proper, the territory surrounding it has long been disputed.

Hodrick: The day Hodel sought to storm it, I warned him not to cast his men's lives aside so callously.
