Hodel: She should have sent more than a simple knight to stop me. There is nothing you can do to change my mind.

Hodrick: General Valmore himself labors to make peace with our neighbors as we speak.

Hodel: Unlikely as it seems, I have little choice but to verify the truth of that claim myself.

Hodrick: For my part, I have not the slightest doubt you shall see Cornia's bond with her neighbors strengthened beyond belief.

Alain: My thanks for saying so, Hodrick.

Alain: Through the course of this war, our two nations have fought as one: disparate peoples banding together in the face of a common evil.

Alain: I only pray we may do the same upon its conclusion, that all of Fevrith might enjoy a shared peace.

#### Hodrick and Alain - Drinking Contest

Hodrick: The night air is bitter indeed, Your Highness. Please, return with me to the warmth of town.

Alain: Hodrick?

Hodrick: What is it, my liege?

Alain: I know I fear what horrors might transpire, should I ultimately fail in my campaign against Galerius.

Hodrick: In that case, allow me to share with you a tale of my own failure. Long ago, a few fellow soldiers and I shared a drinking contest in a tavern. No matter how many flagons of mead crossed our table, none of us three would yield an inch.

Hodrick: One fell down the stairs of the tavern, his face pouring forth a river of blood. Another found the sight so utterly amusing, he wet his trousers amidst unbridled laughter. The third lost command of his faculties entirely, and awoke in the morning naked in a nearby lea. 'Twas deemed a draw, as you might expect.

Hodrick: Yet none of that was as terrible as the scolding from Ser Josef which awaited us the next day.

Alain: Ah, how I wish to have been a modest moth on that tavern wall.

Hodrick: This was fortunately all before you were born, of course.

Alain: To be honest, it's difficult to even imagine a time when you stood an unruly youth like any other.

Hodrick: Not like any other, Your Highness. I must admit, I was the worst of them all.

Alain: Thank you, Hodrick, for choosing to share this story with me.

Hodrick: I may not be able to lift the burdens from your shoulders, but I shall stand ever at your side when they grow too heavy to bear alone.

Alain: I can't help but wonder, which of the three men were you, Hodrick?

Hodrick: I would very much prefer to leave that to your imagination.

Alain: Now that I think about it, I never have heard how you acquired that scar on your face.

Hodrick: Nor shall you. Let us head to bed, Your Highness.

#### Hodrick and Alain - Ring of the Maiden

Hodrick: I know not why you summoned me here, my prince, but I am ever yours to command. What is it?

Alain: I would like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

Hodrick: Is that truly what you mean, Your Highness?

Alain: Why do you seem so surprised? Surely I have made no secret of the trust I bear for you.

Hodrick: No, I suppose not.

Alain: As a boy, I could not wait to grow as strong and dependable as you.

Hodrick: And that you have become, my prince. Both the pillar of justice upon which we all depend, and a man of great compassion.

Alain: So allow me to ask again. Will you accept this ring?

Hodrick: The ring itself, and the kind words in which you have draped it, are my greatest honor.

Hodrick: I am ready, my prince. Nothing could ever surpass this day. Thank you, truly.

#### Hodrick and Alain - Final Battle

Alain: Emancipate his soul.

Galerius: Hmph.

Galerius: Gah.

Alain: Mother!

Galerius: How does it feel, hm? Your dear mother, slain by your own hand.

Alain: What is happening to me?

Hodrick: Your Highness!

Galerius: His strength surpasses even Ilenia's. The might of the unicorn runs deep in his veins.

Galerius: strike at this new body of mine, if you dare. You would simply be volunteering your own as my next vessel.

Galerius: The ring is mine to command, and a futile demise is all that awaits you now.

Galerius: None can ever hope to halt my designs. Bow to your emperor.

Hodrick: Damn.

Galerius: This day is won.

Galerius: The ring... why does it hold such vast energy?

Hodrick: Your humble servant is here beside you.

Hodrick: You must not give in, Your Highness. We swore to overcome Galerius together, and so we shall.

Galerius: It will take more than this to defeat me.

Hodrick: Welcome home, Your Highness.

Alain: As long as I live and breathe, you will never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

Alain: Piteous ghost of an age long past, I shall grant your soul the freedom it desires.

Galerius: You will not!

Galerius: Their emperor shall never know defeat.

Baltro: Your Majesty.

Galerius: Then these insects shall be more than enough. Grant me your strength, and we will stamp them out together.

Hodrick: strike at us and it shall be the last thing you do.

Galerius: What do you think you are doing?

Baltro: If it was not clear, Your Majesty, the sigil seeks none other.

Galerius: Traitorous fool. Finally gone senile, hm?

Alain: Is that you, Mother?

Ilenia: Ngh.

Hodrick: Merciful Father. Her breathing is steady.

Alain: Speak to me, please.

Alain: Josef, see my mother somewhere safe.

Josef: And you, Your Highness?

Alain: We end this long-drawn war here and now.

Hodrick: With Baltro's death, the vile scourge upon our land shall be lifted. All that remains is to cut him down.

Josef: Come home, both of you.

Baltro: What evil should I reanimate next? A monster capable of crushing you beneath its heel, perhaps.

Hodrick: The man is a devil in every sense of the word. Now let him be judged.

Alain: Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call.

Alain: Your emperor is no more, and in his place stands a tyrannical fiend who craves nothing but absolute control.

Alain: Tell me, is this what you truly desire? To sacrifice your very essence in service of this daemon?

Alain: Souls of the departed, if you have any humanity left within you, lend me your aid.

Alain: These souls are not a power one can wield, Baltro. They are human lives, human will in its purest form.

Alain: Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

### Ithilion

#### Ithilion Joins the Liberation Army

**Mayor:** This is quite the mess you have gotten us into, Elina.

**Elina:** Do you not see he is fighting for the good of Elheim? These people need him. We need him.

**Mayor:** We lack the strength to oust even one soldier, let alone all of Zenoira.

**Mayor:** Lady Rosalinde! Oh, thank the Father you are safe.

**Rosalinde:** Tell me, is Ithilion here?

**Elina:** He departed soon thereafter so as not to put us in harm's way.

**Rosalinde:** Ithilion needs us, Alain.

**Alain:** Indeed, and I am not about to abandon him to his fate. We take the field at once.

**Zenoiran Soldier:** After them! This way!

**Elheim Soldier:** They just keep coming, and our numbers grow ever fewer.

**Ithilion:** steel your resolve and strike true!

**Elina:** Ser Ithilion!

**Ithilion:** Avdryan, Terras. And I am sorry for making you worry, Elina.

**Elina:** None of that, please. I am just glad you are back in one piece.

**Ithilion:** As am I. As you can see, they barely even put a scratch in my armor.

**Mayor:** Pardon me, Lady Rosalinde, but what would you have us do now?

**Rosalinde:** We will repay the blood they have spilled in our name by joining them in their cause.

**Alain:** We are most grateful, I assure you.

**Rosalinde:** They sought refuge here when your king could only offer respite, and before we too came under threat.

**Ithilion:** As long as your star shines for the Liberation, Terras, mine too shall shine with it.

**Alain:** There would be no greater honor.

**Elina:** If I may, Ser Ithilion. When the war is over, what will happen to this town?

**Ithilion:** You have shown me greater kindness than I ever thought possible. But there is no foe more terrible than the one we face now, and I will not make a promise I may not be able to keep.

**Elina:** Know, then, that I will be praying for your safety, just as I always have, and just as I always will.

**Ithilion:** Thank you, Elina. And may life treat you better than I have.

**Ithilion:** Count me among the Liberation's numbers, and together we will free this land.

#### Ithilion and Alain - The Underground City

**Alain:** While I am aware that Rosalinde's palace lies underground, what about you, Ithilion? Have you spent much of your life beneath the surface as well?

**Ithilion:** I have. Until I joined her personal guard, I had little reason to leave our subterranean city, so I almost never did. As a child, the sun was always more of a concept than an actual entity which existed in my world.

**Alain:** No other race of Fevrith has most of their population consigned to life secluded within the earth.

**Ithilion:** Maybe not, but it has its benefits. For one, the insular nature of our cities means few invaders think to attack. And those that do often end up lost in a maze of corridors. I can only assume that is why Zenoira went after Laurhal instead.

**Alain:** A cruel twist of fate indeed.

**Ithilion:** Life was good before they turned up. I can still remember the wonder that filled my heart with every word of Ter Rosalinde's tales: to accompany her on the journeys she recounted, to stand in her defense should the need ever arise.

**Alain:** Which is why you now serve in her personal guard.

**Ithilion:** Exactly. I swear to you, Alain, never again will the shadow of Zenoira hang over this nation. And no matter what happens in the course of this war, I will always be there to protect Ter Rosalinde, with my very life if I must.

#### Ring of the Maiden

**Ithilion:** Was there something you need of me?

**Alain:** I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

**Ithilion:** Are you certain the role is mine?

**Alain:** History will surely sing of your undying loyalty, and I can only hope they depict it at my side. Not to mention your skill with the sword. Such talents are a gift to the world over.

**Ithilion:** That is nothing remarkable. It is what is expected from Ter Rosalinde's personal guard. Namely, keeping my Terras safe.

**Alain:** Indeed, and Galerius's downfall will finally bring the peace that Elheim has craved for so long.

**Ithilion:** Then it seems I only have one answer. My blade belongs not only to Ter Rosalinde, but to you as well.

**Alain:** Thank you, Ithilion. Your strength should prove invaluable in the days to come.

**Ithilion:** I swear it will. And believe me, I do not make promises I cannot keep.

#### Final Battle

**Ithilion:** Alain!

**Galerius:** The ring is mine to command. Now, bow to your emperor!

**Ithilion:** Good to have you back. Now come on, stay with me. We have a monster to slay.

**Alain:** Galerius, you saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire.

**Ithilion:** He plans to fight till his last breath, but we shall be the ones to end him.

**Alain:** Mother!

**Ithilion:** At peace, Alain. The queen still lives.

**Alain:** We end this long-drawn war now.

**Ithilion:** Come. The decrepit fool will not live to see another day.

**Ithilion:** Enough of your tripe.

**Alain:** Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call. Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Ending

**Ithilion:** To be honest, when you asked me to swear that covenant, I was not entirely sure I was up to the task. Thank you for granting me the opportunity again.

**Ithilion:** Ter Rosalinde told me to simply enjoy myself for the day, but how am I to do that, exactly?

**Lhinalagos:** After all, it would be quite the shame for us to come all this way only to stand outside the gates.

**Ithilion:** I would like that, yes. It has been far too long since we last had the chance to relax like this.

**Lhinalagos:** Your command in securing this city was nigh flawless, if you will allow me the compliment. The legend of the hero and his journey to redeem our land, and Fevrith whole, will surely live on.

### Jerome

#### Jerome Joins the Liberation Army

**Lotti:** Lord Jerome must know of this!

**Jerome:** Agh! Now look what you have made me do.

**Lotti:** Might I ask what you are making?

**Jerome:** Just a little something for the neighbors. Not that it matters anymore. Now, I assume you have some reason for this unannounced interference?

**Lotti:** They dare come here.

**Jerome:** Zenoira?

**Lotti:** Apparently so. But is this not the opportunity?

**Jerome:** I fear that is not a choice we can make. Zenoira has men stationed at just about every corner in town. You can imagine the consequences for our citizens should we aid the Liberation and lose.

**Lotti:** I suppose so, yes.

**Jerome:** Remember, all that we do is for our people. We will fight the enemy, and we will win. Now prepare for battle, and fetch my sharpest lance. I will be welcoming them myself.

**Jerome:** My road ends here.

**Alain:** You speak the truth, yes, but that does not change the fact that you swore no fealty to Zenoira. Your people all spoke with one voice of their lord's undying devotion to their well-being. So I ask you again: will you join us?

**Jerome:** As if I could refuse a request so boldly impassioned. Very well. It is with great pride and humility that I accept your offer.

**Jerome:** My lance rests with you, and with all those who have trusted me to guide it true. I will see that it does not disappoint.

**Lotti:** Do not worry. I will stay here and stand guard over the city.

#### Jerome and Alain - Letters

**Jerome:** Better now, thank you. The wound has already healed, and I shall surely stand ready to partake in our next battle. As you might imagine, I have grown rather worried for my people's well-being since departing the city.

**Jerome:** Yet before I found opportunity to ask of their fortune myself, they began to send me missives such as these of their own accord.

**Jerome:** I was always so frantic when I lived amongst them, but the more you hasten, the less you truly see of your surroundings. Such anxieties often plagued my mind. Now, to know they think of me frequently enough to send me letters, I feel at great peace, I must admit.

**Jerome:** Both for my people, and for all who reside on this beloved continent of ours.

**Alain:** Once Cornia is at last restored, I hope to rule my kingdom in much the same way.

**Lotti:** Shouldn't you be off saving the world, rather than wasting precious days here in our modest province?

**Jerome:** I simply had to return after receiving those letters from our people, if even for a moment.

**Lotti:** All this time, I had thought you had been relieved of your duties with the Liberation. I even saw him giving souvenirs from your travels to a couple of local kids just now.

**Alain:** It is a pleasure we have someone like you amidst our ranks, Jerome.

**Jerome:** I would much prefer not to halt our army's advance any further than I already have.

**Lotti:** A moment, Lord Jerome. Keep that fire burning strong, and win the peace this world deserves. Oh, and one more thing: who knows when he might decide to oust you for real. Sorry, I did not mean to worry you. I am sure you will be just fine. Be well, my lord!

**Jerome:** I shall strive to do just that. I only pray my presence does not hinder their progress.

#### Ring of the Maiden

**Jerome:** I have word you summoned me.

**Alain:** Jerome, I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

**Jerome:** A test, is it? Hrm. What is a loyal knight meant to say in such a thorny situation?

**Alain:** Calm yourself, please. I assure you, I am not expecting any particular response.

**Jerome:** Nrgh. How shall I ever divulge it? If Alain ever knew I asked my adherents to observe us for fear of being ousted, he would surely oust me then and there.

**Alain:** Listen to me, Jerome. From the day we first met, it was clear how deep and earnest your love for your people was. I would like nothing more than to extend that love toward the entire kingdom, to greet the dawning of peace with you at my side. Would you accept this ring as a symbol of that wish?

**Jerome:** My word. I never dreamt you felt that way. If you are assured in your decision, I would be honored to accept.

**Lotti:** Looks like it all went perfectly to plan.

**Alain:** Indeed it did. Thank you for making sure he did not run off.

**Jerome:** You mean to say you conspired against me?

#### Final Battle

**Jerome:** Lord Alain!

**Galerius:** The ring is mine to command. Now, bow to your emperor!

**Jerome:** No!

**Jerome:** The man who redeemed my life and so many others could never be consumed by such base evil. Return to us, my lord! Sever this villainry.

**Alain:** Jerome!

**Alain:** Galerius, you saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire. But as long as I live and breathe, you will never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

**Alain:** Mother!

**Jerome:** Her condition appears stable, my lord.

**Alain:** We end this long-drawn war now.

**Jerome:** Indeed, the final battle is upon us at last. All that remains is to seize our well-deserved victory.

**Jerome:** I tire of this inhuman treachery. Make him repent, by force if we must.

**Alain:** Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call. Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Ending

**Jerome:** After all, you are the one who delivered the world from evil, while I was merely a sworn assistant. Though perhaps I should stop mentioning it, lest you begin having doubts yourself.

**Jerome:** Thank you, my king. 'Tis no greater honor than to serve at your side.

**Lotti:** Shall we make for Albion, Lord Jerome?

**Jerome:** Ah, well. Perhaps we could stay here just a few moments longer.

**Lotti:** Of course, ser. The decision is yours.

**Lotti:** Lord Jerome must really yearn for the companionship he gained while marching with the Liberation, though I am not sure he even realizes it himself.

**Lotti:** May the Father's light always shine upon your sacred kingdom.

### Josef

#### Josef and Alain - Overwork

Alain: Rgh.

Josef: Are you all right, Your Highness?

Alain: I am. It is merely a headache, is all. Worry not, Josef. I intend to be off to bed any minute now.

Josef: I wish that were true, yet the maps and tactical reports in your hand appear to speak otherwise.

Alain: What manner of leader would I be, should I only rely on the knowledge of others?

Josef: A sensible one, considering the alternative. Now come, you clearly need your rest.

Alain: But if I do not do this, who will?

Josef: Listen to me, my prince. I say this not as your advisor, but as the father given care of you by Queen Ilenia.

Josef: I cannot bear to see you suffer like this, to watch fits of pain cast across your face.

Alain: Then I will not put you through it any longer. I only ask that you help me to my tent in return.

Josef: As you wish. Come with me.

Josef: Are you warm enough, Your Highness?

Alain: I am. It feels as though I am a child again, under your attentive care as I was for so many years on Palevia. Thank you, Josef.

Josef: Be assured in that growth, and let your worries be washed away by the gentle tide of sleep.

Josef: Even in slumber, I can still see echoes of the boy you once were.

Josef: I am the blade of the royal family, and nothing more.

#### Josef and Alain - Old Diplomacy

Alain: Having trouble sleeping, Josef?

Josef: Good evening, Your Highness. I was merely recalling the last time I set foot in these lands, on a voyage of duty at Queen Ilenia's side.

Alain: If you would not mind sharing the tale with me, that is.

Josef: Few in Cornia had ever laid eyes on a bestral before that day.

Alain: And for what purpose were they advancing into our territory?

Josef: That was what we hoped to learn ourselves, and so we sent the lord of the region, Reimann, to capture the errant bestrals.

Alain: The foul sorcerer who betrayed our nation.

Josef: Shortly after, an envoy of soldiers crossed the border from Elheim and demanded we hand over any bestrals we were able to capture.

Josef: Reimann claimed it naught but pretext for the elven nation to invade our own.

Alain: And yet Elheim has little reason for such a move, given their long lifespans and slower population growth.

Josef: Right you are. Queen Ilenia argued those very points herself.

Josef: But there can be no discounting the inordinate fear which people have for the unknown.

Josef: This particular region of Elheim is home to many half-elves, while the pure-blooded tend to be few and far between.

Josef: Reimann insisted they were warriors kept hidden in this territory with the intent of launching an eventual attack.

Josef: Sensing the danger in such spiteful sentiments, Queen Ilenia requested an audience with the then Turenos of Elheim, and I accompanied Her Majesty as her personal guard.

Alain: Were you able to reach a resolution?

Josef: It was upon the fulfillment of that agreement that this cautionary tale met its conclusion.

Alain: I had not realized these lands held such history.

Josef: I have every faith that such skill lives on within you as well.

Alain: I pray you are right. Thank you, Josef, for sharing this story with me.

#### Josef and Alain - Ilenia

Alain: It occurs to me, Josef, that I would never be standing here now without your tireless support.

Josef: Not at all, Your Highness. In fact, I believe it is your kindness which has drawn such wealth of strength to our army.

Alain: I beg to differ. I'm not sure you remember this, but...

Josef: That shall be enough training for the day, my prince.

Alain: Am I getting stronger now?

Josef: Not yet, no. True power demands years of daily practice, while our work has only continued for mere months.

Alain: Hey, look at that flower. I wish my mom was here to see it. She loved flowers.

Josef: Indeed she did. I'm certain the sight would bring her great joy.

Alain: Oops. I'm sorry, Josef.

Josef: For what, exactly?

Alain: I'm not supposed to think about my mom anymore.

Josef: And why would you believe such a thing?

Alain: Nothing I do is ever going to bring her back.

Josef: You have no need to forget her memory, or to stop speaking of her.

Alain: Really?

Josef: The only thing you mustn't do is let yourself be held captive by your grief.

Alain: But remembering her is what makes me sad.

Josef: Yet those memories shall be the very thing that drives you forth in life. Treasure them, as you treasured your mother herself. And pray, never forget that I shall always stand beside you in your times of need.

Alain: Okay.

Josef: I suppose I had forgotten about that, yes.

Alain: In a sense, it's almost as though I stole your life from you.

Josef: I have served as I always have, ever since I was first appointed knight's captain.

Alain: For showing me such warmth of heart all these years.

Josef: A task which I shall gratefully continue for as long as I have left on this earth.

#### Josef and Alain - Ring of the Maiden

Josef: I presume you seek advice regarding the rite, Your Highness. My ears are yours, should you need them.

Alain: I would like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

Josef: This cannot do. I am naught but a humble servant to the crown, hardly worthy of swearing a covenant as your equal.

Alain: I am told the power of these rings grows exponentially with the bond of trust shared by their bearers.

Alain: Do you believe in that bond, Josef?

Josef: Unquestionably.

Alain: Long years have passed since we first fled to Palevia.

Alain: I was a child then, terrified of the dark shadows lurking behind every corner. But I was not alone, with you watching over me.

Alain: You are the closest thing to a father I have ever had, Josef. And now I ask that you walk with me on a new path for all of Cornia.

Josef: Your Highness...

Josef: I think of you the same way, though I dare not let such words pass my lips.

Josef: All this while, I have struggled desperately to keep the tiny flame of Cornia's royal lineage ablaze.

Josef: To imagine it would now blaze radiant as the midday sun...

Josef: You have grown more than I believed possible, Alain.

Alain: Does that mean you will accept?

Josef: Indeed it does. This battle of wills could only have had one winner.

Alain: Our covenant is sealed.

Josef: In sooth, Your Highness, I would like nothing more than to ruminate upon the honor you have granted me here.

Josef: Yet now is not the time for sentimentality. Galerius must be slain, and we shall be the ones playing the executioner.

#### Josef and Alain - Final Battle

Alain: Galerius, Emperor of Zenoira.

Galerius: If you hope to speak, you will find me no willing participant. I have no words for you.

Galerius: End this, now.

Galerius: Gah.

Alain: Mother!

Galerius: How does it feel, hm? Your dear mother, slain by your own hand.

Alain: What is happening to me?

Galerius: What a poor fool he was, doomed to the same fate as the pitiful queen before him.

Galerius: His strength surpasses even Ilenia's. The might of the unicorn runs deep in his veins.

Galerius: strike at this new body of mine, if you dare. You would simply be volunteering your own as my next vessel.

Galerius: The ring is mine to command, and a futile demise is all that awaits you now.

Galerius: None can ever hope to halt my designs.

Galerius: Worry not. You will make a fine Zenoiran vessel once it is over.

Galerius: The ring... why does it hold such vast energy?

Galerius: It will take more than this to defeat me. Zenoira's reign shall never end.

Josef: Alain!

Alain: Galerius. You saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire.

Galerius: How do you know of that?

Galerius: You will not!

Josef: Behind me, Your Highness.

Galerius: While the souls of Zenoira remain trapped in the Beyond, their emperor shall never know defeat.

Baltro: Your Majesty.

Galerius: How goes the rite?

Galerius: Then these insects shall be more than enough. Grant me your strength, and we will stamp them out together.

Galerius: What do you think you are doing?

Baltro: If it was not clear, Your Majesty, the sigil seeks none other.

Galerius: Traitorous fool. Finally gone senile, hm?

Alain: Mother!

Ilenia: Ngh.

Alain: Speak to me, please.

Josef: I never imagined he possessed such frightful mastery over the bodies of others.

Ilenia: Alain. I cannot say how much time has passed since that day, but you have grown so much.

Ilenia: If only I could have been there to witness it.

Alain: Scarlett, see my mother somewhere safe.

Baltro: Your end draws near.

Alain: Many times you have tried, Baltro, but you shall never break our spirit. I promise you that.

Alain: Now prepare to be vanquished by the might of Fevrith.

Josef: I failed in my duty ten years past, but I shall not falter again.

Josef: We shall never let you so callously trample their memory.

Alain: Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call.

Alain: Your emperor is no more, and in his place stands a tyrannical fiend who craves nothing but absolute control.

Alain: Tell me, is this what you truly desire? To sacrifice your very essence in service of this daemon?

Alain: Souls of the departed, if you have any humanity left within you, lend me your aid.

Alain: These souls are not a power one can wield, Baltro. They are human lives, human will in its purest form.

Alain: Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Josef and Alain - Ending

Josef: I swore my life on guiding you to the throne, no matter the cost such a duty might incur.

Josef: And as your faithful servant, I will walk ever at your side until my legs may no longer carry me.

Josef: Ah, I can still remember when you were but a child. How you have grown, my king, since our days on Palevia.

### Kitra

#### Kitra and Alain - The Wrong Hammer

Alain: Kitra? That hammer you're carrying...

Kitra: What about it?

Alain: I can't say I remember seeing such intricate carvings on its handle.

Kitra: I must've grabbed the wrong one from the armory this morning.

Alain: Is there a reason you don't keep your weapon at your side, as most of our soldiers do?

Kitra: Besides, sleeping next to something I've used for war would just give me nightmares, y'know?

Alain: Hm. Now you have me considering whether I should even be keeping my sword with me.

Kitra: I don't have to do anything like that myself.

Alain: Though taking the wrong weapon by mistake certainly could cause problems were battle to strike.

Kitra: Right. I'd better go give it back to 'em. Oh, and thanks for noticing, Prince.

Alain: Perhaps Josef would know a method of quickly telling them apart.

#### Kitra and Alain - Helping Friends

Kitra: That's that taken care of. Now, what's next?

Alain: Mending your equipment, Kitra?

Kitra: Oh! Hi, Prince.

Kitra: Anyway, I'm hoping it'll all be done by the time they get outta bed in the morning.

Alain: In that case, I will help.

Kitra: You, Prince?

Alain: Is there a problem with that? Everything this army does is for my sake, so it's only fair I return the favor every now and then.

Alain: Besides, the work will go far quicker with two of us, will it not?

Kitra: Well, yeah, but... you sure you've got the time for this?

Alain: Beyond sure. Simply tell me where to start and it shall be done.

Kitra: I'm gonna stay here and finish patching up this saddle for now.

Alain: I would be glad to. Best of luck in your task, Kitra.

Alain: I hadn't expected a simple meal to prove so bothersome, yet at last, the deed is done.

Kitra: But look at that. Just a couple hours, and we're all finished.

Alain: Fran and Miriam are lucky indeed to have a friend as kind and thoughtful as you.

Kitra: You really think so?

#### Kitra and Alain - Ring of the Maiden

Kitra: What's up, Prince? Got something you wanna tell me?

Alain: I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

Kitra: Look, I know this thing's about trust and all, but I'm not exactly the "maiden" kinda girl. You sure?

Alain: I am. There's none other I would ask this of.

Alain: Is it truly such an odd request? You're pure of heart, Kitra. True to yourself, and strong besides.

Alain: Which doesn't even account for your compassion, your kindness, your diligence, your dedication.

Alain: With a partner as marvelous as you by my side, the ring's power will surely never falter.

Kitra: Urgh!

Alain: Kitra?

Kitra: Just stop!

Alain: Did I say something wrong?

Kitra: Ugh, I don't even know how I'm supposed to respond to that.

Alain: Sorry.

Kitra: Fine then. I'll do it.

Alain: Thank you, Kitra. I'd have it no other way.

Kitra: Done and done. Zenoira won't know what hit 'em.

Alain: And there's that strength again. I'm honored to be able to call it mine.

#### Kitra and Alain - Final Battle

Galerius: End this, now.

Galerius: Hmph.

Galerius: Gah.

Alain: Mother!

Galerius: How does it feel, hm? Your dear mother, slain by your own hand?

Alain: What is happening to me?

Kitra: Yo, what's wrong, Prince?

Galerius: His strength surpasses even Ilenia's. The might of the unicorn runs deep in his veins.

Galerius: strike at this new body of mine, if you dare.

Galerius: You'd simply be volunteering your own as my next vessel.

Galerius: The ring is mine to command, and a futile demise is all that awaits you now.

Galerius: None can ever hope to halt my designs. Bow to your emperor.

Galerius: This day is won.

Galerius: You will make a fine Zenoiran vessel once it is over.

Galerius: Enough. Can't you see it's over?

Galerius: The ring...

Galerius: But why does it hold such vast energy?

Kitra: I knew you wouldn't quit on me, Prince.

Kitra: Now c'mon. We've got a tyrant to beat.

Galerius: It will take more than this to defeat me.

Kitra: Alain!

Alain: Galerius. You saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire.

Alain: But as long as I live and breathe, you'll never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

Galerius: How do you know of that?

Galerius: Their emperor shall never know defeat.

Baltro: Your Majesty.

Galerius: How goes the rite?

Galerius: Then these insects shall be more than enough. Grant me your strength, and we'll stamp them out together.

Galerius: What do you think you're doing?

Baltro: If it wasn't clear, Your Majesty, the sigil seeks none other.

Galerius: Traitorous fool. Finally gone senile, hm?

Alain: Mother!

Ilenia: Ngh.

Kitra: It's okay, Prince. She's breathing just fine.

Alain: Speak to me, please.

Josef: I never imagined he possessed such frightful mastery over the bodies of others.

Ilenia: Alain. I can't say how much time has passed since that day, but you've grown so much.

Ilenia: If only I could have been there to witness it.

Josef: And you, Your Highness?

Kitra: I'm ready when you are. That sigil won't stand a chance against us.

Josef: Come home, both of you.

Baltro: What evil should I reanimate next? A monster capable of crushing you beneath its heel, perhaps.

Alain: Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call.

Alain: Your emperor is no more, and in his place stands a tyrannical fiend who craves nothing but absolute control.

Alain: Tell me, is this what you truly desire? To sacrifice your very essence in service of this daemon?

Alain: Souls of the departed, if you have any humanity left within you, lend me your aid.

Alain: These souls are not a power one can wield, Baltro. They are human lives, human will in its purest form.

Alain: Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Kitra and Alain - Ending

Kitra: And that beaming smile? It was like nothing I've ever seen.

Kitra: I'm getting you back for what you said at the altar. Hope you don't mind.

### Leah

#### Leah and Virginia Rejoin Alain

Virginia: Josef!

Josef: You were a child when last we met, but now a princess fair and true.

Virginia: A lot can change in ten years.

Josef: I am relieved to see you safe.

Virginia: The same to you. When our scouts brought word of your army's approach, I knew you were in hiding.

Virginia: I was sent here to Drakenhold ten years past as a refugee when Galerius rose.

Virginia: There's nothing to forgive. My attendant Leah sees my every need fulfilled.

Leah: The issue at hand, your ladyship?

Virginia: Go on, then. Yes, yes.

Leah: The good Prince Gilbert is currently amassing troops at Baumratte in hopes of recapturing his castle.

Leah: We ask that you and your soldiers cooperate in that siege.

Leah: But such a request must surely meet the approval of your commander. Might we solicit an audience?

Virginia: Ah, I almost forgot. Where is he?

Alain: It's been too long, Virginia.

Virginia: Is that you, Alain? I barely recognized you, grown as you are.

Virginia: What I mean to say is, I'm proud of you.

Virginia: That, and that my blade belongs to this Liberation of yours from here forward.

Leah: Your ladyship, please. This isn't a decision you should make without at least consulting him first.

Virginia: I admit I owe him quite a lot for what he's done. I don't plan on letting that debt go unpaid.

Virginia: Which is exactly why Alain here is going to help us, yes? Everybody wins by my count.

Virginia: Satisfied?

Lex: Hey, uh, you sure about this? She seemed more like a windstorm than a...

Alain: She was always more sister than cousin to me, in truth. Whenever I needed an ear, hers was the first I'd pull.

Alain: In any case, Leah, the Liberation Army will answer your call.

Alain: And thank you for the kindness you've shown Virginia all these years. I know she can be a bit difficult.

Leah: 'Tis no greater kindness than yours, Prince. Cornia's aid is a beacon of light in our darkest hour.

#### Leah and Alain - Drakenhold Service

Alain: I've been curious, Leah. How did you come to enter Gilbert's service?

Leah: Through my duty to the royal court, of course. Even at a young age, I often attended to the late King Hugo.

Alain: 'Tis the role of your family, then, to maintain the brilliance of Drakenhold's crown.

Leah: From what I've been told, I was left at the gates of Castle Soldraga as a newborn.

Alain: Forgive me. I didn't mean to assume.

Leah: He treated me almost like his own daughter at times, brushing my hair and doing whatever he could to ensure I felt comfortable.

Leah: Yet I know one thing for certain. I owe my life to the royal family.

Alain: Understandably so, yes.

Leah: But my stance on the matter will be forever unchanged.

Alain: No matter how hard you wished it was love, and only love.

Leah: Yet whatever the reason, the fact still remains that I was saved. In light of that truth, I've nothing but the utmost gratitude.

Leah: Know that I shall ever hold that same gratitude deep in my heart.

#### Leah and Alain - Sleepless Night

Alain: Leah!

Leah: Is everything all right, my prince?

Leah: I'm fine, yes. Though at times after everyone else has gone to sleep, I find myself succumbing to a sudden rush of loneliness.

Leah: A sensation which can only be swept away by the gentle evening breeze.

Alain: It frightened Josef to no end, to wake up in the middle of the night and find me missing.

Leah: Something similar happened to me once.

Leah: He feared the worst, of course. But rather than scold me, he simply ushered me back to my room and began to sing.

Leah: In that moment, I couldn't help but wonder if that was what it felt like to have parents of my own.

Alain: 'Tis a lovely memory indeed.

Alain: But if you'd like, I would be glad to stay at your side until the tide of sleep eventually rolls in.

Leah: Should you not be getting rest yourself, my prince?

Alain: Perhaps you could tell me more of King Hugo while I do.

Leah: I would very much like that.

Leah: Now, when I was just a girl of only seven or eight...

#### Leah and Alain - Ring of the Maiden

Leah: Apologies for keeping you, my prince. Is there something I can help with?

Alain: I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

Leah: In truth, I had believed it some grave error that I found myself asked here.

Leah: How could I possibly be worthy of such an honor?

Alain: Hold your gaze high, Leah.

Alain: We've spent many a sleepless night of late, locked in gripping conversation.

Alain: And while time may slip through our fingers like so many grains of sand, some thoughts never fade from my mind.

Alain: How dedicated and kind you are. How true to yourself. How utterly stunning in every way.

Leah: I'm not sure how to respond.

Leah: I never had anything growing up, not until Gilbert and his late father gave me a home to call my own.

Leah: Yet amid the long, silent nights in cold castle walls, I couldn't help but wonder why I was brought into this world only to be abandoned in my infancy.

Alain: Leah...

Leah: But every minute with you has been...

Leah: For the first time in all my years, I've realized my purpose on this earth.

Leah: I want to protect the kingdom who welcomed me as family when I had none.

Leah: That, and I want to do so beside the first man who's ever made me feel loved as I truly am.

Leah: I've waited my entire life for this moment, and I wouldn't dare let it slip away. My answer is yes, Alain.

Alain: You'll never be alone again, for as long as I live. I shall be with you, always.

Alain: Thank you for your courage. I'm thrilled to hear it.

Alain: And should sleep ever elude you, I'd be more than happy to while the night away in loving conversation.

Leah: I can't wait.

#### Leah and Alain - Final Battle
