Ilenia: Ngh.

Leah: It's all right, Alain. Her life is in no danger.

Alain: Speak to me, please.

Josef: I never imagined he possessed such frightful mastery over the bodies of others.

Ilenia: Alain. I can't say how much time has passed since that day, but you've grown so much.

Ilenia: If only I could have been there to witness it.

Alain: Josef, see my mother somewhere safe.

Alain: We end this long-drawn war now.

Leah: Our lands, our homes, will suffer his infernal schemes no longer.

Josef: Come home, both of you.

Baltro: What evil should I reanimate next? A monster capable of crushing you beneath its heel, perhaps.

Leah: Foul beast who preys on others. Prepare to meet your end.

Alain: Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call.

Alain: Your emperor is no more, and in his place stands a tyrannical fiend who craves nothing but absolute control.

Alain: Tell me, is this what you truly desire? To sacrifice your very essence in service of this daemon?

Alain: Souls of the departed, if you have any humanity left within you, lend me your aid.

Alain: These souls are not a power one can wield, Baltro. They are human lives, human will in its purest form.

Alain: Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Leah and Alain - Ending

Leah: This is where I belong, Alain, now and forevermore.

Leah: With you.

Aramis: Know that however far I may be, I shall never stop believing in your cause.

### Lex

#### Alain and Lex - Worry

Lex: All that worrying is going to kill you one of these days. Let me guess, it is about Scarlett?

Alain: I could not pretend otherwise. The lie would escape before it touched my lips.

Alain: It has been some time since she was abducted, and all I have been afforded are vague prayers.

Lex: You have done plenty. I know how badly you want her back, but we are going to need more people if we want a real shot at it.

Alain: Perhaps, yet the danger to Scarlett grows with each grain passing through the hourglass.

Lex: Renault is the last thing we have to worry about right now. We are getting there.

Lex: You are getting there, even though you are very good at not seeing it.

Lex: Do not try to do this alone. There is only one way we are saving Scarlett, and that is together. But we will save her. I would bet my life on it.

#### Lex and Alain - Training on Palevia

Alain: You always were the optimist.

Lex: Dammit. You got a good hit in, I will give you that. There is just no stopping you these days.

Alain: Yet you have grown no less than I have.

Alain: still, we could likely train for the rest of our lives and even then never manage to best Josef.

Lex: Weird to think he is back on the mainland now, finally making that Liberation Army thing a reality.

Lex: Guess that means we will be going up against Zenoira soon.

Alain: Indeed it does.

Alain: Should I turn a deaf ear to those suffering, I would have little claim to feel this crown is mine.

Alain: That, and I owe it to my mother to keep them safe.

Lex: Well, yeah, but Zenoira has the whole world in the palm of their hand. How are we going to fight back against that?

Lex: You have got a point there. Sorry for not sounding all too confident.

Lex: Just make sure you do not take it all on yourself. I will be with you every step of the way.

Alain: Thank you, Lex. You know I cannot do this without you.

Lex: stop. You are going to make me blush.

Lex: Anyway, that is enough training for today. We are going to miss lunch if we do not get moving.

Alain: I suppose it is that time.

Alain: Hm? It is a ship.

Lex: Looks like they are flying Zenoiran colors, too.

Alain: This island is no longer safe. We have to tell the others.

Lex: You head for the cathedral. I will make sure the town knows what is coming.

#### Lex and Alain - His Mother's Pie

Lex: I got some bread for Alain, fresh out of the oven.

Lex: Here, I will tear off half for you.

Lex: I might even start a bakery once we are done with all this war stuff.

Lex: It is a northern specialty, meant to go with a nice hot bowl of soup.

Alain: What is this wonderful smell?

Lex: Perfect timing, Alain.

Alain: Is that a pie you have there?

Lex: I could not help remembering the way my mom always used to make it, too.

Alain: A task we often carried out without even needing to be asked, all in hopes of another delicious bite.

Lex: Here. Let me know if I did her justice.

Alain: Lex, this is wonderful.

Alain: The subtle dusting of sugar perfectly complements the tartness of the berries, while the flaky crust ties together the entire ensemble.

Alain: It is just as I remember it.

Lex: If you say it is good, then surely everyone else will like it too.

Alain: It brings back thoughts of Palevia, and of our time spent with your mother.

Alain: Hrm?

Lex: What is wrong, Alain?

Alain: My head feels strange, somehow.

Lex: Uh-oh. Chloe told me to add some wine to the filling for a bit of extra flavor.

Lex: Maybe I should not have poured the whole bottle in after all.

#### Lex and Alain - Cape's Grave

Lex: Here's the place.

Alain: Where have you brought me, Lex?

Lex: You remember Cape? The dog we used to play with when we were kids? This is her grave.

Alain: As if I could ever forget her. She was a sweet girl, who loved us just as much as we did her, and possibly far more so.

Alain: You never told me what happened that day. Only that you had buried her, and nothing more. Could you tell me now, Lex?

Lex: Long as you're sure that's what you want. You and Josef were off training somewhere, so it was just me and her taking a walk over in town. That's when we got jumped by a bandit.

Alain: What?

Lex: Next thing I knew, Cape was biting at the guy's legs, trying to give me a chance to get away. But there's only so much a dog can do against a monster with a knife. I'm sorry I didn't tell you, Alain. I knew what was coming, but I was just too much of a damn coward to do anything about it.

Alain: It was around then that you began to focus more on your training, wasn't it?

Lex: And for you, if it comes down to it, I'm ready to do the same thing she did.

Alain: Well, I'll not stand for it. Never again shall I stand and watch while a dear friend casts their life away.

Lex: Almost forgot. I brought some of Cape's favorite snacks to lay on her grave. Thanks for everything, old girl.

#### Lex and Alain - Ring of the Maiden

Lex: Let me guess, lady troubles? You called the right guy.

Alain: I would like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

Lex: Sure you do. You think this is funny?

Alain: Sorry. I am sorry, but I do mean it.

Alain: From everything I have heard, it seems these rings grow stronger based on the depth of their bearers' bond.

Lex: All that, and you are wasting it on me? No wonder you have got the love life of a doorknob.

Alain: Listen to me, Lex.

Alain: You once said you were prepared to lay down your life if it meant guaranteeing my survival.

Alain: So this time, promise me that we will live on. Together.

Lex: I do not know what to say. Though I guess I am doing something right, huh?

Alain: I have always thought so. You simply never realized it yourself.

Lex: Aw, shucks.

Lex: And yeah, your way is a ton better. A lot less dying, too.

Alain: Then we will swear to it. Here.

Lex: Whoa. That do it?

Alain: So it would seem.

#### Lex and Alain - Final Battle

Galerius: End this, now.

Galerius: Hmph!

Galerius: Gah.

Alain: Mother!

Galerius: How does it feel, hm? Your dear mother, slain by your own hand.

Alain: What is happening to me?

Lex: Hey, get a hold of yourself!

Galerius: His strength surpasses even Ilenia's. The might of the unicorn runs deep in his veins.

Galerius: You would simply be volunteering your own as my next vessel.

Galerius: The ring is mine to command, and a futile demise is all that awaits you now.

Galerius: None can ever hope to halt my designs. Now, bow to your emperor.

Lex: Dammit.

Galerius: This day is won by Zenoira. You will make a fine Zenoiran vessel once it is over.

Galerius: The ring... why does it hold such vast energy?

Lex: You hear me in there, Alain? This guy has got nothing on you.

Galerius: It will take more than this to defeat me.

Lex: Alain!

Alain: Galerius. You saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire.

Alain: But as long as I live and breathe, you will never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

Galerius: How do you know of that?

Galerius: You will not!

Galerius: Their emperor shall never know defeat.

Baltro: Your Majesty.

Galerius: How goes the rite?

Galerius: Then these insects shall be more than enough. Grant me your strength, and we will stamp them out together.

Galerius: What do you think you are doing?

Baltro: If it was not clear, Your Majesty, the sigil seeks none other.

Galerius: Traitorous fool. Finally gone senile, hm?

Alain: Mother!

Ilenia: Ngh.

Lex: Hey, it is your mom. She is alive!

Alain: Speak to me, please.

Josef: I never imagined he possessed such frightful mastery over the bodies of others.

Ilenia: Alain. I cannot say how much time has passed since that day, but you have grown so much.

Ilenia: It seems I owe Josef a great deal for raising you in my absence.

Alain: Josef, see my mother somewhere safe.

Josef: And you, Your Highness?

Alain: We end this long-drawn war now.

Lex: Always knew it would come down to this. Ready when you are.

Josef: Come home, both of you.

Alain: Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call.

Alain: Your emperor is no more, and in his place stands a tyrannical fiend who craves nothing but absolute control.

Alain: Tell me, is this what you truly desire? To sacrifice your very essence in service of this daemon?

Alain: Souls of the departed, if you have any humanity left within you, lend me your aid.

Alain: These souls are not a power one can wield, Baltro. They are human lives, human will in its purest form.

Alain: Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Lex and Alain - Ending

Lex: I guess what I am trying to say is, we have got a good thing going here.

Lex: So I hope you are ready to put up with me for the rest of forever.

Lex: I am always a shout away if you ever want to spar, though.

#### Lex and Alain - Bread

Lex: Got some bread for you, Alain. Fresh out of the oven.

Alain: Do you mean to say you're the one who made it?

Lex: Sure do.

Alain: Then forgive me, Lex, but I can't eat this.

Lex: Why the hell not?

Alain: Do you remember the last time you baked us "bread"? It was closer to biting into a rock than any sort of actual food.

Lex: Oh, c'mon. That was ages ago. Here, I'll tear off half for you.

Alain: I have to say, this is incredible.

Lex: See? I'm thinking I might even start a bakery once we're done with all this war stuff.

Chloe: Something's wrong with this bread you made, Lex. It's hard as stone!

Lex: That's 'cause you're not eating it right. It's a northern specialty, meant to go with a nice, hot bowl of soup.

Chloe: Well, then maybe you should remember to tell people next time. I'm lucky I still have all my teeth after that.

Alain: Does such a dish truly exist?

Lex: Not sure why, though. I was using the same dough and everything.

Alain: Ah... perhaps you should hold off on that bakery for now, Lex.

### Lhinalagos

#### Lhinalagos Joins the Liberation Army

**Lhinalagos:** Even our final attempt ends in failure.

**Elheim Soldier:** Lhinalagos, sir! Ter Rosalinde approaches with an envoy of soldiers.

**Lhinalagos:** By the stars. My lady!

**Yahna:** It's been a while, Lhin.

**Lhinalagos:** My lady.

**Rosalinde:** I would not dare pass up willing reinforcements, but the state of affairs remains dire. We must withdraw.

**Lhinalagos:** The enemy is but a tail away.

**Alain:** Nothing is decided until the battle is over. We have come to aid your resistance at Rosalinde's request.

**Lhinalagos:** And you are?

**Alain:** Alain, leader of the Liberation Army.

**Lhinalagos:** Lhinalagos, of said resistance.

**Rosalinde:** Firm as your voice may ring, our defeat is unavoidable. Few able soldiers remain in this hold, and fewer still are willing to fight.

**Alain:** My army will push forth to the enemy stronghold. All I ask of you is to guard our rear.

**Lhinalagos:** I am willing to overlook your confidence. Even if we fall in the process, our arrows will find peace in Zenoiran necks, I assure you of that.

**Lhinalagos:** I must say, I have heard tell of the Liberation Army's ferocity, but your warriors are even more skilled than the rumors claim.

**Alain:** We are glad to have arrived in time.

**Lhinalagos:** Your kindness is touching, truly. As you can well see, that battle was a grave one indeed. Most of our ranks lie decimated, while those who lived will never again stand among the squadron on the front lines.

**Lhinalagos:** The whispers of the trees say the enemy is prioritizing raw manpower over any kind of quality or skill. As things stand, I can offer no peace to the countless lives that have fallen before the steel of these oppressors.

**Lhinalagos:** Instead, I will carry their spirits with me until the day I have finally purged Zenoira from our home. I would like to do so by your side.

**Alain:** Then join us, Lhinalagos.

**Lhinalagos:** It is a debt I shall repay with my life. Now come, let us topple Zenoira's grasp on this land together.

#### Lhinalagos and Alain - Strategy

**Alain:** Is everything all right, Lhinalagos? You seem upset.

**Lhinalagos:** Ah, it is you. It was a welcome stroke of luck, yet I am well aware that such fortune would have little chance of striking again.

**Lhinalagos:** Hence, I was reflecting on that horrible day, hoping to grasp how best to claim victory absent outside assistance. There is much to consider if I hope to be adequately prepared for our next battle.

**Alain:** You have some strength of heart, to be thinking of this while the pain is surely still fresh in your mind.

**Lhinalagos:** All that remains now is the burning desire to avenge my fallen allies.

**Alain:** Might I help you in that pursuit?

**Lhinalagos:** That is more than I could possibly ask of you.

**Alain:** I, too, wish to avoid the needless loss of life as much as possible. We can exchange any further ideas over its abundance of old charts and maps.

**Lhinalagos:** Very well. I would not deny the help of a skilled commander such as you. Lead the way, my prince.

**Lhinalagos:** Hm. He may not have the benefit of my boundless years, but he is quite a dependable young man.

#### Ring of the Maiden

**Lhinalagos:** The wind carries word of you, Sir Alain. To what do I owe the honor?

**Alain:** I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

**Lhinalagos:** That ring has been passed down through the Turenos line for generations.

**Alain:** Indeed. It is only fitting for the one I trust most.

**Lhinalagos:** Do you recall the day we met? I was in the heat of a fierce battle we seemed destined to lose. I was fully prepared to greet the Divine that day, and I surely would have had you not come to my rescue.

**Lhinalagos:** My reunion with Ter Eltolinde would have fallen painfully short. That is not a debt I will ever manage to repay, not even granted a prolonged elven lifespan.

**Lhinalagos:** Hence, should you consider me the object of your fancy, I must unquestionably consent.

**Alain:** Thank you, Lhin, if you will let me call you that.

**Lhinalagos:** I would. I swear to you, Alain, I shall give everything I am in restoring this world to its natural order.

**Lhinalagos:** All that remains now is to march onward to a righteous conclusion. The night may grow darker yet, but our resolve shall light the way, arm in gauntlet-clad arm.

#### Final Battle

**Lhinalagos:** Alain!

**Galerius:** The ring is mine to command. Now, bow to your emperor!

**Lhinalagos:** Even now, you struggle desperately against the overwhelming forces of evil.

**Alain:** I will not yield.

**Lhinalagos:** Alain!

**Alain:** Mother!

**Lhinalagos:** It is all right. Her condition is stable.

**Alain:** We end this long-drawn war now.

**Lhinalagos:** You are nothing more than human flesh. An aberration I shall cleanse from this world.

**Alain:** Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call. Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Ending

**Lhinalagos:** Yet with you at my side, victory felt all but fated in even the most perilous of circumstances. I am merely proud to stand beside you as a loyal friend. Thank you, my king, for everything.

**Lhinalagos:** Would you care to train together once we have returned to Elheim, Ithilion?

**Ithilion:** If you want, but I cannot promise I will not hurt you.

**Ithilion:** From the moment we left Elheim, each new landscape was more beautiful than the last. Though I will admit, few vistas could ever match the spectacle of Gran Corrine. And I would never have seen any of it without you, Alain.

**Ithilion:** Ter Rosalinde told me to simply enjoy myself for the day, but how am I to do that, exactly?

**Lhinalagos:** After all, it would be quite the shame for us to come all this way only to stand outside the gates.

**Ithilion:** I would like that, yes. It has been far too long since we last had the chance to relax like this.

### Liza

#### Liza and Alain - Life in the Desert

**Alain:** Liza, may I ask you about life in the desert?

**Liza:** You sure about that? No tellin' what happens when you go pokin' around where you're not welcome.

**Alain:** Just as Aubin has always described you.

**Liza:** Grr. I'm gonna make that bastard pay for that.

**Alain:** I understand the danger. Even so, learning more of your homeland is one step toward strengthening Cornia's bond with your nation.

**Liza:** You've got some weird ideas in that head of yours, Prince. But if you really wanna learn, I'll tell you. I've got stories a guy like you couldn't even dream of.

**Alain:** Then I look forward to hearing them.

#### Liza and Alain - More Stories

**Alain:** I had not grasped how different life in the desert could be.

**Liza:** Told you. It ain't a place people understand from a few pretty stories.

**Alain:** Gloucester had spoken of it before, though mostly to complain about the hardships.

**Liza:** That sounds like him.

**Alain:** I would rather hear more from you as well.

**Liza:** Fine. But next time, you gotta pay.

**Alain:** Then I will bring a worthy gift.

**Liza:** Heh. Guess I'll hold you to that.

#### Liza and Alain - Ribbons

**Alain:** Liza, today I would like to ask about you rather than the desert.

**Liza:** About me? People are gonna talk if they see a prince chattin' with some random girl from nowhere.

**Alain:** That concern is unnecessary. I think I understand why Aubin and Magellan are so close to you.

**Liza:** Don't go sayin' weird stuff like that.

**Alain:** I also brought you something.

**Liza:** Ribbons? You think these'd look good on me?

**Alain:** I cannot say for certain, but I am glad you find them cute.

**Liza:** Huh. Guess I can try 'em on.

#### Liza and Alain - Wearing the Gift

**Alain:** You are wearing the ribbons.

**Liza:** Had to take the other ones off to clean 'em. That's all.

**Alain:** Magellan said you might not like them.

**Liza:** He said what?

**Alain:** Which makes me all the more pleased to know how wonderful you look in them.

**Liza:** Don't you dare tell Magellan or Aubin I said anything about this.

**Alain:** Of course.

**Liza:** It's kinda nice, too.

#### Ring of the Maiden

**Liza:** What's the big idea askin' me here? Guy like you's probably got a hundred better choices.

**Alain:** Liza, I want you to have this ring.

**Liza:** You should really try bein' more careful with stuff like this. Never know whose feelings you might end up hurtin'.

**Alain:** I am serious.

**Liza:** Funny joke.

**Alain:** It is no joke. I want you beside me.

**Liza:** I'm loud, I'm rude, and I'm such a desert kid I got sand runnin' through my veins. You can't possibly want my sqvalor dirtyin' the crown.

**Alain:** Anyone who disparages your demeanor will answer to me. I cannot imagine my life without you in it, and I promise to make our union as perfect as you imagine it ought to be.

**Liza:** I guess I could be convinced, if you're that set on it.

**Alain:** Fairer words have never crossed my ears.

**Liza:** Don't make me regret this, Alain.

**Alain:** I will not. Those people are your family, Liza, and they will always have my protection.

**Liza:** Then I guess you've got mine, too.

#### Final Battle

**Liza:** Alain!

**Galerius:** The Unicorn's power belongs to me.

**Liza:** Dammit. What...

**Alain:** I will not fall.

**Liza:** It's him. Not a doubt in my mind. Hey, Alain! Remember what you told me back at the altar? How you couldn't imagine life without me in it?

**Alain:** I remember.

**Liza:** Then get back here and prove it!

**Alain:** Mother!

**Liza:** She's breathin' just fine, Alain. Don't worry.

**Alain:** Thank you.

**Liza:** This guy's gonna pay for what he did to my people. To all of us.

**Alain:** Then we finish this together.

#### Ending

**Liza:** I appreciate you worryin', Alain. Really. Not that I mind the attention.

**Magellan:** Headin' back to the desert, Liza?

**Liza:** Are you?

**Magellan:** Might track some people down. Fix up a town or two.

**Liza:** I'm comin', too.

**Magellan:** What about the Scorpions?

**Liza:** Aubin'll take care of 'em for us.

**Aubin:** Guess I wouldn't mind doin' a favor.

**Liza:** Things won't go back to normal overnight. But we're gonna keep pushin' forward, heads held high. Just like you did.

**Magellan:** Every day ridin' with you was better than the last. Hope I didn't hold ya back too much.

**Aubin:** War's over, but we've still got tons left to do.

**Magellan:** Me and Aubin are in it for the long haul.

**Aubin:** Just lemme know when you got some downtime, and we can sail the open seas, you and me.

**Alain:** I will. Until then, I know the desert is in good hands.

### Magellan

#### Magellan and Alain - A Debt Repaid

**Magellan:** Don't tell me ya forgot about the coin ya lent me.

**Alain:** I have not. But I did not expect you to bring it up now.

**Magellan:** Figured I oughta say somethin'. Back then, Galerius and that old bag o' bones had me under their spell. Before I knew it, his damn magick had me swingin' my axe for Zenoira.

**Alain:** Baltro's sorcery has done that to far too many.

**Magellan:** Yeah. If you hadn't stepped in, I might still be stuck that way. Looks like I owe ya one.

**Alain:** Then help me finish what we started.

**Magellan:** Heh. Mind fillin' me in on the master plan, boss?

#### Magellan and Alain - Morning Air

**Magellan:** Mornin', Alain! You're up early.

**Alain:** Indeed I am. And wide awake now, thanks to your resounding greeting.

**Magellan:** Back home, wakin' up around this time means sand in your teeth and freezing air in your lungs. Didn't think a morning could feel this nice when you ain't fightin' the world around ya.

**Alain:** Few places are as harsh as the desert. I am impressed that an unfamiliar climate has not affected you.

**Magellan:** Folks from my homeland are tough. Proud, too. We don't much like askin' for help, even when we need it.

**Alain:** Gloucester served as an intermediary for Drakenhold, did he not?

**Magellan:** He did. And then Zenoira came along and ruined the whole damn thing. But me and you are gonna drive those bastards out of Fevrith and get our desert back for good.

**Alain:** I will do all I can to see that happen.

**Magellan:** Good. That's what I like to hear.

#### Ring of the Maiden

**Magellan:** Huh. Never seen somewhere like this before. Place like this would've been buried by sand years ago back home.

**Alain:** Magellan, there is something I wish to give you.

**Magellan:** A ring? What's it mean?

**Alain:** It is proof that I trust you above all others. I want you by my side in the final battle.

**Magellan:** Heh. If you hadn't come along, I might've been stuck as Zenoira's puppet for the rest of my damn life. But here I am, still standin'. Livin'. And it's all thanks to you.

**Alain:** You have stood with me since then. I can think of no one better.

**Magellan:** Yep. And that's exactly why I'll have your back. More than anyone else. We got a world to save, don't we?

**Alain:** We do.

**Magellan:** Then let's quit standin' around and get to it.

#### Final Battle

**Magellan:** Alain!

**Galerius:** What good shall your resistance do? The power of the Unicorn is mine.

**Magellan:** Guy's strong as a damn ox!

**Alain:** I will not yield. Not here.

**Magellan:** Alain!

**Alain:** Mother!

**Magellan:** She's okay, far as I can tell.

**Alain:** Thank you.

**Magellan:** Time to put this maniac away for good.

**Baltro:** You would still defy me?

**Magellan:** C'mon, Alain. There's no talkin' to guys like this.

**Alain:** Then we end it here.

#### Ending

**Magellan:** But no chance that was happenin' with you leadin' the charge.

**Alain:** It was not my strength alone that won the day.

**Magellan:** Sure, sure. still, a guy like you sittin' the throne, and this kingdom'll be just fine. Not a doubt in my mind.

**Liza:** Here you went and saved the world. Thanks for that, Alain.

**Alain:** Thank you both. I am glad we could see this through together.

### Mandrin

#### Mandrin and Alain - Grass

**Alain:** If I may, Mandrin. I saw you giving your food to a child in town earlier.

**Mandrin:** Oh yeah? And what of it?

**Alain:** I suppose I am merely wondering why. Will you not go hungry with less to eat?

**Mandrin:** Once in a while, I would get travelers stopping by to tear off some of their bread for me. If I ended up surviving past childhood, I was gonna do for other people what those travelers did for me.

**Alain:** Yet I cannot agree with it, not if it means you are going to hinder your own well-being.

**Mandrin:** Worst comes to worst, there is always the grass.

**Alain:** Then we feast together, if that is your answer. My meal can go to a child in town as well.

**Mandrin:** You have gotta be kidding me.

**Alain:** Yet 'tis only by knowing the bitter taste of grass myself that I can truly understand their pain.

**Mandrin:** Heh. Never thought I would hear words like that coming out of a prince's mouth. But I guess I did not think you would ask me to join your army, either. You are a pretty good guy, you know?

**Alain:** Thank you for saying so. In any case, which varieties of grass are safe to eat?

**Mandrin:** Well, there is one thing you wanna look out for...

#### Ring of the Maiden

**Mandrin:** Pretty place you got here. Why am I along for the ride?

**Alain:** Mandrin, I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

**Mandrin:** You mind repeating that?

**Alain:** I said I would like you to take this ring.

**Mandrin:** You feeling all right? Cause it seems to me you are a few horses short.

**Alain:** I am of perfectly sound mind, I promise you.

**Mandrin:** Life is a funny thing, huh? One day you are off robbin' a church, the next you are getting handed some fancy ring by a crown prince.

**Alain:** Hahah. I suppose it is quite amusing when you put it like that. I cannot picture success coming without that strength at my side, nor that kindness.

**Mandrin:** Betting you know I cannot turn down a friend in need, either. Giving all I got for someone is my whole deal.

**Mandrin:** And if that someone is gonna be king, maybe we can make a country where kids will not have to go to sleep dreaming for even the slightest scraps of food.

**Alain:** We will see it done, you and I, together. What kind of friend would I be if I were all talk and no action?

**Mandrin:** A crap one, but we both know that is not you. Now come on, let us have that ring.

**Alain:** It would be my pleasure.

**Mandrin:** Right, then. Time to roll up my sleeves and get to work. Oh, and thanks for this, Alain.

#### Final Battle

**Mandrin:** Alain!

**Galerius:** The ring is mine to command. Now, bow to your emperor!

**Mandrin:** Dammit.

**Mandrin:** I will keep fighting for you, no matter what hell comes our way!

**Alain:** Mandrin!

**Alain:** Galerius, you saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire. But as long as I live and breathe, you will never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

**Alain:** Mother!

**Mandrin:** She is banged up pretty bad. We gotta help her, fast.

**Alain:** We end this long-drawn war now.

**Mandrin:** With you through it all, boss. Let us bury this bastard.

**Mandrin:** You ever get tired of hearing drivel? Well, do not worry. We are up for shutting it down.

**Alain:** Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call. Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Ending

**Mandrin:** Me, though? I will never forget it. So do not go breaking that oath now. We have still got lots of work to do, yeah, friend?

**Mandrin:** Never seen you smile that big, Gammel. You gonna tell me what it is for, or what?

**Gammel:** Ain't it obvious? I'm just real excited about the boss here gettin' crowned king.

**Mandrin:** Now tell me the truth or I'll smack it outta you.

### Melisandre

#### Melisandre Recruited

Josef: What shall be done with her, my prince?

Alain: Come, Melisandre. You belong with me.

Melisandre: Was that a proposal?

Alain: Perhaps I misspoke. I mean that you belong with us. The Liberation, that is. We have great need of fighters of your distinction.

Melisandre: Oh. Well, I suppose it's still a tempting offer.

Colm: You mean to accept, milady? But their hopes of success are nigh nonexistent.

Melisandre: And now that we've failed him, he's bound to complete the trifecta with our heads on the chopping block.

Colm: A fair point. We'd more than likely face the same fate were we to decline the Liberation's offer besides.

Colm: In truth, no odds are too small when they're the sole chance to preserve your noble lineage.

Melisandre: Speaking of that lineage, just imagine:

Melisandre: Cornia's illustrious House Meillet, allied with the rebels who seek to reclaim her status. Why, we'd be a prized feather in their cap.

Melisandre: Isn't that right, Alain?

Alain: I wouldn't dare disagree. Our union would be a significant one indeed.

Melisandre: Then it's settled.

Melisandre: Know that that's why I'm joining, above anything else.

Alain: Thank you, Melisandre.

Melisandre: That's not all I want, though. Once you claim the throne, I'll be expecting a place at your side for real.

Alain: Sorry?

Melisandre: Oh, don't worry. I'm not asking to be queen. Just one of the few dozen consorts every king calls upon.

Alain: Fascinating, yes. Let's discuss it another time, shall we?

#### Melisandre and Alain - An Enthusiastic Challenge

Melisandre: Well, look who it is.

Melisandre: Though it didn't last especially long. Not with the way he charged toward me, absent even a hint of fear in his eyes.

Alain: Melisandre? Is that you?

Melisandre: Oh! Alain...

Melisandre: I wasn't watching you, if that's what you were wondering.

Alain: Oh? I'm surprised you didn't call out to me, were that the case.

Melisandre: Ah, what a luxuriant mane. And how enchanting his gaze.

Alain: Must you stand so close, Melisandre? You're beginning to terrify me.

Melisandre: Ah, I'm sorry. I should know better than to stare.

Melisandre: By the by, how would you feel about a little sparring match?

Alain: Now? I don't see why not.

Melisandre: I'm glad to hear it. And this way, I can look at you all I want.

Melisandre: Now let's begin.

Alain: You seem rather motivated by this, Melisandre, but know that I'll not hold myself back either.

Melisandre: Nor would I want you to.

Melisandre: After all, none can pique my excitement quite like you can.

#### Melisandre and Alain - Morning Training

Melisandre: That should be good for today.

Melisandre: With just enough time to head back to my tent before breakfast as well.

Melisandre: Alain? How long have you been standing there?

Alain: Only a moment, in truth. I'm surprised you didn't notice me sooner, Melisandre.

Melisandre: Urgh. You're not supposed to see me like this. My hair is a complete mess from all my training.

Alain: In that moment, Melisandre, I found myself utterly captivated by your beauty.

Alain: A sight made all the more magical by the amber hues of the morning sun glistening on the fresh-laid snow.

Alain: 'Tis no surprise you felt confident enough to announce yourself at our camp entirely alone.

Melisandre: I didn't think you would have noticed all that.

Alain: How could I not? With those swords in hand, there could truthfully be none more talented than you.

Alain: Melisandre? Forgive me. I didn't mean to offend.

Melisandre: I studied every day and every night in hopes of attaining that goal, of proving myself worthy of leading House Meillet.

Melisandre: It would have been, if I wasn't so naturally gifted. To me, schooling was just another chore like any other.

Melisandre: It was then and only then that I wanted to be the best at something. Not for my house, but for myself.

Melisandre: And to hear you say that I actually am is the highest honor you could possibly give me.

Alain: Then I'm glad I decided to speak the truth.

Alain: A kiss on the cheek? But why did you...

Melisandre: Just my way of saying thank you, and to remind you to do your best too.

Alain: How am I even meant to respond to that?

#### Melisandre and Alain - Ring of the Maiden

Alain: I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

Melisandre: You mean... you'll take me as your bride?

Melisandre: This barely feels real. I'm dreaming, am I?

Alain: I assure you, you're wide awake.

Melisandre: Oh!

Melisandre: You were hardly subtle in your approach when we first met. Now allow me to return the favor.

Alain: Your hand, please.

Alain: And with that, our oath is sworn.

Melisandre: Oh, Alain...

Melisandre: And I know what I said before, but don't go taking any wives but me. Or consorts.

Alain: I promise. You're the only one I could ever need.

#### Melisandre and Alain - Final Battle

Alain: Galerius, Emperor of Zenoira.

Galerius: Heheh. If you hope to speak, you'll find me no willing participant. I have no words for you.

Galerius: End this, now.

Galerius: Hmph.

Galerius: Gah.

Alain: Mother!

Galerius: How does it feel, hm? Your dear mother, slain by your own hand?

Alain: What is happening to me?

Melisandre: Alain?

Galerius: What a poor fool he was, doomed to the same fate as the pitiful queen before him.

Galerius: His strength surpasses even Ilenia's. The might of the unicorn runs deep in his veins.

Galerius: The ring is mine to command, and a futile demise is all that awaits you now.

Galerius: None can ever hope to halt my designs. Bow to your emperor.

Galerius: This day is won.

Galerius: You will make a fine Zenoiran vessel once it is over.

Galerius: Enough. Can't you see it's over?

Galerius: The ring...

Galerius: But why does it hold such vast energy?

Melisandre: It's you, isn't it? I know you're still in there.

Melisandre: What use are unicorns or maidens if I don't have you?

Galerius: It will take more than this to defeat me.

Melisandre: Alain!

Alain: Galerius. You saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire.

Alain: But as long as I live and breathe, you'll never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

Galerius: How do you know of that?

Galerius: You will not!

Galerius: Their emperor shall never know defeat.

Baltro: Your Majesty.

Galerius: How goes the rite?

Galerius: Then these insects shall be more than enough. Grant me your strength, and we'll stamp them out together.

Galerius: What do you think you're doing?

Baltro: If it wasn't clear, Your Majesty, the sigil seeks none other.

Galerius: Traitorous fool. Finally gone senile, hm?

Alain: Mother!

Ilenia: Ngh.

Melisandre: It's all right, Alain. She's breathing, and steadily at that.

Alain: Speak to me, please.

Josef: I never imagined he possessed such frightful mastery over the bodies of others.

Ilenia: Alain. I can't say how much time has passed since that day, but you've grown so much.

Ilenia: If only I could have been there to witness it.

Alain: Josef, see my mother somewhere safe.

Josef: And you, Your Highness?

Alain: We end this long-drawn war now.

Melisandre: Don't worry. We'll see it through to the very last.

Baltro: What evil should I reanimate next? A monster capable of crushing you beneath its heel, perhaps.

Melisandre: You're the monster, and you'll pay for toying with people's lives.

Alain: Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call.

Alain: Your emperor is no more, and in his place stands a tyrannical fiend who craves nothing but absolute control.

Alain: Tell me, is this what you truly desire? To sacrifice your very essence in service of this daemon?

Alain: Souls of the departed, if you have any humanity left within you, lend me your aid.

Alain: These souls are not a power one can wield, Baltro. They are human lives, human will in its purest form.

Alain: Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Melisandre and Alain - Ending

Colm: Of course, House Meillet was my sole priority when first we met.

Colm: But having seen what a fine man you are, and what a fine ruler you've become, I'm confident my lady made the right choice in joining you.

Colm: She always knew you bore the strength of will to succeed in your aims.

Colm: Come, my lady. House Meillet awaits.

Melisandre: I've already told you, Colm. I'm not going anywhere until I have a private audience with Alain himself.

Colm: Your noble house, on the other hand, will suffer greatly absent the presence of its leader.

Melisandre: Please, Colm. You can tell the others it was another of my selfish whims if you must.

Colm: I don't much enjoy being made an accomplice in your passions, but very well.

Colm: Now what excuse shall I give the servants for our tardiness?

Melisandre: Or maybe we can just enjoy being engaged for now, if that's what you'd prefer.

Melisandre: I don't mind either way.

Melisandre: And as long as our love continues to blossom, I'm sure we'll be the happiest couple Fevrith has ever seen.

Melisandre: I wish I could see him as a warrior again, blade in hand just one more time.

Colm: My lady, please. There shall be no need for such displays in this blossoming age of peace.

Colm: After all, who would be foolish enough to point their sword at the king himself?

Melisandre: I guess you're right, but now I wish I had offered to train with him while I still had the chance.

### Miriam

#### Miriam and Alain - Distinction

Miriam: Might I request an audience for a moment, Your Highness?

Alain: But of course. What is it, Miriam?

Miriam: I was merely wondering how you regard my work compared to that of the rest of our army.

Alain: 'Tis a surprising level of incertitude coming from you.

Alain: Yet you needn't assess yourself by the feats of others. Everyone has their own natural strengths, and you are no different.

Alain: Is there a reason you seek such an answer?

Miriam: 'Tis the same conclusion I seek myself as well.

Miriam: I received a letter from my father this morning, stating the importance of distinguishing my deeds from those of my peers.

Miriam: I suppose he's purely fixated on what plaudit our house shall receive upon the end of this war.

Alain: Recognition from the crown would prove a boon to any noble family, yes.

Miriam: But it is also a necessary one, should we ever wish to bring peace to these afflicted lands.

Alain: And to my eye, you've already achieved the very distinction your father wishes for.

Miriam: Thank you for the generous words, Your Highness.

#### Miriam and Alain - A Visible Smile

Alain: Have you received some manner of good news, Miriam?

Miriam: Your Highness. Nothing in particular, no. Why do you ask?

Alain: Have you not noticed? It seems you have been smiling more often lately.

Miriam: While I have not consciously meant to do so, I have often hidden who I truly am.

Miriam: Rather than confront those fears, I chose to flee from them. To feign the austerity I felt was necessary.

Miriam: I wish to change that because of you.

Alain: Hence the smile from earlier. You were simply expressing the joy you have found in such a life.

Miriam: I am certain it will only grow easier in the days and months to come.

Alain: Then I look forward to seeing what other new expressions await me when it does.

Miriam: You do? I had not thought my mood was so easy to read.

Alain: It is not, actually. I believe I only noticed because of how often I find my gaze fixed upon you.

Miriam: Your Highness.

Alain: Is there a problem, Miriam?

Miriam: Not at all. Pray think nothing of it.

Miriam: Do you not grasp how embarrassing this is, to be told my appearance is the object of your attention?

Alain: Forgive me. I did not intend to startle you.

Miriam: It is all right. I fully plan to carry that joy for all to see.

#### Miriam and Alain - Ring of the Maiden

Miriam: How can I be of assistance, Highness?

Alain: I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

Miriam: Oh, I... Are you certain I'm deserving of such an honor?

Alain: I am. I'd see it passed to none but you.

Miriam: I cannot accept.

Alain: And might I ask why?

Miriam: Because, Your Highness, you've only made this request to appease my father.

Alain: I would never. This is a matter of the heart, not a political transaction.

Miriam: You say that, and yet, I struggle to see it any other way.

Miriam: But someday I shall carve a new path. One that I and only I walk.

Miriam: So forgive me, Your Highness. I have no choice but to refuse for now.

Alain: Miriam, wait! I asked you here because the ring belongs to you.

Alain: Not your father, and certainly not anyone else. I mean that with every ounce of my being.

Alain: And if I may, you already own your own sun, a star that burns not with obligation but immense strength.

Alain: Now, please. Tell me how you truly feel.

Miriam: Alain...

Miriam: I trust you speak those words with the purest intentions, and thank you for enouncing them.

Miriam: In sooth, when I heard you had summoned me here, well...

Miriam: My heart nearly burst forth from my chest.

Miriam: I want nothing more than to feel that same feeling every day of my life. To stand beside you as your loving betrothed.

Miriam: And I promise, I'll never hide myself from you again.

Miriam: I want you to see me.

Alain: Thank you, Miriam. Such bold declarations are not easy to make, yet you've shown great courage in doing so.

Miriam: I must be wearing the most untoward smile right now.

Miriam: But it's so very undignified, don't you think?

Miriam: I'll have you not laugh at my struggles, thank you.

#### Miriam and Alain - Final Battle

Galerius: End this, now.

Galerius: Hmph.

Galerius: Gah.

Alain: Mother!

Galerius: How does it feel, hm? Your dear mother, slain by your own hand?

Alain: What is happening to me?

Miriam: Your Highness!

Galerius: What a poor fool he was, doomed to the same fate as the pitiful queen before him.

Galerius: His strength surpasses even Ilenia's. The might of the unicorn runs deep in his veins.

Galerius: You'd simply be volunteering your own as my next vessel.

Galerius: The ring is mine to command, and a futile demise is all that awaits you now.

Galerius: None can ever hope to halt my designs. Bow to your emperor.

Miriam: No. 'Tis only a true daemon that strikes a man who has already lowered his blade.

Galerius: This day is won.

Galerius: You will make a fine Zenoiran vessel once it is over.

Galerius: Enough. Can't you see it's over?

Galerius: The ring...

Galerius: But why does it hold such vast energy?

Miriam: Only one man could be the cause.

Miriam: 'Tis you, Alain. The redeemer of all Fevrith and the shores beyond.

Galerius: It will take more than this to defeat me.

Miriam: Alain! It's truly you.

Alain: Galerius. You saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire.

Alain: But as long as I live and breathe, you'll never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

Galerius: How do you know of that?

Galerius: You will not!

Galerius: Their emperor shall never know defeat.

Baltro: Your Majesty.

Galerius: How goes the rite?

Galerius: Then these insects shall be more than enough. Grant me your strength, and we'll stamp them out together.

Baltro: If it wasn't clear, Your Majesty, the sigil seeks none other.

Galerius: Traitorous fool. Finally gone senile, hm?

Alain: Mother!

Ilenia: Ngh.

Miriam: What fortune... She appears unharmed.

Alain: Speak to me, please.

Ilenia: Alain. I can't say how much time has passed since that day, but you've grown so much.

Ilenia: If only I could have been there to witness it.

Ilenia: It seems I owe Josef a great deal for raising you in my absence.

Alain: Josef, see my mother somewhere safe.

Josef: And you, Your Highness?

Alain: We end this long-drawn war now.

Josef: Come home, both of you.

Baltro: What evil should I reanimate next? A monster capable of crushing you beneath its heel, perhaps.

Miriam: They are not your pawns to gamble with.

Alain: Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call.

Alain: Your emperor is no more, and in his place stands a tyrannical fiend who craves nothing but absolute control.

Alain: Tell me, is this what you truly desire? To sacrifice your very essence in service of this daemon?

Alain: Souls of the departed, if you have any humanity left within you, lend me your aid.

Alain: These souls are not a power one can wield, Baltro. They are human lives, human will in its purest form.

Alain: Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Miriam and Alain - Ending

Miriam: Yet had I refused the ring, despite your warm insistence, I would have regretted it for all of my days.

Miriam: I'm certain of that.

Miriam: Yet I know you'll always be there to catch me, my love.

Miriam: Queen Ilenia shall be safe 'neath my watchful eye. I assure you of that.

Fran: They all couldn't wait to see you, even before the ceremony started.

Fran: Myself included, of course.

Fran: But I'll still be working in the palace with the Knights of the Rose, so we'll have chances for conversation whenever we want.

Fran: Maybe focus your attention on those who traveled from abroad instead.

Fran: I trust you're not getting into any trouble over there, Kitra?

Kitra: I'm here to protect the queen, not bother her.

Fran: That's a relief. Sometimes I've wondered if you'll never grow up at all.

Kitra: Well, before the ceremony today... actually, just forget I ever said anything.

Fran: As if that's going to happen. Tell me what you've done this instant.

Kitra: Hey, not so loud! I'm dead meat if the queen finds out about this.

Kitra: You out here alone, Your Majesty?

Kitra: Though knowing you, I'm sure you'd smack 'em down without even lifting a finger.

Miriam: Kitra? How many times must I tell you to speak more formally when addressing His Majesty?

Kitra: Plus, the queen told me she didn't mind, so I kind of stopped trying. Sorry.

Miriam: You realize you're meant to conform to the wills of our masters, not impose your own upon them, yes?

#### Miriam and Alain - A Cold

Miriam: Is it a cold, perhaps, brought about by the harsh climes of Bastorias?

Alain: I am fine.

Miriam: So you do have a cold. I could recognize a sneeze like that anywhere.

Miriam: Surely the fluctuations in relative body heat are to blame. Come, I shall see you to bed at once.

Alain: Miriam, I do not think this requires such concern.

Miriam: It would seem you have caused quite the commotion of late.

Miriam: I fully expect an explanation once you have recovered from your ailments. We shall postpone this conversation until then.

### Monica

#### Monica First Encounter

Alain: What's going on there?

Renault: What shall we do, my prince?

Alain: We teach them that tormenting the innocent is not a hobby that comes without its price.

Monica: I am Monica, daughter of this territory's ruling house and commander of its army.

Monica: Pray forgive me for galloping past you, good swordsmen.

Alain: I would think a knight such as you more capable of ensuring the safety of your lands.

Monica: You would have me guard not only my towns and checkpoints, but the wilderness between them as well?

Monica: You clearly know little of governance, wanderer. 'Tis simply impossible when the rebel army could march upon us at any moment.

Alain: I suppose you have a point, yes.

Monica: And unfortunately, their ranks have proven quite elusive, causing us ceaseless headaches all the while.

Alain: That must be difficult.

Monica: In any case, who are you? 'Tis a rare sight to witness a man traveling with an attendant these days.

Alain: My name is... Alec.

Alain: And this man is not my attendant, but my friend.

Monica: Oh? I would never have surmised as much.

Hans: Forgive me for intruding upon your conversation.

Hans: A short while back, a compatriot of mine, a cleric by the name of Laika, was abducted by the leader of those bandits from before.

Hans: I set off in hopes of rescuing her. Well, you saw how they surrounded me.

Monica: Doubtless they'll seek to sell her off to a slave market.

Hans: Oh, heavens forbid. You must help her!

Monica: I fear I've not a single soldier I can spare for your cause.

Monica: Though perhaps Ser Alec here would be willing to aid you.

Monica: What do you say?

Alain: Have you any idea where these bandits might have taken her?

Hans: There were a good many of them, but I believe their leader is the one who has her.

Monica: Best of luck to you, Ser Alec.

Hans: Laika! Thank the Father you're all right.

Laika: I'm sorry to worry you, Hans.

Hans: Don't be. This wasn't your fault.

Hans: And you, Ser Alec. Words will forever fail to capture my gratitude for what you've done this day.

Laika: We'll never forget this, brave hero.

Alain: Please. Your continued safety is thanks enough.

Alain: Our role in this is concluded. I trust you'll see them to safety.

Monica: Whatever cur has claimed you're naught but a reclusive coward, they're dead wrong.

Monica: I suppose that's what I get for believing rumors. Forgive me, Prince Alain.

Alain: You must have me confused. I'm-

Monica: Champion of the rebel army, and lost son of Queen Ilenia. I'm well aware.

Monica: Why did you leave us to dispatch those rogues by ourselves?

Monica: Or do you greet all your acquaintances with such shameless detachment?

Alain: You know her, Clive?

Clive: In a manner of speaking, yes.

Clive: Beloved granddaughter to Cornia's own Marquis Nordheim.

Clive: And, though the affair is years since buried, she was my fiancee as well.

Alain: This is a great deal to grasp.

Monica: Ex-fiancee would be more accurate, Your Highness.

Monica: As for you, Clive, I've no doubt you're aware of the shadow your Liberation antics cast over my family.

Monica: Zenoira confiscated our territory. Stripped us of our title.

Monica: And what scant land we were seen fit to retain stood on the farthest fringes of the entire kingdom.

Clive: Monica, I'm sorry. I never meant for any of this.

Monica: In any case, our land now rests firmly in Zenoira's steeled fist, and I haven't the authority to let the Liberation cross it.

Monica: We all know the tale. Yesterday's fiancee becomes today's foe.

Monica: A story as tragic as it is trite. But I've made my peace with what must be done.

#### Monica Recruited

Monica's Soldier: They're still quartered in Saint le Riche, ma'am, but they'll be prepared to march at a moment's notice.

Monica: Then we resolve to face them head-on.

Monica: Whoever brings me the heads of these insurgents can name their reward.

Monica's Soldier: Yes, ma'am.

Matthias: You stare straight through me.

Monica: Hmph. Clive and this Liberation of his mean to threaten us into submission, and resist Zenoiran rule besides.

Matthias: And I suspect that fire in your belly burns brighter than you would have me believe.

Monica: Yet when Grandfather refused to bend the knee to Galerius, they forsook us as if we were common swine.

Monica: If one as proud and dignified as he could be dragged to such depths, I dare not imagine myself immune.

Monica: Far too many have suffered as it stands. I won't condemn still more to the slaughter.

Monica: Even if it means cutting Clive down myself.

Monica: In another time, another life, this could have all gone differently.

Monica: Now, come. Your blood will uphold the Nordheim name.

Clive: Let us see if you can uphold that boast.

Alain: We stand to gain nothing from this bloodshed, Lady Monica. I implore you, withdraw your soldiers.

Monica: Your breath is wasted on such words, Prince.

Monica: But if you want to hear the strength of our surrender, listen well.

Monica: It seems the rumors spoke true. Very well, I admit defeat.

Alain: We promise nothing. We come for peace, not blood.

Alain: Now, the rostrum is yours, Clive. Go on.

Clive: Marquis Nordheim is a benefactor to the Liberation.

Clive: In our fledgling days we had no backing to speak of, and naught to fill our coffers but dust.

Clive: Until, that is, your grandfather took it upon himself to fund our development.

Clive: By his words, he'd much sooner see his wealth invested in Cornia's future than stripped barren by its captors.

Clive: What remains of your noble house could never risk having its fealty questioned by its Zenoiran masters.

Clive: Hence the marquis sent us here. They will hear you fought valiantly and were left with no choice but to capitulate.

Alain: Then we mustn't do that love a disservice.

Alain: Not to mention our dire need of reinforcements. Come with us, Monica, and strike true your blade for the Liberation.

Monica: And please, keep our people safe.

Matthias: Well, I merely hope you find it within yourself to reconcile with Ser Clive.

Monica: I suppose we'll see.

#### Monica and Alain - Marquis Nordheim's Letter

Monica: Rgh...

Alain: That was a rather impressive sigh there, Monica. Is something the matter?

Monica: Yet I'll have you know, it's sometimes best to leave a woman to her misery.

Alain: Forgive me. I merely thought to offer my help, if you needed it.

Monica: I've received a letter from my grandfather.

Monica: One which details every last aspect of the very machinations Clive mentioned earlier.

Monica: He wanted to thank me, and to apologize as well.

Monica: But if he truly thinks a letter is enough to redress his failings, then he's dearly mistaken.

Alain: I can see your point, yes.

Monica: Despite his impulsiveness, my grandfather is surely well-intentioned at heart, if not a little too cunning for his own good.

Monica: As far as I can remember, the man has cared more for card games and horseback riding than inheritances or decorum.

Monica: In all honesty, it's a miracle the old fox has lived as long as he has.

Alain: I think I understand the reason for that sigh now, Monica. It was one of concern for your grandfather's safety.

Monica: Enough about the sigh already.

Monica: And I'd appreciate it if you kept this matter to yourself while you're at it.

#### Monica and Alain - Ring of the Maiden

Monica: Was there something you wished to discuss, my prince? This is quite a lovely spot for a chat.

Alain: I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

Monica: That's a bold declaration, there.

Alain: When we first locked swords, I saw in you a knight of firm convictions and truly immense skill.

Alain: With one such as you beside me, I'm certain we can bring Galerius to heel.

Monica: So that's how it is.

Monica: You desire my strength, yet care nothing for matters of my heart.

Alain: I only ask this of you as the one I trust most. The one I love.

Monica: Oh, but it is fun to watch you squirm.

Alain: Pray, do not tease me so.

Monica: If you insist. But allow me to return your sincerity in kind.

Monica: I could never refuse this offer, not after the next king so boldly professed his love.

Monica: As you know, my life has long been devoted to Cornia and her people.

Monica: And I would be honored to continue on that path of devotion as your beloved wife.

Alain: Thank you, Monica.

Monica: You know, I never realized just how cute this little ring would be.

Monica: I wonder how that ex-fiance of mine will react when he sees it.

#### Monica and Alain - Final Battle

Galerius: End this, now.

Galerius: Hmph.

Galerius: Gah.

Alain: Mother!

Galerius: How does it feel, hm? Your dear mother, slain by your own hand?

Alain: What is happening to me?

Monica: Alain!

Galerius: What a poor fool he was, doomed to the same fate as the pitiful queen before him.

Galerius: His strength surpasses even Ilenia's. The might of the unicorn runs deep in his veins.

Galerius: strike at this new body of mine, if you dare.

Galerius: You'd simply be volunteering your own as my next vessel.

Galerius: None can ever hope to halt my designs. Bow to your emperor.

Galerius: This day is won.

Galerius: You will make a fine Zenoiran vessel once it is over.

Galerius: The ring...

Galerius: But why does it hold such vast energy?

Monica: Listen to me, Alain. Should you give in now, Cornia would be lost to the flow of time, a forgotten land and a forgotten people.

Monica: Is that how you'll let this end?

Galerius: It will take more than this to defeat me.

Monica: Alain!

Alain: Galerius. You saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire.

Alain: But as long as I live and breathe, you'll never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

Galerius: How do you know of that?

Galerius: You will not!

Galerius: Their emperor shall never know defeat.

Baltro: Your Majesty.

Galerius: How goes the rite?

Galerius: Then these insects shall be more than enough. Grant me your strength, and we'll stamp them out together.

Galerius: What do you think you're doing?

Baltro: If it wasn't clear, Your Majesty, the sigil seeks none other.

Galerius: Traitorous fool. Finally gone senile, hm?

Alain: Mother!

Ilenia: Ngh.

Monica: By the Father's grace, she still breathes, Alain.

Alain: Speak to me, please.

Josef: I never imagined he possessed such frightful mastery over the bodies of others.

Ilenia: Alain. I can't say how much time has passed since that day, but you've grown so much.

Ilenia: If only I could have been there to witness it.

Alain: Josef, see my mother somewhere safe.

Josef: And you, Your Highness?

Alain: We end this long-drawn war now.

Monica: Our march could only ever reach one conclusion. Onward, to the closing act.

Josef: Come home, both of you.

Baltro: What evil should I reanimate next? A monster capable of crushing you beneath its heel, perhaps.

Monica: Wild ramblings of a man gone mad.

Alain: Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call.

Alain: Your emperor is no more, and in his place stands a tyrannical fiend who craves nothing but absolute control.

Alain: Tell me, is this what you truly desire? To sacrifice your very essence in service of this daemon?

Alain: Souls of the departed, if you have any humanity left within you, lend me your aid.

Alain: Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Monica and Alain - Ending

Monica: Thank you, Alain, for so swiftly expressing your endorsement of House Nordheim.

Monica: And I should thank you for again swearing the covenant with me.

Monica: I only ask that your reign support that endeavor, Alain.

Monica: It seems our time together has come to an end, Clive.

Clive: Indeed it does.

Clive: I wish to pay a visit to Marquis Nordheim, and would be most pleased if you were willing to perhaps accompany me.

Monica: If there's anything I can do to aid in those struggles, simply let me know.

Clive: I will. Thank you, Monica.

Clive: Ten long years have I clung to my spear, wishing that this moment would one day come to pass.

Clive: And now it has, thanks to you. I've nothing but the utmost gratitude, my king.

### Morard

#### Morard and Alain - Storybook King

**Morard:** Roaaar! Fear not, for the king of beasts is here to... Ahem.

**Alain:** I did not mean to interrupt.

**Morard:** Every so often, I act out the plot of a well-known storybook for the children back in Bastoritza. It has been a while since I have done so, given everything that has happened with the war.

**Alain:** I enjoyed it.

**Morard:** I am glad you enjoyed it, Alain. Well then, now is your chance. Here is the script I have been working off.

**Alain:** You would have me take part?

**Morard:** That is a good start, Alain. Now try that again with a little more energy.

#### Morard and Alain - Purpose

**Alain:** You lost your memories, and in doing so, your body as well.

**Morard:** As far as I can remember, yes. I expect I am the only human in all of Fevrith to have ever experienced such a thing.

**Alain:** Yet I have to imagine you have always borne this clarity of purpose, even as a human.

**Morard:** Purpose, huh? I am not sure that had anything to do with it. Deserting Zenoira was one thing, but I kept it from the very people I had come to think of as family. So do not talk to me about purpose, Alain. The only constant in my life is betrayal and deception.

**Alain:** 'Twas a staggering feat of bravery, Morard, and I will not let you convince yourself otherwise.

**Morard:** Hm. Yet in that moment, it was not a fear of death that gripped my heart. It was pride. Maybe everything really has turned out for the best.

#### Ring of the Maiden

**Morard:** Alain, what is all this?

**Alain:** Morard, I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

**Morard:** Someone like me does not deserve the honor.

**Alain:** That is where you are wrong, Morard. You have lived a life others could scarcely even imagine: a remorseful human transformed into the most massive of bestrals. Yet you never languished in the face of such great misfortune. You used it as fuel to propel you forth.

**Alain:** 'Tis a feat only a select few might ever achieve, if any at all.

**Morard:** I cannot say I ever thought of it that way. But while we are on the subject of feats, you are barely old enough to hold a sword, let alone lead an army, but here you are fixing to save the whole damned world. I have never seen anything like it.

**Morard:** Fine, then. If you are that desperate for my help, who am I to say no?

**Morard:** Have to admit, it is a real laugh knowing an old Zenoiran nobody will be the one bringing down the entire empire.

**Alain:** I suppose it goes to show life truly is full of surprises.

**Morard:** Says the man who just proposed to a lion. Either way, I have got even more to protect now. First Yunifi and now you. So let us get moving. We have a battle to win!

#### Final Battle

**Morard:** What is wrong, Alain?

**Galerius:** The ring is mine to command. Now, bow to your emperor!

**Morard:** I knew you were still in there. Well, what are you waiting for? Finish him off!

**Morard:** You did it, Alain!

**Alain:** Galerius, you saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire. But as long as I live and breathe, you will never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

**Alain:** Piteous ghost of an age long past, I shall grant your soul the freedom it desires.

**Morard:** Should have known it would not be easy.

**Alain:** Mother!

**Morard:** She is still alive!

**Alain:** Josef, see my mother somewhere safe. We end this long-drawn war, here and now.

**Morard:** That sigil must fall, no matter the cost.

**Yunifi:** So this is it, huh? We have come a long way from slinging stones back in Bastorias.

**Morard:** Indeed we have, but this battle will determine the fate of our home as well. It is now or never, Yunifi.

**Yunifi:** Then I am glad I have got you backing me up. Come on!

**Morard:** No. This world has seen enough devilry.

**Alain:** Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call. Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Ending

**Morard:** In a way, Alain, each and every one of them is your loyal subject now.

**Yunifi:** You okay there, Morard?

**Morard:** Hm? Ah, it certainly does not help that Cornia is so warm either.

**Yunifi:** Almost like we can finally just relax after all these years.

**Morard:** Right you are. As for now, I am looking forward to a good sleep once we get back to Bastorias.

**Yunifi:** But do not worry. I know you will be ready for anything that comes your way.

**Ramona:** I look forward to your reign with great anticipation, Alain. I have no doubt that the world shall be a better place with you as king.

**Ramona:** I must say, I cannot help but admire the sight of it.

**Yunifi:** Trust me, Ramona, we know. Everyone saw you studying the brickwork up on the parapets earlier.

**Ramona:** Did you, now? I was not aware my inclinations were that transparent. Though I find it rather embarrassing to have been caught in the act.

### Nina

#### Nina Recruited
