### Umerus

#### Umerus and Alain - Avoiding the Prince

**Umerus:** Hello, my prince.

**Alain:** Forgive me for asking this, but have you been avoiding me?

**Umerus:** I am not sure what you mean.

**Alain:** These past few days, you seemed to flee at the mere sight of me. What if I had hoped to speak with you?

**Umerus:** Something like my expulsion from the Liberation?

**Alain:** That, and Scarlett has missed you greatly in the years since she left Albion.

**Umerus:** She has? I am sorry, Alain. I will try to be a little less distant from now on.

**Alain:** Please, 'tis not a matter worth apologizing over.

**Umerus:** Maybe not, but I will atone for my lapse in judgment, even if laying down my life is the only way to do so.

**Alain:** Do remember to be kind to yourself as well, Umerus.

**Umerus:** I will try, my prince.

#### Umerus and Alain - The Flower

**Alain:** I thought perhaps it might be a variety you have never encountered before.

**Umerus:** It only grows in the deepest forests, and wilts just seven days after it first blooms. As beautiful a life as it is fleeting. These delicate white petals are simply breathtaking. Why have you given this to me?

**Alain:** Because you like flowers, of course.

**Umerus:** That is not what I mean.

**Alain:** Ah. You speak of my intention. I suppose I thought it might convince you to drop your guard around me.

**Umerus:** Even after I fled at the very sight of you. I just hope you can forgive me for what I have done.

**Alain:** There is no need for that, Umerus. At least, as long as you do not start avoiding me again.

**Umerus:** Thank you for the flower, Alain. I love it.

#### Ring of the Maiden

**Umerus:** Why have you summoned me here?

**Alain:** Umerus, I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

**Umerus:** I do not deserve such an honor. Or did you forget what I have done? How I turned my blade against you?

**Alain:** I remember. But I have also observed you in the days since, seen how tirelessly you have worked to atone for your past transgressions. I would say you have more than done so. Such single-minded resolve speaks to the profound purity of your heart.

**Alain:** In any case, it is not as though you betrayed us out of malice or greed. So please, Umerus, let this bitter dance of self-reproach end here and now. From the moment you accept this ring, your sins will be no more. You shall stand among us as an equal.

**Umerus:** You are kind, Alain. Far too kind. But I do like that about you. I accept your offer. I promise to never leave your side from this day forward, neither in battle nor in this life.

**Umerus:** Thank you, Alain. My heart is forever yours.

#### Final Battle

**Umerus:** Alain!

**Galerius:** The ring is mine to command. Now, bow to your emperor!

**Umerus:** It is you. You are still fighting, struggling to break free against all odds. Well, I refuse to let you fight alone, just like we promised. I am right here, Alain, and I will never leave your side.

**Alain:** Umerus!

**Alain:** Galerius, you saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire. But as long as I live and breathe, you will never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

**Alain:** Mother!

**Alain:** We end this long-drawn war now.

**Umerus:** All the suffering he has caused our lands will finally be repaid. This warped man will never see victory.

**Alain:** Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call. Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Ending

**Umerus:** When those flowers finally bloom, Alain, they will do so for you alone. Made all the more beautiful when viewed from the castle, I hope.

**Galadmir:** That has been evident since the moment that crown was placed on your head. I may have tested you once, but you have more than proven yourself worthy of my trust. Our entire kingdom will have nothing but praise for the greatest hero Fevrith has ever known.

### Virginia

#### Virginia and Alain - Rumors

Virginia: Impudent cretins. You'll pay for insulting him like that.

Alain: What's happening here?

Leah: It's the princess, ser. You have to stop her.

Alain: What do you think you're doing, Virginia?

Virginia: As for you, you don't want to know what'll happen if I catch you spreading such slander again.

Alain: What was it they were saying, exactly?

Virginia: They claimed you had murdered Queen Ilenia.

Alain: They what?

Virginia: All part of some baseless rumor that you and Galerius have been working together since the day Zenoira rose to power.

Virginia: You're the one who seeks to slay the monster, not enable his reign.

Alain: I understand now.

Alain: Yet I can't begrudge them that. 'Tis only natural to doubt a man who appears after ten years, claiming himself to be a long-deceased prince.

Alain: Action alone shall prove those rumors false now.

Virginia: The bastards can't even imagine the pain you've been through.

Virginia: The pressure of carrying the hope of a nation entirely on your own shoulders. The utter despair of losing everything you held dear.

Virginia: It makes me sick just thinking about it.

Alain: Be that as it may, Virginia, I appreciate your anger on my behalf.

Virginia: Then don't worry. There's plenty more where that came from.

Alain: Please, Virginia. I'm a grown man, not a child.

#### Virginia and Alain - Chess and Home

Alain: A chess board?

Alain: Yet we were cast half a continent away from each other before I had the chance to make good on that promise.

Alain: I can, and I will.

Alain: Did you not have anyone to play chess with when you were taking refuge in Drakenhold?

Alain: Forgive me. It's only that your strategy remains the same as it was all those years ago.

Alain: 'Tis a cruel reminder of what this war has stolen from you: the opportunity to enjoy life as every child should.

Alain: You're always getting angry on my behalf, regardless of what those around you may think of the matter.

Alain: I need to apologize for our last conversation, Virginia.

Virginia: I thought it was cute, seeing you cry as much as you used to as a spoiled little child.

Alain: I'm glad you're the only one who ever saw me like that.

Alain: And I the same, Virginia.

Alain: Concealed as you were in a foreign land, there were none you could turn to in your times of loneliness.

Alain: Yet now you have me.

Alain: Nor am I a helpless prince who needs you to argue on his behalf.

Alain: And I promise we shall bear them together.

Virginia: I don't know, Alain. I just...

Alain: Think of nothing else for now, Virginia. With me, all you need do is speak from the heart.

Virginia: I want to go home. Back to Gran Corrine, and back to our castle.

Virginia: Promise me that we'll live in Cornia someday, and that we'll do so again together. Please.

Alain: And once we do, we can play in the garden just as we did when we were young.

Alain: You have my word.

#### Virginia and Alain - Ring of the Maiden

Virginia: Well? I'll be taking that ring now.

Alain: Of course.

Virginia: Glad you know what's best for you.

Virginia: Honestly, I had always believed I'd be queen someday. I thought it was inevitable, really.

Virginia: But that horrible day ten years past, I nearly lost hope entirely.

Alain: It must have been awfully hard. I at least had Josef to protect me, but you were all alone in this world.

Virginia: Deep down, I knew Cornia had fallen. I just didn't want to admit it.

Virginia: still, there were nights I let myself slip into fantasy: memories of you and Aunt Ilenia.

Virginia: Dreaming how one day we would reinstate the royal family.

Virginia: But it seems that's no longer a dream. Not anymore.

Alain: Assuming I have you at my side, that is.

Alain: Virginia, I need you more than you could possibly know.

Virginia: Our covenant is sealed.

Virginia: You can come a bit closer, if you want.

Virginia: I once thought of you as a brother, but you're so much more to me than that.

Virginia: We will be king and queen.

#### Virginia and Alain - Final Battle

Alain: Galerius, Emperor of Zenoira.

Galerius: If you hope to speak, you'll find me no willing participant. I have no words for you.

Galerius: End this, now.

Galerius: Hmph.

Galerius: What do you think you're doing?

Baltro: If it wasn't clear, Your Majesty, the sigil seeks none other.

Galerius: Traitorous fool. Finally gone senile, hm?

Ilenia: Ngh.

Virginia: I don't know how, but she's perfectly fine.

Virginia: Tomorrow is a new dawn, both for our kingdom and for us.

Virginia: Oh, and let me know if you ever want to take in the garden together. I'll join you any time you like.

Virginia: Can I ask you something, Leah? Why do you keep standing off in the distance when I'm speaking to someone?

Leah: Well, I'd prefer not to interrupt your merriment, my ladyship.

Virginia: Nonsense. They'd all like to talk to you, not see you watching them from half a mile off.

Leah: I'll do just that, thank you.

### Yahna

#### Yahna Recruited

Alain: It's not every day you get stared down by a cat.

Yahna: Hm. You don't look like any Zenoirans I've ever seen.

Alain: We're not, actually. And who might you be?

Yahna: I'm Yahna, a witch from the marshland hamlet ahead.

Hodrick: Did I hear that correctly? You say your name is Yahna?

Hodrick: You must be a descendant of the old court sorceress, the great and noble Yahna who served under Queen Ilenia's grandfather.

Hodrick: Such knowledge brings my heart great joy. I was but a child when I knew her, yet she left a lasting warmth few can match.

Hodrick: I never expected to come across one of her lineage in a place as bleak and desolate as this.

Alain: We caught wind of Zenoiran soldiers discussing their fruitless search for an old witch.

Yahna: That would be our elder, yes. We magicked her away somewhere safe in hopes of eluding their gaze.

Yahna: But those dogs still bear down on the hamlet, using their hunt as an excuse to tear its walls apart board by board.

Alain: A distressing tale indeed.

Yahna: Though the final act is yet to be written. Please, help us break free of their bloodied fangs.

Alain: You needn't so much as ask. We'll do what we must to bring an end to these abuses.

Yahna: Thank you both. I never could have restored peace to the hamlet without your help.

Yahna: Ah, well. Perhaps it's better if I just introduce you.

Hodrick: Hm? I would never decline such an honor, my lady, but what reason could you possibly have for asking me to join?

Yahna: You'll see soon enough. Now, come along.

Alain: Tell us, Yahna. Where is this elder you spoke of?

Yahna: still haven't caught on, hm?

Yahna: You always were the most naive pup in the litter, my little Hodrick.

Hodrick: That name...

Yahna: Decrepit? Old? Antique?

Yahna: So I crafted a spell to peel back the years and restore my youth, though I daresay it dampened my magick as well.

Hodrick: Astonishing what miracles sorcery empowers.

Yahna: It's one of the most prized techniques my master taught me, and not a feat for the weak of heart, mind you.

Yahna: Now, I'd very much like to resume my duties, and I'd like to do so in service of the Liberation.

Yahna: Let this old vassal put a young hand toward restoring her homeland.

#### Yahna and Alain - Court Sorceress

Alain: I understand you once served as court sorceress for Cornia's royal family, Yahna.

Yahna: I did, yes. Long before you were born.

Alain: What were your duties in such a role?

Yahna: Mostly mundane things like erecting magick barriers, brewing curative potions, and training the younger witches and wizards of the castle.

Yahna: Though that often only consisted of hearing their worries, then crafting a simple incantation to ease their troubled minds.

Alain: And what manner of problems were they concerned about?

Yahna: The most common was a fundamental reluctance to even raise their weapon to another human being.

Yahna: Cornia and Drakenhold were still locked in frequent border disputes back then, so the fear of battle was ever present in people's thoughts.

Yahna: But weave a quick spell, and all their hesitations would melt away.

Alain: Which would in turn prevent those anxieties from becoming a liability in the critical moment.

Yahna: It was a useful technique, to be sure.

Yahna: And given the effect Zenoira's magick has already had on our people, we need to be more careful than ever about using this approach.

Alain: Great enough that I've no doubts about allowing you to cast such a spell on me.

Yahna: I'll be sure to make the effects especially mild, to leave your heart as unscathed as possible.

#### Yahna and Alain - Poison Arrow

Alain: Watch out, Yahna!

Yahna: Ah!

Yahna: A poison arrow! Prince? No...

Alain: Ngh... Is that you, Yahna?

Yahna: The commander of an army should never go risking his own life for a mere soldier.

Yahna: Or are you trying to squander the sacrifice your mother made for you?

Alain: Yet I do know you've the knowledge to cure the poison, should the need arise.

Yahna: Not all poisons. This one is extremely potent, designed to be used for assassinations.

Yahna: If I hadn't been right here next to you when the arrow struck, you'd be off making merry with the Father right about now.

Alain: I truly am sorry for what I've done.

Yahna: But in that moment, I think I knew just how my master must have felt.

Alain: You mean the witch Alcina.

Yahna: Even forgetting everything I just told you, I still want you to live.

Yahna: Not because you're a prince, but because you're you.

Alain: Heheh. Well, I'm glad to hear it.

Yahna: What's so funny about that?

Alain: Worry not. I'll deflect the arrow with my shield next time, rather than take the blow myself.

Yahna: Meaning you will still step in front of me.

Yahna: What am I ever going to do with you, Prince?

#### Yahna and Alain - Ring of the Maiden

Yahna: You wanted something, Prince?

Alain: I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

Yahna: Well, this is a surprise.

Yahna: I've walked this earth for countless years, and never once received such a bold proposal.

Alain: Yet I would have no other, Yahna. Your experience, your wisdom, and your kindness are, simply put, unparalleled.

Alain: I ask that you not only stand beside me, but guide my way as my bewitching bride.

Yahna: I admit, I was thinking I'd take up my old job as court sorcerer once the war was over, but... queen, hm?

Alain: Your beauty would light the castle no matter what role you took.

Alain: Though I was hoping you'd choose to light my life as well.

Alain: What do you say?

Yahna: I've lived tens of thousands of days in my life, but this one is surely the happiest of them all.

Yahna: I'll have that ring now.

Yahna: And I promise, those Zenoiran fools won't touch a hair on your head as long as I'm here.

Yahna: We'll get through this together, Alain. And rebuild Cornia as husband and wife.

Alain: I would have it no other way.

Yahna: So why is it that I feel so blissfully warm?

#### Yahna and Alain - Final Battle

Galerius: End this, now.

Galerius: Hmph.

Galerius: Gah.

Alain: Mother!

Galerius: How does it feel, hm? Your dear mother, slain by your own hand.

Alain: What is happening to me?

Yahna: Get back, Alain!

Galerius: What a poor fool he was, doomed to the same fate as the pitiful queen before him.

Galerius: His strength surpasses even Ilenia's. The might of the unicorn runs deep in his veins.

Galerius: The ring is mine to command, and a futile demise is all that awaits you now.

Galerius: None can ever hope to halt my designs. Bow to your emperor.

Galerius: You will make a fine Zenoiran vessel once it is over.

Galerius: The ring... why does it hold such vast energy?

Yahna: Seems the Maiden was right, not that I ever doubted her.

Yahna: Now then... let's break this accursed spell together.

Galerius: It will take more than this to defeat me.

Alain: Galerius. You saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire.

Alain: But as long as I live and breathe, you'll never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

Galerius: How do you know of that?

Galerius: You will not!

Galerius: Their emperor shall never know defeat.

Baltro: Your Majesty.

Galerius: How goes the rite?

Galerius: Then these insects shall be more than enough. Grant me your strength, and we'll stamp them out together.

Galerius: What do you think you're doing?

Baltro: If it wasn't clear, Your Majesty, the sigil seeks none other.

Galerius: Traitorous fool. Finally gone senile, hm?

Alain: Mother!

Ilenia: Ngh.

Yahna: She's still breathing. You fought well, my queen.

Alain: Speak to me, please.

Josef: I never imagined he possessed such frightful mastery over the bodies of others.

Ilenia: Alain. I can't say how much time has passed since that day, but you've grown so much.

Ilenia: If only I could have been there to witness it.

Ilenia: It seems I owe Josef a great deal for raising you in my absence.

Alain: Josef, see my mother somewhere safe.

Josef: And you, Your Highness?

Alain: We end this long-drawn war now.

Yahna: Baltro will rue the day he crossed our path.

Josef: Come home, both of you.

Baltro: What evil should I reanimate next? A monster capable of crushing you beneath its heel, perhaps.

Alain: Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call.

Alain: Your emperor is no more, and in his place stands a tyrannical fiend who craves nothing but absolute control.

Alain: Tell me, is this what you truly desire? To sacrifice your very essence in service of this daemon?

Alain: Souls of the departed, if you have any humanity left within you, lend me your aid.

Alain: These souls are not a power one can wield, Baltro. They are human lives, human will in its purest form.

Alain: Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Yahna and Alain - Ending

Yahna: Seeing it sitting there, wrapped delicately around my finger, brings me a greater joy than I could have even expected.

Yahna: I suppose now I'll have to return the favor.

Yahna: If anything's giving you trouble, just let your old court sorceress know and I'll make it disappear for you.

Yahna: You know, it's been years since I've seen the castle up close like this.

Yahna: But you won't let that stop you, not even for a second.

Yahna: You'll make a wonderful king, Alain. I'm more than certain of it.

#### Yahna and Alain - Court Sorceress

Alain: What sort of duties did a court sorceress perform?

Yahna: Magick barriers, curative potions, training younger witches and wizards. At times I also eased anxieties during border disputes with Drakenhold.

Alain: You did all that alone?

Yahna: With help where I could find it. One must be careful now, especially where Zenoira's magick is concerned.

Alain: Then I will trust your caution. Cast the spell on me.

Yahna: It is mild, but I appreciate the faith.

Alain: You have earned it many times over.

#### Yahna and Alain - Poison Arrow

Yahna: Alain!

Alain: I am fine.

Yahna: You are not fine. That arrow was poisoned.

Alain: It was aimed at you.

Yahna: A commander does not throw his life away for a mere soldier. Queen Ilenia would have scolded you until sunrise.

Alain: Then I am fortunate you are here instead.

Yahna: The poison was meant for assassination. If I had not been right here, you would be with your father.

Alain: Thank you, Yahna.

Yahna: I know how my master felt. Not because you are the prince, but because you are you.

Alain: Next time I will deflect the arrow with my shield.

Yahna: And still step in front of me.

Alain: Most likely.

### Yunifi

#### Yunifi and Alain - A Nose for Trouble

**Yunifi:** Aha! I knew it was you, Alain.

**Alain:** You knew from my scent?

**Yunifi:** You have this noble smell, but it is kinda rough around the edges, too. Totally different from pretty much any bestral. Were you out here picking berries? I can smell them in your bag.

**Yunifi:** I even know what you are thinking right now. Oh, it does not work like that. That was just a little joke.

**Yunifi:** But wait a sec. We have to get out of here, Alain. There is a blizzard coming our way, and fast. I am serious. Come on!

**Alain:** 'Tis a good thing we left when we did, Yunifi. Any later, and we would have found ourselves trapped in quite the storm.

**Yunifi:** That is just how it goes when you have lived in Bastorias as long as I have. You ever need a nose for something, I am your girl. This should be the place. Oh, and the ice is pretty thin around here, so make sure...

**Alain:** still, it is striking just how dangerous a land Bastorias can be, especially when something as commonplace as gathering materials can carry deadly implications. Were you not here next to me, I would not even be able to walk safely.

**Yunifi:** That is a bit of an exaggeration, do you not think?

**Alain:** Not in the slightest. Absent your guidance, our battles through the tundra would prove far more difficult. I would hazard to say you are the only reason we have survived for as long as we have.

**Yunifi:** Well, I am just happy to help where I can. You will have to follow my footsteps exactly if you do not want to fall into any holes hidden under the snow.

#### Yunifi and Alain - After the War

**Alain:** Thank you, Yunifi. To be honest, it is so cold out here that I was beginning to grow somewhat numb. Yet again, we have met with success in battle, and it is entirely thanks to you.

**Yunifi:** I dunno. It feels like maybe you are complimenting me too much.

**Alain:** I am not certain I see the problem with that.

**Yunifi:** I guess it is just getting my hopes up, is all. It makes me think you might even wanna live here in Bastorias with me after the war.

**Alain:** That is not possible, Yunifi.

**Yunifi:** Not for the man who is gonna be king, I know.

**Alain:** Indeed. Reclaiming my kingdom is the very reason I embarked on this journey to begin with.

**Yunifi:** I would not really be able to help you as much if we are not braving the tundra together.

**Alain:** But I would gladly let you lead me by the hand no matter where we are in all the world. In truth, I have grown rather fond of the way you pull me around.

**Alain:** Not only that, but I wish to do the same for you in my home of Cornia once we have claimed it as our own once more. Would you be open to that?

**Yunifi:** I have always wanted to see where you are from, too. So no matter what happens, just promise me you are really gonna do it. Show me around Cornia, I mean.

**Alain:** I promise, Yunifi.

#### Ring of the Maiden

**Yunifi:** Well, I am here. What is this about?

**Alain:** Yunifi, I'd like you to have the Ring of the Maiden.

**Yunifi:** Ah! If you are asking me that, then... does that mean I get to be with you forever?

**Alain:** It does, if you are willing to accept. I can picture no brighter future, Yunifi.

**Yunifi:** You know, I have never had a "real" family. Not that I can remember, at least. I mean, I do have Morard as family, and they are the best foster family I could have ever asked for.

**Yunifi:** But I want something more. A family I can call my own. And I want it with you, Alain. So it makes me really happy you feel the same.

**Alain:** I as well. In truth, I have never been happier. I take it this means you will accept, then?

**Yunifi:** As if you even have to ask. Now that that is all done with, maybe someday we can add to this little family of ours.

**Alain:** Haha. A nice idea, but I fear I only have one pair of rings.

**Yunifi:** That is not what I meant.

#### Final Battle

**Yunifi:** Alain!

**Galerius:** The ring is mine to command. Now, bow to your emperor!

**Yunifi:** You really think I would be happy with just a ring, huh? Well, you are wrong. A world without you is a world I do not wanna live in!

**Alain:** Yunifi!

**Alain:** Galerius, you saw in Fevrith's innocent people mere vessels to house your own fallen empire. But as long as I live and breathe, you will never inflict such callous devastation on our world.

**Alain:** Mother!

**Yunifi:** Phew. She is okay.

**Alain:** We end this long-drawn war now.

**Yunifi:** Let us finish him off for good, Alain.

**Alain:** Many times you have tried, Baltro, but you shall never break our spirit. I promise you that. Now prepare to be vanquished by the might of Fevrith!

**Yunifi:** So this is it, huh? We have come a long way from slinging stones back in Bastorias.

**Morard:** Indeed we have, but this battle will determine the fate of our home as well. It is now or never, Yunifi.

**Yunifi:** Then I am glad I have got you backing me up. Come on!

**Alain:** Spirits of Zenoira, hear my call. Let us lift the curse of the unicorn and bring the salvation of heaven to these lost souls.

#### Ending

**Yunifi:** You did promise to give me a little tour of Cornia first, remember? I wanna love it just as much as you. By that, I mean just as much as you love Cornia. Not as much as I love you. I am not sure that would even be possible, really.

**Yunifi:** Who knows the next time we will all be together like this, if ever.

**Morard:** The next time you see someone, it will be like no time has passed at all. I am sure of that.

**Yunifi:** Yeah. Thanks, Morard.

## Character Relationships

### Adel and Berenice

#### Adel and Berenice - Old Memories

Adel: Hold a moment! Is that you, Berenice?

Berenice: Got booted from the order, you mean. Guess this means you ride for the Liberation now?

Adel: I take it you still bear little interest in cavalry work.

Berenice: Would rather stick to what I do best. Me and horses do not really see eye to eye.

Adel: In training, you spent more time on the ground than in a saddle.

Adel: still, none of us could ever match your skill with a blade.

Berenice: Good thing there is more to being a knight than clomping around on some dumb beast.

Berenice: Besides, I am just a regular old mercenary now. For us, steel is the only thing that matters.

Adel: Seeing you just stirred up some old memories.

Berenice: Do not worry about it. I have to say, it feels good being back on the same side.

Berenice: See you on the battlefield, Adel.

Adel: I cannot wait.

#### Berenice and Adel - Sparring

Adel: Hmph! Hah!

Berenice: You fighting ghosts out here, or what?

Adel: I have only one option. Strive to reach the heights of my betters, or be left ever choking upon their dust.

Berenice: I am always looking for people who want to spar. What do you say?

Berenice: Word of warning, though. Think of me like some common soldier and I promise you will regret it.

Adel: You even positioned yourself opposite my spear while keeping at a safe distance.

Berenice: Cannot say I was expecting a fight that tough.

Berenice: I am not planning to choke on your dust, either.

### Adel and Celeste

#### Adel and Celeste - Storybook Hero

Celeste: Adel, wait! That was amazing.

Adel: What was?

Celeste: Our last battle, of course.

Celeste: You are a true knight in every sense of the word, the spitting image of the great hero I used to read about in storybooks.

Adel: Oh.

Celeste: The ideal picture of chivalry, charging forth with blessed spear in hand.

Adel: Please, Celeste. That is quite enough, I would say.

Celeste: It is nowhere close. I will continue to sing your praises from the first light of dawn until the radiant moon is nestled in the sky's embrace.

Adel: How am I meant to respond to such fearless flattery? I beg you, no more.

Celeste: Perhaps I let my emotions get the better of me.

Celeste: A fierce rodent warrior, marching to battle astride a faithful canine steed. I can imagine nothing more wonderful.

Adel: That is... not quite the comparison I expected.

### Adel and Clive

#### Adel and Clive - Training Days

Adel: Hmph!

Clive: Hah!

Clive: Training like this delivers my mind straight to our days coming through the order.

Adel: I was just thinking the same thing. I am amazed we even survived it.

Commander: Faster. Even the slowest foot soldier could dodge such languid thrusts.

Clive: Understood, ser.

Commander: Speed means nothing if you cannot even land a simple blow.

Adel: Thank you, ser.

Commander: Move!

Adel: I realize now it was not a lack of confidence that motivated the command. He was protecting us.

Clive: Indeed. It is the only reason we stand here today.

Adel: And strength is the only way we will see his faith rewarded.

Clive: I could not agree more. We must further hone our spears as the captain said, and do proud those who keep faith in us, His Highness most of all.

Adel: Come, Clive. We have training to do.

#### Adel and Clive - The Weight of War

Clive: Though we often face those who capitulated to Zenoira, a thought has only now occurred to me.

Clive: I am certain some of them surrendered not out of true deference, but merely from the wish to see those they love safe.

Adel: Those we crossed spears with in our battle for the province were no different, I would guess.

Clive: With each combatant felled, I could not help but feel some distant sense of loss.

Adel: We take up arms to protect the weak, and to deliver justice to those who stray from its light.

Adel: I will not tell you to just get over it, either. Remorse is a natural part of warfare.

Adel: All involved must bear the weight of their actions, and the consequences.

Adel: Some reluctantly sided with Zenoira. So do not waver in your conviction, Clive. They would strike you down at the first sign of doubt.

Clive: Indeed. I shall take heart in your words, as I always have.

Clive: If I may, Adel, I am proud to name you a dear friend.

Adel: Let us make it through this together, shall we?

### Adel and Jerome

#### Adel and Jerome - Pies

Jerome: I do hope they turned out all right.

Adel: I thought I smelled something good. Did you make these pies yourself, Ser Jerome?

Jerome: Yet now, at the pivotal moment, I find myself wracked with doubt. What use does an army have for mere confections?

Adel: Plenty, I would say. You would not know it, but a lot of our friends have quite the sweet tooth.

Adel: Good news, everyone! Ser Jerome has...

Jerome: Silence, I beg of you. In truth, I have more than one matter which concerns me.

Adel: Oh? Go on.

Jerome: What if they think accepting them would display an utter lack of foresight? Who knows what vile trick I could be plotting?

Adel: It sounds to me like you are overthinking this.

Jerome: Am I?

Adel: They will see you are not up to anything nefarious.

Jerome: Swearing they are not poisoned will only make matters worse.

Adel: Everyone is always clamoring for a good dessert. Their noses would lead them straight to you.

Jerome: Then I shall do just that. I was fortunate indeed to have encountered you when I did. Thank you, Adel.

Adel: They will be happy to hear you poured your heart into a little gesture for them.

Jerome: I would rather you did not tell them that, actually. I think the embarrassment would kill me where I stand.

### Adel and Melisandre

#### Melisandre and Adel - A Sudden Sister

Town Girl: Could I interest you in some flowers, fair knight? Or fresh vegetables, picked just this morning?

Melisandre: What are you doing still in town, Adel? Our mother is worried sick about you.

Melisandre: I should have known not to let you run off alone. We have to get home at once.

Adel: Melisandre? What is the meaning of this?

Melisandre: You needed help, did you not? You seemed far too flustered to resolve the situation on your own.

Adel: still, why make us out to be siblings?

Melisandre: Judging by your mannerisms, I imagine you do not have any real sisters of your own.

Adel: Was it that obvious? You are right, though. I cannot quite act the part if I have never experienced it.

Adel: I wonder if this is what it is really like having a sister.

Melisandre: How could you even imagine it after such a sickly display?

Adel: I did not think it that offensive.

### Adel and Rolf

#### Rolf and Adel - A Hunter's Gratitude

Rolf: Adel, I have something for you.

Adel: For me? Whatever for?

Rolf: You helped me in battle. When I had fallen, you pulled me back to my feet.

Adel: Anyone would have done the same.

Rolf: Perhaps. But you were the one who did.

Adel: I see. still, this is more thanks than the deed deserves.

Rolf: My mother taught me never to forget a kindness. She died young, and I had few lessons from her, so I take them seriously.

Adel: Then you have more than shown your appreciation. Any more gratitude and you will make me blush.

#### Adel and Rolf - A Hunter's Gratitude

Rolf: Here, Adel. This is for you.

Adel: I am not sure what I have done to deserve this, Rolf.

Rolf: Do you not remember? You helped me yesterday during the battle.

Adel: I did pull you to your feet after you had fallen over, but just about anyone would do the same.

Rolf: And only you actually did it. Anyway, I should be going.

Adel: Wait. Do not tell me this is for returning your coin purse after you dropped it.

Adel: That was a common courtesy, Rolf, and nothing more.

Rolf: Maybe so, but a debt is a debt, no matter how small.

Adel: Why are you so serious about this?

Rolf: It is something my mother said the day she died. I was still young, but I remember what she told me clear as day.

Rolf: She never had the chance to teach me many lessons, so I try to take the ones she did teach as seriously as possible.

Adel: Cannot you express the same emotion with a simple thank you?

Rolf: To be perfectly honest, I have never known if words would be enough.

Adel: Do not worry, Rolf. You have more than shown just how appreciative you are.

Rolf: That is good to hear. Thank you again, Adel.

Adel: Please, any more gratitude and I might blush.

### Adel and Yahna

#### Yahna and Adel - Bitter Medicine

Yahna: Adel, drink this before bed. It will quiet your worries and help you sleep.

Adel: It smells powerful.

Yahna: It is.

Adel: A gallant knight does not fear a little medicine.

Yahna: Then drink.

Adel: By the saints, that is bitter!

Yahna: Hm. I should improve the flavor.

Adel: Please do. For gallantry's sake.

#### Adel and Yahna - Bitter Medicine

Yahna: What is the matter, boy? Cannot sleep?

Adel: Ah, Yahna. Apologies if I woke you.

Yahna: Let me guess, the rush of our battle earlier is keeping you awake. It is a common problem among younger knights.

Adel: You have the short of it. And while I know I will suffer for this unease tomorrow, here I stand all the same.

Yahna: The human mind can be a cruel thing sometimes. Here, drink this.

Yahna: It is a concoction of mine that can quell your worries and lull you to a peaceful sleep, though I expect you will find it bitter indeed.

Adel: I can only imagine the slumber such a potion might bring. Now, let us see.

Adel: Pffft!

Yahna: That is why I always carry a spare bottle. Try again.

Adel: Summon your courage, Adel. Prove your worth as a gallant knight of Cornia.

Yahna: Hm. Maybe I should put some effort into the flavor.

### Adel, Clive, and Monica

#### Clive, Monica, and Adel

Adel: Lady Monica! Sorry, I didn't see you there. Hope I'm not interrupting anything.

Monica: I would be glad to drink with you. And so would Clive, it seems. Lead the way, Adel.

Adel: Once this war's over, you think we're gonna start families of our own?

Monica: Why, is there a lucky lady you had in mind?

Adel: I spent most of my time on the training ground with sweaty old men, not out on the town with girls. Same as Clive here!

Clive: I think you've had enough for the evening, Adel.

Adel: Whaddya mean? I'm barely even drunk yet. If only we had brides of our own, maybe things'd be different. All the better if it could be someone gorgeous like you, Monica.

Monica: Speaking of betrothal, though, I believe Clive here was once engaged himself.

Adel: Now wait just a sec! Is she telling the truth, Clive?

Clive: Yes, but that arrangement has years since been dissolved.

Adel: I thought you and me were the same. Lone wolves, all our lives!

Clive: Calm yourself, Adel. And you, Monica. Cease this mockery of our past at once.

Monica: I suppose I forgot. Clive's former fiancee is none other than myself.

Clive: Was that truly necessary, Monica?

Monica: I think the shock may have broken him.

### Amalia and Chloe

#### Amalia and Chloe - A Day's Food

Chloe: Amalia? Where did you get all that food?

Amalia: Went and hunted it myself, actually. This should be enough to get me through the day.

Chloe: The day? It must be half my body weight.

Amalia: It is only natural when you have a body this big.

Amalia: Do not worry about your fancy knife work or elaborate seasoning. Cannot be taking all night with this, you know.

Amalia: I will just toss some salt on top once it is finished.

Chloe: As long as you are sure.

Chloe: Though it must be tough eating all this in one sitting.

Amalia: You have got that right. I would rather spend my time swinging my sword than shoving food down my throat.

Chloe: You really love fighting, huh?

Amalia: With a fork and proper manners, at that.

### Amalia and Leah

#### Amalia and Leah - A Rematch

Leah: Oh, Amalia. I did not realize you were out here.

Amalia: It is you. Gilbert's...

Leah: My name is Leah.

Amalia: Right. So, you need something? A revenge match, is it? Fine by me.

Leah: I hoped you would say that. Let us commence.

Leah: Ngh.

Amalia: You held your own pretty well there, but it looks like I win again.

Leah: Thank you for agreeing to this, Amalia. You have shown me just how far I have yet to climb.

Amalia: You have got the perfect strategy for someone your size to topple a brute like me.

Leah: Do you truly mean that?

Leah: In that moment, I swore to rededicate myself to my training.

Leah: I would like to spar with you again sometime, if you would not mind.

Amalia: Just say the word, and I am there.

Leah: With that, I take my leave. Farewell for now.

Amalia: Damn. Better train harder if I do not want to end up on the end of her sword.

### Amalia and Mordon

#### Amalia and Mordon - The Sword

Mordon: You there. Amalia, was it?

Amalia: Mordon. Here to pester me for mead money, I assume?

Mordon: It is about that sword you have got. Mind if I take a closer look?

Amalia: Not at all. You have got better taste than I realized.

Mordon: Keep a grip on that thing, mind you. I would rather not get cleaved in two today.

Amalia: Do not worry. The sword is practically part of my body.

Mordon: It has a real aura to it. Intimidating, if I had to pick a word.

Mordon: What really makes me curious is what it is made of. Looks to me like some kind of stone, not iron. But I have never felt stone like this.

Amalia: The thing has been in my family for generations. Do not even think it is from Fevrith.

Mordon: Wherever it is from, they must have had quite some skill to cut and polish stone this hard.

Amalia: Anyway, are we done here or what?

Mordon: Just a few more minutes, please. I will buy you all the rounds you could ever want once we are done.

Amalia: You sure about that? I drink as much as a small army.

Mordon: We will see if you have the stomach to back that up.

Mordon: What stunning engraving.

Mordon: Listen, I know you did me a favor showing me your sword. But I did not think you would drain every last cask in the tavern.

Amalia: You are the one who offered. Now come on, I am still thirsty.

Mordon: What have I gotten myself into?

#### Mordon and Amalia - The Sword

Mordon: That sword of yours is something else. stone-like, but not iron. I have never seen its like.

Amalia: You have a good eye.

Mordon: Let me study it over drinks.

Amalia: Very well.

Mordon: You emptied the tavern.

Amalia: You offered.

Mordon: Aye, and I regret it more with every cup.

### Aramis and Gilbert

#### Aramis and Gilbert - Brothers

Aramis: Gilbert.

Gilbert: Ah, Ludwig. What brings you here?

Aramis: Concern for you. Our king shouldn't be wandering out alone in the dark of night.

Gilbert: You needn't worry yourself. I wasn't planning to stay long.

Aramis: This river always was your favorite place to clear your mind.

Gilbert: You remember that?

Aramis: Like the day Father scolded you for absconding with his mantle. Your tears practically formed a stream of their own.

Gilbert: You were always there to protect me, even if it meant suffering the punishment yourself.

Gilbert: merely one of the many things that has changed since you left.

Aramis: Indeed.

Gilbert: The stories you used to read to me. Your favorite pastry. The tones of your voice and the tint of your eyes.

Gilbert: Remind me of who we once were, and teach me who you've become in the time since.

Aramis: I would like nothing more.

Aramis: Perhaps you thought to shift the blame, yet the jam staining your lips made the true culprit rather obvious indeed.

Gilbert: That's quite enough recounting of my adolescent mischief, thank you.

Aramis: Oh? I thought you would be pleased to hear I still remember.

Gilbert: I was, for the first twenty stories. 'Tis clear to me that you recall every agonizing detail of my childhood.

Gilbert: Now, I wish to hear of yours instead.

Gilbert: Ludwig?

Aramis: Alas, the same is true for me. My time as crown prince is but a clouded blur in my mind.

Gilbert: Surely you jest.

Aramis: It is as though the "Ludwig" you refer to is another man entirely.

Aramis: I, who chose to wander our lands rather than bear the burden of kingship, a burden which now rests upon your shoulders.

Gilbert: I would ask the same question of you. If you've truly renounced all that you once were, what of me?

Gilbert: In my belief, nothing can sever a bond of blood.

Gilbert: Even should I never see you again, for as long as I live.

Aramis: Yet again, I'm met with my own inadequacies.

Aramis: You always have had the better of me, Gilbert.

Aramis: And if not that, then at least the finest brother.

Gilbert: Thank you, Ludwig.

### Aramis and Gloucester

#### Aramis and Gloucester - Old Friends

Gloucester: It's a great honor to walk at your side once more, my prince.

Gloucester: Ser Aramis, that is.

Aramis: Please, Gloucester. I'd much prefer if you refrained from scowling every time you said my name.

Gloucester: Forgive me. I intended no such thing.

Aramis: You always have been fairly easy to read.

Gloucester: The fates have thrust you through much these past few years. To see it laid so bare before me, I cannot help but feel an immense sadness.

Aramis: Despite my struggles, I daresay I would make the same decision time and again, if given the opportunity.

Gloucester: But Prince Ludwig...

Aramis: It mustn't be easy, awakening from a years-long spell to learn you've committed such grave sins.

Aramis: And yet, you don't hide from the truth, but face it head-on. It's a trait I wish I possessed myself.

Gloucester: Your words humble me, Ser Aramis.

Gloucester: But I entreat you, don't keep the pain you feel entirely to yourself.

Gloucester: If I can't be your aid amidst times of sorrow, I've no right to stand at your side in days of peace.

Aramis: Very well. Your ear will be the first and only that I pull.

Gloucester: How would you have me serve?

Aramis: I was actually thinking we could go for a meal together.

Gloucester: I'm sorry?

Aramis: I'd be honored to have you join me, if you're interested.

Gloucester: It would be my humblest pleasure.

Aramis: An exquisite meal, as promised. I'm simply glad we had the chance to enjoy it together.

Gloucester: Is that all you asked me here for?

Aramis: It is indeed.

Gloucester: But a meal, Ser Aramis? You must surely have something else you'd have me do.

Aramis: Did you not enjoy yourself?

Gloucester: That's not it at all. I merely expected something more, I suppose.

Aramis: What need is there for such grandeur amongst peers?

Gloucester: You would truly count me as such?

Aramis: Hence, I asked you to join me for this meal instead. Not as lord and retainer, but old friends.

Aramis: And for what it's worth, I quite enjoyed myself. I do hope we can do it again sometime.

Gloucester: In the many years I've served him, I've never seen a smile play so sincerely across his face.

Gloucester: But perhaps discarding his name wasn't the mistake I thought it to be.

### Aramis and Leah

#### Aramis and Leah - Recognition

Aramis: I must say, I didn't expect to be identified so quickly.

Aramis: And here I thought myself a more masterful liar than that.

Leah: There's no hiding the eyes of our late king.

Aramis: still, it's only natural you see him in me. I know you bore a deep love for my father.

Leah: As your brother has said, there are many people who wish for your return.

Aramis: And you, Leah? What is it that you wish for the man who did nothing but watch as his father perished?

Leah: I'm certain he would be grateful to see his eldest son survive this war, no matter how that came about.

Leah: And I feel much the same.

Leah: To be frank, when I realized it was you who stood before me...

Aramis: Instead of your knowledge of it against me, that is.

Leah: What duplicity are you implying?

Aramis: Forgive me. I didn't mean to discredit your loyalty.

Aramis: And for idolizing my father so dearly.

### Aramis and Melisandre

#### Aramis and Melisandre - Refinement

Melisandre: And there's another one. Nobody told me the men of the Liberation would be so handsome.

Melisandre: He's nothing compared to Alain, of course, but far more beauty than I'd expect from a simple mercenary.

Aramis: Lady Melisandre of Cornia's esteemed House Meillet. You've been watching me for some time now.

Aramis: To what do I owe the honor?

Melisandre: You carry yourself quite unlike your peers. With more refinement, more elegance.

Melisandre: It makes me wonder where you hail from. Is it a noble family? Or royalty, perhaps?

Aramis: I admit, I've always had a fondness for the stage. If you think me well suited to it, I'll gladly accept the compliment.

Melisandre: Then would you be able to play the role of bandit instead? Or barbarian, if asked?

Aramis: Of course, should one of our tactics require such a ruse, or should my employer will it.

Melisandre: If anything, you're more like a heroic prince. One who hides his noble standing in order to fight for justice.

Aramis: You think too much of me, my lady. My heart beats for gold and nothing else.

Melisandre: If you say so. Either way, we'll be spending plenty more time together.

Melisandre: I'd love to hear more about your mercenary work. What battles you've won. Who taught you those manners.

Aramis: And I the same regarding the illustrious House Meillet. Farewell, my lady.

Aramis: I'll have to watch out for her moving forward.

### Aramis and Primm

#### Aramis and Primm - Rewards

Primm: What do I do?

Aramis: You seem rather troubled over there.

Primm: Well, it's embarrassing to admit, but I've spent almost all my money at the local tavern.

Aramis: Oh?

Primm: Lately I've been working even harder than normal, meaning my diet has grown somewhat out of control.

Primm: steak hache, rice pilaf, pot-au-feu. A nice salad here, a tarte tatin there.

Primm: Fresh pasta, the most wonderful galettes. Oh, and carpaccio! And oysters, too.

Aramis: I'm not sure how your stomach can possibly handle all that.

Primm: My stomach isn't the issue, sadly. My coin purse is.

Aramis: Perhaps you wouldn't be bleeding your funds dry if you rewarded yourself with something other than food.

Primm: But what should I replace it with?

Primm: Hm. What if you were my reward? Talking to you, that is.

Aramis: No, I don't think that will work at all.

Primm: Oh. Right, of course not. I'm sure you have far better things to do than entertain me whenever I please.

Aramis: That's not the problem, Primm. Were that your reward, I could never speak to you at any other time.

Primm: But that would be almost like punishment.

Primm: I only suggested it so I could learn more about you.

Aramis: Did you, now?

Aramis: Well, far be it from me to refuse the wishes of so beautiful a rose.

Aramis: But first, we must decide upon a new reward for you.

Primm: You're going to help me think of one, Ser Aramis?

Aramis: After all, I was the one who suggested it in the first place.

Aramis: A moment of your time, Primm. I believe I've come up with an adequate reward for you.

Primm: Does it have something to do with all of these soldiers?

Aramis: Indeed it does. Members of our army who have found themselves on the receiving end of your magick.

Aramis: If you would, everyone.

Liberation Swordfighter: Lady Primm! We're forever grateful for the healing you provided us.

Liberation Wyvern Knight: Hooray for Lady Primm!

Liberation Mercenary: Long live Lady Primm!

Aramis: Well? What did you think?

Primm: It's just the kind of surprise I'd expect from someone like you.

Aramis: It seems you didn't enjoy it, then.

Primm: I'm not sure I could handle a parade in my honor every time I want a reward.

Aramis: Yes. I suppose it wasn't the most practical of ideas.

Primm: Usually, a reward is accompanied by a nice, long hug.

Aramis: Interesting. In that case, I've no choice but to do the same.

Primm: Are you sure, Ser Aramis?

Aramis: Only then will I be able to tell you what fine work you've done.

Primm: This is getting to be a bit more effort than I bargained for.

Aramis: Before I forget, we only emerged victorious in yesterday's battle thanks to your magick.

Aramis: How glad I am to have freed such a gorgeous blossom from her Drakenhold gaol those many days ago.

Primm: Thank you, Aramis.

Primm: I'm not sure my heart could handle receiving a reward like this with every new achievement.

### Aramis and Travis

#### Aramis and Travis - The Book

Travis: What're you reading there?

Aramis: Ah! Why have you snuck up on me, spy?

Aramis: I may have mistaken you for an enemy and cut you down.

Travis: Sorry about that.

Travis: I get the feeling you're hiding something. Or maybe a few somethings.

Aramis: I'm little more than a common soldier who enjoys a life of peace and quiet.

Travis: The one about a solitary sellsword who rebels against his cruel despot and becomes king himself.

Travis: An aspiration of yours, perhaps? You certainly have the talent, if nothing else.

Aramis: I think not.

Aramis: Hence I thought there may be wisdom to glean, even from fiction like this.

Travis: There's an Aramis in that story too, just like in ours.

Aramis: A relative of the main character, yes. The man turns to crime in order to protect his family, and in the end burns at the stake for it.

Travis: Your parents must have been peculiar indeed to give you a name like that in Drakenhold.

Aramis: I'll agree with you there.

### Aramis and Virginia

#### Virginia and Aramis - Hair and Sparring

Aramis: I must say, I never have relished the heat here in Drakenhold.

Virginia: And yet you refuse to let a barber's blade anywhere near those flowing locks of yours. It would help, you know.

Aramis: Perhaps. But long hair is a defining feature of the man I've made of myself.

Aramis: In any case, I've grown used to it by now.

Virginia: Somehow, I doubt I'll ever understand you.

Virginia: My aunt was an amazing woman, but my respect for her comes from actions, not appearances.

Virginia: Not to mention the incessant burden long hair poses in battle.

Aramis: Hair can even serve as a weapon, if used correctly.

Virginia: Say whatever drivel you want.

Aramis: It's the truth.

Aramis: Imagine dodging an enemy's attack at the last moment, then flinging your hair in their face.

Aramis: Aim for their eyes, rob them of their sight, and the day will surely be yours.

Virginia: I admit, I've never considered it like that.

Virginia: If you really think it can aid me in combat, I might be willing to learn.

Aramis: It was nothing more than a little joke at your expense.

Virginia: Loathsome ingrate. How dare you!

Aramis: I'm sorry, truly. It was a temptation I simply couldn't shy away from.

Aramis: Now then, I fear I can bear this heat no longer. Farewell.

Virginia: But it seems life in the real world has changed him. For the better, I'd say.

Aramis: This is quite the revelation, Virginia. I never expected you to so earnestly wield the art I crafted in mere jest.

Aramis: I had heard rumors of your unbridled ways, but now I know them to be true myself.

Virginia: Joke or no, this sparring session has more than proven their potential.

Aramis: There's no telling how my brother might react to such news.

Virginia: And what does Gilbert have to do with this, exactly?

Aramis: Anyone would lament, knowing a precious jewel has suffered damage not long after leaving their care.

Virginia: Ah, of course. This must be another one of your jests.

Virginia: You're far, far easier to get along with.

Aramis: In fact, those who once knew me as prince still strive desperately to see even a shadow of the man I used to be.

Virginia: I have no fondness for the stiff formality of a royal court myself.

Virginia: Nor for your past self.

Aramis: For once, I find myself at a loss for words.

Virginia: And that's how I plan to address you. As a simple sellsword, not the heir you once were.

Aramis: I'd like that very much, thank you.

Aramis: I only hope we find the chance to spar again soon.

Virginia: We surely will. After all, I'd never shy away from an easy victory.

### Aubin and Dinah

#### Dinah and Aubin - Trust

**Aubin:** You followin' me for somethin', Dinah?

**Dinah:** Hm.

**Aubin:** Back in the day, me and my friends would come down to this shore every night. Talk about what we were hopin' to get outta life. Thought I would come by and relive the memory.

**Dinah:** You must have cared a lot about these friends of yours.

**Aubin:** More than my own damn life. Always have and always will.

**Dinah:** Even if they were not the same race as you? Me, I still cannot bring myself to trust humans. Not fully.

**Aubin:** The second we were together, we had the whole world treatin' us like thieves and lowlifes. Not to mention what it is like actually livin' here. Ya see a lot of good people die way too young.

**Aubin:** When every day is a struggle just to keep on survivin', stuff like race never even crosses your mind.

**Dinah:** Huh.

**Aubin:** Plenty of humans did ya wrong over the years, I know. But I will more than earn it, I can promise ya that.

**Dinah:** You already have. Besides, I know what the eyes of a liar look like, and those are not it. Guess I have got some work to do myself.

**Aubin:** We all do, Dinah. That is what makes life worth livin'. And here I thought I was gonna be thinkin' about old memories tonight, not makin' new ones.

### Aubin and Gloucester

#### Aubin and Gloucester

Aubin: I hear ya been steerin' clear of your family ever since we set ya free from Zenoira, Gloucester.

Gloucester: How did you know that?

Aubin: I'm not one for givin' advice, but ya might wanna stop by. Let 'em breathe easy after all this stressin'.

Gloucester: I can't do that. Not until I've atoned for the sins I've committed.

Aubin: They'd be stuck sufferin' that pain for the rest o' their lives.

Gloucester: It changes nothing. Until that duty is done, I'll never yield to my own selfish desires for care or affection.

Aubin: Little harsh, don't ya think?

Gloucester: It is what it is. Apologies if I caused you concern. Yet I've no intention of leaving this world any time soon. My family will just have to wait.

Aubin: If you say so. But if I ever run into 'em myself, I'm still gonna tell 'em you're doin' okay.

### Aubin and Jeremy

#### Aubin and Jeremy

Aubin: It was real pitiful, watchin' ya beg for your life while all your men lay dead around ya. I get ya were tryin' to survive, but that doesn't mean I gotta like it.

Jeremy: So what, just 'cause my men were gone, I shoulda asked to go with 'em? Besides, the boss knew damn well what he was gettin' when he took me on.

Aubin: And what if it was your own family layin' there? Would ya still've acted like they were nothin' to ya?

Jeremy: Yeah. I'd leave 'em, just like anyone else. If ya don't like it, try tellin' the boss to put us in different units for once.

Aubin: Gotta say, it does make me wonder. What would I do if Magellan or Liza went n' got themselves killed? And who was that "good man" he was talkin' about, anyway?

#### Aubin and Jeremy - The Good Man

Jeremy: Heh, if it ain't my best pal Aubin. How can I help ya?

Aubin: The one ya said took his morals to the grave. I think I know who it is. Now c'mon, out with it.

Jeremy: Suit yourself. I wasn't about to let him march off to his death, so I followed pretty close behind. But the bastards saw me. Just as they were gonna strike the killin' blow, my friend jumped in the way. Took it himself. There's only one person I'm lookin' out for now, and it's me.

Aubin: Didn't realize ya had it that rough. I was happy just callin' ya a coward instead o' learnin' the truth for myself. I'm sorry, Jeremy.

Jeremy: Ugh. First the boss, n' now you. Why can't everyone just leave me the hell alone? Ya ask me, you're all too damn nice for your own good.

Aubin: And you're not the ruthless dog ya pretend to be.

Jeremy: Ya go n' get yourself killed like he did, n' I'll regret ever tellin' ya about this in the first place.

Aubin: Better hope I don't help him outta instinct, then.

### Aubin and Liza

#### Aubin and Liza

Aubin: Well, look who's gone n' grown up. Feels like yesterday ya were just some little brat hidin' in your brother's shadow. 'Course, we were all brats back then. Remember the days we spent swimmin' in the oasis? You, me, n' Magellan, not a shred o' clothes between us.

Liza: Why'd you abandon us, Aubin?

Aubin: I couldn't read a word o' what it said, mind ya, but I always loved lookin' at the pictures. Till Zenoira took our boat, that is. Been livin' as a merc ever since.

Liza: That's not what I asked. And for the record, I know all about that dream of yours. I wanna know why you didn't take me with you, dammit. You promised.

Aubin: I did?

Liza: Don't tell me you forgot!

Aubin: Look. Even if I wanted to take ya, you were what, seven? Eight? Ocean's no place for a girl like that.

Liza: Grr...

Aubin: I did bring ya somethin', though. Some kinda stone they say ya can only get outside o' Fevrith.

Liza: Well, you're dead wrong. I don't want your damn rock, and I don't want your lies either!

Aubin: That coulda gone better. Guess I've got Magellan n' the old lady to thank for goin' soft on her all those years.

### Aubin and Magellan

#### Aubin and Magellan - The Desert

Aubin: Desert's changed a lot since I've been gone.

Magellan: Ya can probably guess what happened next. They sent an army down here to try n' stop us. Me n' the boss figured we could still talk him 'round, though. He killed her, Aubin. Beat me half to death too. After that, can't remember a damn thing.

Aubin: Always knew the old shrew wouldn't go peacefully.

Magellan: Without her leadin' us, the rest o' the gang scattered to the wind.

Aubin: Lookin' at it now, she was prob'ly the closest thing to a mom we ever had.

Magellan: To me, to Gloucester, and to her.

Aubin: Just like she taught us.

#### Aubin and Magellan - Homeland

Aubin: Damn, it's cold.

Magellan: Gotta wonder how the folks here deal with it all year 'round.

Aubin: Like we had it any better. That desert'll kill ya durin' the day, then chill ya to the bone once night comes knockin'.

Magellan: still...

Aubin: We had a chance to show the world what that stretch o' sand means to us. To show 'em who we really are.

Magellan: If she seriously meant all that, then she shoulda just said so.

Aubin: Yeah, like that'd work. Whole speech woulda gone in one ear n' out the other. She was right, though. Now c'mon, we've got work to do.

### Aubin and Ridiel

Ridiel: Watch where you are going, old man.

Ridiel: Wait. Is that you, Aubin?
