Aubin: Guess that friend is you, huh?

Ridiel: She is really doing that for me?

Aubin: I will even give you a little coin for ingredients, to make up for bumping into you.

Ridiel: I never even considered making something together.

Ridiel: Now hand over that gold, and Chloe and I will make enough sharbat for all three of us.

Aubin: Sounds good to me. Just do not go getting sick off it, yeah?

#### Aubin and Ridiel

Ridiel: I can't wait to see the look on Chloe's face when I surprise her with it. No... my sharbat! Watch where you're going, old man! Wait. Is that you, Aubin?

Aubin: Old man? Y'know I'm still in my twenties, yeah?

Ridiel: I waited for hours to get that sharbat for me and Chloe, and now the only ones who get to enjoy it are the desert ants.

Aubin: Guess that friend is you, huh?

Ridiel: She's really doing that for me?

Aubin: I'll even give ya a little coin for ingredients, make up for bumpin' into ya.

Ridiel: Now hand over that gold, and Chloe and I will make enough sharbat for all three of us.

Aubin: Sounds good to me. Just don't go gettin' sick off it, yeah?

### Aubin, Liza, and Magellan

#### Aubin, Liza, and Magellan - Dream of the Boat

Aubin: Well, whaddya think? Pretty amazin', yeah?

Liza: I've never seen this much water in my life, 'cept in your book, I mean!

Magellan: Y'mean the one the ol' boss gave ya?

Aubin: Besides, what's the point o' sailin' the ocean if I don't got my friends here to enjoy it with?

Magellan: So this is that dream you were always talkin' about.

Aubin: The hell was that? We're takin' on water pretty fast. She's goin' down!

Aubin: Ahh!

Liza: Hey! Watch where you're goin'!

Aubin: It was all just a dream? What the...

Liza: You okay, Aubin? You're sweatin' like a damn pig over there.

Aubin: Liza! You're alive! Wait, where's Magellan?

Liza: Quit it with the huggin'! You're gonna make me all sweaty now!

Aubin: Sorry.

Liza: Some dumb dream where we all died on your boat?

Aubin: It's not funny. I really thought I went n' got the both o' ya killed.

Liza: Well, even if you did, I'm sure we wouldn't have minded goin' down with a friend.

Aubin: That's not the point, Liza. Especially knowin' full well that it's my damn fault.

Liza: What're you mutterin' about over there? It was just a dream, Aubin. Besides, you know it'll take way more than that to kill us. When you do get that boat of yours, you'd better not go settin' sail alone. You hear me?

Aubin: Loud n' clear.

### Auch and Berenice

#### Auch and Berenice - Fist-Fighting

Berenice: Nice hit you got in back there, Auch.

Berenice: You smacked him away without so much as thinking about it. Did not even use your staff, just a fist.

Berenice: Knocked the guy out cold, too. Pretty good work for a fluke.

Berenice: We have got to tap into that skill. Train you up into a real bruiser.

Auch: Please, never stand that close to me again.

Berenice: Shame. I would be glad to teach you.

Auch: I have not enough time to hone my sorcery as it stands.

Berenice: A little muscle will give that magick of yours all the oomph you could ever need.

Berenice: Now quit your complaining and let us get started already. I think I am going to enjoy this.

### Auch and Fodoquia

#### Fodoquia and Auch - Voices of the Dead

**Auch:** I wish to hear my mother's voice, if only one more time.

**Fodoquia:** Compose yourself, Auch, and speak plain, that I might better understand your words.

**Auch:** He claimed that angels could pull back the veil of death and summon the voices of those beyond.

**Fodoquia:** Where did you hear such a claim?

**Auch:** Cornia, ser.

**Fodoquia:** It hardly comes as a surprise to learn the prevalence of such falsehoods.

**Auch:** Then you cannot speak to the dead?

**Fodoquia:** Would that I were able. I desperately long to hear my son's voice even one more time.

**Auch:** I did not realize you were a father, Fodoquia.

**Fodoquia:** My boy loved life more than life itself, yet he was stolen from me upon Zenoira's invasion of Albion.

**Auch:** I am sorry to hear that.

**Fodoquia:** We shall not hear them again until we ourselves have passed on to the great beyond. Even if it were possible, such desecration would defile our very souls and disturb the slumber of those we wish to contact. Do you understand?

**Auch:** I do.

**Fodoquia:** Then hold fast to the memories of your loved ones, for only they can provide the comfort you seek. You would do well to remember those words, Auch. I pray you will not succumb to the same mistakes I did in its pursuit.

### Auch and Kitra

#### Kitra and Auch - A Frozen Pendant

Kitra: There you are, Auch! I need your help, fast.

Auch: What do you think you are doing? Unhand my collar this instant.

Kitra: By the time I realized this morning, it was already frozen solid.

Auch: I am a powerful sorcerer, not a piece of charcoal willing to summon forth flames at your convenience.

Auch: If you will excuse me, I would like to get back to my studies. I have little enough respite as it is without your interruptions.

Kitra: Wait, please. That pendant is the only thing I have left from my mom.

Auch: What did you say?

Kitra: Magick is the only chance I have got.

Auch: Fine. But just this once, you understand?

Kitra: Thanks again, Auch. If you ever want a hand with something, I will come running any time you need me.

Auch: All I ask is that you take greater care of your mementos from now on.

### Auch and Melisandre

#### Auch and Melisandre - A Precious Gem

Melisandre: You know, Auch, you are actually quite handsome. If only you did not hide it behind robes and hoods all the time.

Auch: I will thank you not to stare, please. My looks have always been a complicated matter.

Melisandre: How so?

Auch: Sometimes I wonder if a wretch like me even deserves her visage.

Melisandre: Why not put in a little more effort, then? At least you could honor her memory in the process.

Auch: I never had an answer. Even now. But I have done nothing of note with my life.

Melisandre: How cruel. A precious gem does not become so on its own. It needs to be polished and cared for, not smashed into a thousand pieces.

Melisandre: Once you can do that, you will come to like the way you look, too. I am sure of it.

Auch: Well... I suppose it could not hurt to try.

Melisandre: That is more like it. As for my part, I cannot wait to see the new and improved you.

### Auch and Rolf

#### Rolf and Auch - A Chicken Spell

Auch: Behold, Rolf! A feat of transformative sorcery!

Rolf: You have been trying this spell on those chickens all day. We need them for dinner.

Auch: Precisely why success would be so useful. Yet even the swamp witches can manage shapeshifting more elegantly than I.

Rolf: You are already an accomplished sorcerer, Auch. You should take pride in that.

Auch: You truly think so?

Rolf: I do.

Auch: Then perhaps confidence is the missing component. Observe!

Rolf: Auch?

Auch: Cluck.

Rolf: You changed yourself into a chicken.

Auch: Cluck!

Rolf: Do not run toward Chloe. She is preparing dinner.

#### Rolf and Auch - Chess and Albion

Auch: If Albion's angels truly descend upon the battlefield, then one must consider the doctrinal ramifications as well as the tactical ones.

Rolf: I see.

Auch: You are listening?

Rolf: I trust your assessment. I may not be the best person to discuss it with, but I am listening.

Auch: Most people tire of me before I finish a sentence.

Rolf: You do have much to say.

Auch: And yet you find no fault in it.

Rolf: I did find one thing.

Auch: Oh?

Rolf: You are about to be checkmated.

Auch: I deserve this for taunting you.

#### Auch and Rolf - A Chicken Spell

Rolf: Are you almost done, Auch? I will be needing those chickens for dinner soon.

Auch: Just a few more moments, if you would. I have not quite perfected my shape-shifting spell.

Rolf: Yes?

Auch: Perhaps the art is better left to the witches of that accursed swamp instead.

Rolf: What do you mean?

Auch: From the moment they are born, they spend their entire lives surrounded by magick. Even children are capable of incredible spells.

Auch: Maybe then, my mother would have appreciated me for who I was.

Rolf: I cannot claim to understand how you feel, but there is little point in dwelling on hypotheticals.

Auch: You think I do not know that?

Rolf: Despite all the time you spend berating yourself, you are a rather accomplished sorcerer.

Rolf: All I ask is that you take pride in that. Recognize your skill, as I have come to do.

Auch: Hmph. You are far kinder than your miserable demeanor tends to suggest.

Rolf: I am sorry?

Auch: Now then, observe the triumph of my final attempt.

Auch: Hah!

Auch: Bawk!

Rolf: Incredible. It is nigh impossible to tell you apart from the other chickens.

Rolf: Is something wrong, Auch? Can you not change yourself back?

Auch: Bawk.

Rolf: I will have to find help. Another sorcerer, perhaps? Or maybe a chicken farmer?

Rolf: But if I leave him unattended, someone might carry him off to the kitchens by mistake.

Auch: Bawk! Bawk!

Rolf: Auch, wait! That is where Chloe is preparing dinner!

#### Auch and Rolf - Chess and Albion

Auch: All I have to do now is promote this pawn, and victory will be mine.

Rolf: You have carved through my defenses as though they were mere paper.

Auch: I could never lose a game of chess to a mere archer like you.

Rolf: Where to move next?

Auch: I have to say, the Liberation's march has led us some distance from our homes.

Auch: Never in my most fanciful dreams did I imagine we would see Albion.

Auch: Speaking of which, I had always thought angels to be exclusively young women. Yet there are men among them as well. Children, too, and even the elderly.

Auch: Though nothing confounds me quite like the large, muscular angels with their massive shields.

Auch: Perhaps it is a manner of levitation magick, endemic to the sacred shores of Albion. What do you think, Rolf?

Rolf: I trust your assessment, whatever it may be. Though I am not sure I am the right person to ask about such things.

Rolf: Your mind is constantly flooded with grand ideas, while I barely say a word in response. Do you never grow bored of such conversations?

Auch: Of course not. If anything, it makes my life easier.

Rolf: How so?

Auch: You never find fault in my words, for one, so I am free to say whatever thought crosses my mind. And you actually listen to what I have to say.

Rolf: I imagine few others could stomach your endless rambling.

Auch: What?

Rolf: By the way, you are about to get checkmated.

Auch: Do not be ridiculous. I... no. How is this possible?

Rolf: Now, what was that you said about losing to a mere archer?

Auch: I suppose this is what I deserve for taunting you.

### Auch and Selvie

#### Selvie and Auch - Ancient History

Selvie: Ah, the scholar Auch who once oversaw these ruins.

Auch: And you are Selvie, yes?

Selvie: I have heard that your mother was the only reason you ever took interest in ancient history to begin with.

Auch: Is there something wrong with that?

Selvie: Show me what it means to care for something beyond your own self-interest.

Auch: I am not sure I am qualified for that.

Selvie: Speak to me about your mother. If I can better understand how you truly feel about her, perhaps I can learn to take advantage of such emotions myself.

Auch: Strange. Most people simply grimace and walk off at my first mention of her, and certainly never ask to know more.

Selvie: Fascinating. Why is that, I wonder?

Auch: Under one condition. You have to listen to every word of it. No leaving partway through.

Selvie: I think I will be able to manage that.

### Auch and Yahna

#### Yahna and Auch - A Mother's Stew

Yahna: Auch, is this your notebook?

Auch: Do not read that!

Yahna: This recipe is from a remote part of Cornia.

Auch: My mother made it. I thought she invented it.

Yahna: I know the dish. One ingredient is difficult to find, but we can substitute another.

Auch: It is too sweet.

Yahna: Then we adjust it.

Auch: What if I forget how Mother's version tasted?

Yahna: A bowl of soup cannot wash memories away.

Auch: Then give me another bowl. For research.

Yahna: Of course. Research.

#### Auch and Yahna - A Mother's Stew

Auch: No, this is not right either. Why will you not work? What was it that she always used to put in here?

Yahna: What is all the grumbling for, Auch?

Auch: Hey! Get your hands off my notebook!

Yahna: A recipe, hm? Last I heard, they only eat this stew in the more remote regions of Cornia.

Auch: Local cuisine, then. I had always assumed my mother created the dish herself.

Yahna: Its key ingredient spoils rather quickly, but we should have a fitting substitute somewhere around here. Care to try it?

Auch: Why are you doing this, exactly? My culinary troubles should be no concern of yours.

Yahna: I only wanted to help a young sorcerer in need. Do not read too much into it.

Auch: I suppose we can test it out, just this once.

Auch: I would say it is close, but far too sweet.

Yahna: Hm, yes. It seems I will have to use a little less honey next time.

Auch: I cannot keep eating this. To be frank, I fear I will forget what my mother's version ever tasted like.

Yahna: Those must be powerful memories indeed, if a spoonful of soup is enough to wash them away.

Auch: You dare mock me? Bring it here. I will drink the entire bowl.

Yahna: Be my guest.

Yahna: He really is an arrogant child. Yet for some reason, I cannot resist helping him.

### Berengaria and Bruno

#### Berengaria and Bruno - The Old Crew

Berengaria: So, Bruno. I hear you took charge of the Tricorns after I left.

Berengaria: This might sound weird, but how's everyone doing?

Bruno: Things were tough for a while after you ditched us, but we kept it goin' pretty good.

Bruno: Least, 'til Zenoira got hold of me.

Berengaria: What do you mean?

Bruno: The bodies surroundin' me weren't our friends, but sorcerers and flyin' types.

Bruno: Figure everyone musta left when Zenoira got hold of me.

Berengaria: They probably weren't too happy about all the new blood you were bringing in.

Berengaria: That's probably what pushed them over the edge.

Bruno: What you're sayin' is, it's my fault ya don't have a gang to come back to.

Berengaria: I abandoned you, remember? Left you all out in the cold for nothing.

Berengaria: After what I've done, I don't have the right.

Berengaria: All the same... I'm glad to know you still want me around anyway.

Berengaria: You understand?

Bruno: Loud and clear.

#### Berengaria and Bruno - steel Butterflies

Bruno: Hey, boss. Ya gotta hear this.

Berengaria: What is it, Bruno? With that kind of excitement, I'd think you just saw a unicorn.

Bruno: It's even better than that. There's gonna be a feast tonight.

Bruno: Buncha our mercs are secretly hopin' to throw a party for Alain, not the other way 'round.

Berengaria: And I imagine they only told you on the condition you'd keep quiet about it?

Bruno: Well, sure. But what was I supposed to do, not tell ya?

Bruno: Anyway, I was thinkin' we could go on a little huntin' trip, just like we used to for all the Tricorn feasts.

Berengaria: Wait a second, Bruno. These mercs didn't happen to have any tattoos, did they?

Bruno: Now that ya mention it, they all did have some kinda cocoon-lookin' thing on their shoulder, yeah.

Berengaria: Bandits. The steel Butterflies.

Berengaria: Bring your axe, Bruno. Looks like we'll have that hunting trip after all.

Bruno: What about the party?

Berengaria: Sorry to break it to you, but there is no party. The bandits just told you that to keep you quiet.

Berengaria: Now come on. We don't have much time.

Berengaria: You did good back there, Bruno. If not for you, we'd all be face-down in a ditch right now.

Bruno: Shame about the feast, though. Was lookin' forward to throwin' back a few rounds together.

Berengaria: There's no reason we can't still do that. Grab us a bottle or two, will you?

Bruno: Now you're talkin' my language. I'll bring Travis too.

#### Bruno and Berengaria - The Old Crew

Berengaria: I heard you took charge of the Tricorns after I left.

Bruno: Someone had to.

Berengaria: How is everyone?

Bruno: Until Zenoira took us captive, they were alive. After the spell broke, the bodies around me were sorcerers and winged fighters. Not our friends.

Berengaria: Then they refused to follow the one controlling you.

Bruno: Maybe the new blood angered the old crew. Or maybe they just hated working for whatever bastard had his claws in me.

Berengaria: I abandoned them. I have no right to ask.

Bruno: Hold on, boss. You are here now.

Berengaria: And you still want me around?

Bruno: Aye. We all do.

#### Bruno and Berengaria - steel Butterflies

Bruno: The mercs are planning a feast for Alain. I was thinking of making it like the old Tricorn hunts.

Berengaria: Those men have markings.

Bruno: Markings?

Berengaria: A cocoon. steel Butterflies.

Bruno: Bandits, then.

Berengaria: And armed.

Bruno: There goes the feast.

Berengaria: We can still stop them.

Bruno: Right. I will get the axes.

Berengaria: And after that, grab a bottle or two. Bring Travis as well.

Bruno: Now that sounds like a feast.

### Berengaria and Gilbert

#### Berengaria and Gilbert - Baltro's Control

Gilbert: Ah, Berengaria. How are you feeling?

Berengaria: Sorry about all that. Better, thanks.

Gilbert: 'Tis no trouble in the slightest.

Gilbert: Though I must ask, why do you not stand by Travis, to comfort him in his time of need?

Berengaria: First, let me tell you what it was like getting put under that bastard Baltro's control.

Berengaria: And then, silence. No cares in the world, no worries, no pain.

Berengaria: It made me wonder if things weren't better off that way.

Gilbert: Hence you feel forever guilt for succumbing to its allure.

Berengaria: It was all nonsense, of course. And now that I have my body back, the only thought I've got left for Zenoira is hate.

Gilbert: Countless souls suffer under the weight of who others expect them to be. Myself included.

Berengaria: You understand, then.

Berengaria: After what I've done, Gilbert, I don't deserve to stroll back in like nothing happened.

Berengaria: I abandoned my own brother when he needed me most. Abandoned myself too.

Berengaria: Getting my revenge is just one small part of that.

Berengaria: Appreciate the concern, though.

Gilbert: Would that he could see it himself.

### Berengaria and Leah

#### Berengaria and Leah - Blue Birds

Leah: It was during a royal ball at Castle Soldraga ten long years ago.

Berengaria: That must have been you, hiding in the dark of his shadow.

Leah: A blue bird?

Berengaria: When I saw one with the prince, I took it as a sign that things'd turn out just fine.

Leah: If anything, I was more akin to a curse inflicted upon the late king for ever daring to shelter me.

Berengaria: Easy there. I meant what I said.

Berengaria: And while I'm not gonna pretend to know what the king saw in you, they're little more than a reminder that nothing comes without hard work.

Leah: Motivation, then, not a guarantee.

Berengaria: They're not idle wishes for peace, but a warning of what might happen if we don't strive to protect it.

Berengaria: I thought about my family. About a life of happiness, and how hard I'd have to fight to make it real.

Berengaria: Anyway, take care of that hair of yours.

### Berengaria and Travis

#### Berengaria and Travis - Scars

Travis: Ren? What are you thinking about?

Berengaria: Just thinking about some of these scars. Got more than I realized while Baltro had his hooks in me.

Berengaria: Though considering how long that lasted, I'm just glad I walked away with all my limbs.

Travis: Do they hurt? The scars, that is.

Berengaria: One does, sometimes.

Berengaria: The one I got dragging you down from that tree. You climbed all the way up, but got too scared to make it back to solid ground.

Travis: You're never gonna stop teasing me for that, are you? We were kids, Ren.

Berengaria: Yep, and we both ended up falling on our faces. I'm just glad you were okay.

Travis: Only because you shielded me from the impact. All our lives, you've put yourself in harm's way for me.

Berengaria: Taken my fair share of scars for it too. But you're always the one cleaning up my mess.

Travis: I knew you were gone forever, for all I knew.

Travis: And if you were, well, I'd never have forgiven you for leaving me. Or myself, for letting it happen.

Berengaria: I know an apology can't quite make up for what I did, but I'm sorry.

Berengaria: And hey, we promised we'd stick together from now on, right?

#### Berengaria and Travis - Nightmares

Travis: Like words mean anything to you. I know you'll just leave me again the first chance you get.

Berengaria: You planning on telling me what happened, or what?

Travis: I overheard some people talking about stealing your armor.

Travis: Turns out there's not much I can do against a pack of thieves.

Berengaria: Then why'd you even try? I could have handled them myself.

Berengaria: If anything, I'm the one who should've gotten hurt.

Travis: Well, maybe now you understand how I feel.

Berengaria: Don't tell me this was on purpose.

Travis: Nah, I'm not that eager to prove a point.

Travis: still, it doesn't feel good watching the only family you've got run themselves into the ground.

Travis: Does it, Ren?

Travis: It's like you're powerless. All you can do is let it happen.

Travis: If one of us is bound to get hurt, I'd much rather it be me.

Berengaria: Travis...

Berengaria: I never realized the pain I was putting you through.

Travis: If you really mean that, then stop.

Travis: Oh, and I'm sorry too. This wasn't how I wanted this conversation to go.

Berengaria: Damn it all.

Berengaria: I told myself I was doing this to protect him, but maybe it doesn't matter what I thought.

Berengaria: Looks like this is goodbye.

Travis: Wait, Ren. Please! I can't keep doing this alone.

Travis: Ah!

Berengaria: Haven't seen someone scream themselves awake in years.

Travis: Just a bad dream, is all. I thought you were leaving me again.

Berengaria: Oh, good. Now I'm giving you nightmares.

Travis: Heheh.

Berengaria: What's so funny?

Travis: I'd always dream about being in the Tricorns together, fighting side by side like nothing had ever happened.

Travis: Wished I could just live in my dreams, instead of alone on the outside.

Berengaria: I had no idea.

Travis: I'd take that over how it used to be, any day of the week.

Berengaria: Wait. Doesn't this mean you'll be having nightmares for the rest of your life?

Travis: Oh, um...

Berengaria: Can't say I envy that.

Berengaria: But it's like you said. Better that than the alternative.

Berengaria: Besides, how else am I gonna make sure you're staying out of trouble?

Travis: Thanks, Ren.

Travis: You have no idea how long I've waited to hear you say that.

#### Travis and Berengaria - Nightmare

Berengaria: Looks like this is goodbye.

Travis: Wait, Ren. Please! I can't keep doing this alone!

Travis: Ah!

Berengaria: You okay, Travis? Haven't seen someone scream themselves awake in years.

Travis: Just a bad dream, is all. I thought you were leaving me again.

Berengaria: Oh, good. Now I'm giving you nightmares.

Travis: Heheh.

Berengaria: What's so funny?

Travis: I'd always dream about being in the Tricorns together, fighting side by side like nothing had ever happened. I wished I could just live in my dreams instead of alone on the outside.

Berengaria: I had no idea.

Travis: I'd take that over how it used to be, any day of the week.

Berengaria: Wait. Doesn't this mean you'll be having nightmares for the rest of your life?

Travis: Oh, um...

Berengaria: Can't say I envy that. But it's like you said, better that than the alternative. Besides, how else am I gonna make sure you're staying out of trouble?

Travis: Thanks, Ren. You have no idea how long I've waited to hear you say that.

### Berengaria and Virginia

#### Berengaria and Virginia - Bandit Hunt

Virginia: stop right there!

Berengaria: Well, look who it is. Prince Gilbert's prized hostage.

Virginia: Do you really have to be so incessantly aggressive?

Berengaria: That's hilarious, coming from you. So, you need something?

Virginia: I want to know where you're skulking off to. You're not planning to sell us out to Zenoira, are you?

Berengaria: Good guess, princess, but no. Betraying the Liberation's not in my best interest.

Virginia: And if it were?

Berengaria: Heard there's some bandits making camp to the north of here. Thought I'd clear them out before it became a problem.

Virginia: What, that's it? Then let me join you.

Berengaria: Sorry, not what I meant. I'm just used to fighting alone, is all.

Virginia: Hmph. You dare imply I can't handle myself in battle?

Berengaria: That's not it. Our countries have got enough bad blood as it is, Virginia. Imagine how much worse it'd get if you died on my watch.

Virginia: I'm more than capable of pulling my weight against a lowly band of brigands.

Berengaria: Suit yourself.

Berengaria: If you insist on coming with, I need you to follow my orders down to the letter.

Berengaria: Think you can do that?

Virginia: You forget who you're dealing with. It won't be a problem.

Berengaria: Huh. Guess she's actually pretty reliable, so long as you can keep her reined in.

Virginia: What was that?

Berengaria: Oh, nothing. Now c'mon, we've got work to do.

### Berenice and Clive

#### Clive and Berenice

Berenice: Yeah, just keep walking if you know what's good for you.

Clive: Berenice! What's going on here?

Berenice: Oh, that? Just a little scuffle, is all.

Town Girl: Thank you, ma'am!

Clive: You stepped in to assist that girl. A noble deed, marred by a most ignoble methodology.

Berenice: You and I both know I've never been too big on tact.

Clive: Be that as it may, there are more means to solve an issue than with your fists.

Berenice: Black eyes and bruises are the only language a guy like that talks.

Clive: Perhaps so, yes.

Berenice: Can't promise it'll turn out any different, though.

Clive: Whatever shall I do with you, Berenice?

#### Berenice and Clive - The Knight She Was

Clive: At times I wonder, Berenice. How would matters stand now had you never been cast from our order?

Berenice: Quite a question, that.

Clive: Perhaps your life would not have been strewn across the nation like shattered glass.

Berenice: You think so?

Berenice: I remember Gailey. I told him he would get hand-picked for the royal guard in no time if he kept fighting like that.

Berenice: That was what he wanted, right? Queen Ilenia was all he ever talked about.

Gailey: Would it pain you to call me captain for once?

Knight of the Ashen Blue: They say Ilenia is letting Drakenhold practically walk all over us. We would never be that spineless if I were in charge.

Gailey: What was that about our queen? Say it again. I dare you.

Knight of the Ashen Blue: You want to fight? Ilenia's little lapdog sure has some bark today.

Berenice: Easy there, old man. Do you really want to throw away your shot at the royal guard over a pair of nothings?

Knight of the Ashen Blue: I was only speaking the truth. Now come here. I need payback for earlier.

Berenice: That is enough, you two. Take back what you said and we can all walk away happy.

Gailey: Wait!

Berenice: Too late.

Knight of the Ashen Blue: You are going to pay for that!

Gailey: If you are expecting me to thank you for that outburst, it will not happen.

Berenice: It turned out those two were up to some nasty stuff behind our backs.

Gailey: Then they certainly have no right to serve in her royal name.

Berenice: Fighting in the ranks probably gets me expelled, huh? Just like them.

Gailey: Such is the sentence, yes.

Berenice: A mercenary fits me better than a knight.

Clive: I attempted to appeal on your behalf, but there was only so much I could say, having not been present myself.

Clive: Not that it would have mattered. You never stopped insisting you had struck first.

Clive: If only you had told the truth, Berenice.

Berenice: Maybe I would have walked a different road, but all of them led right to the same spot.

Berenice: The old man would have done anything for Ilenia, and so would I.

#### Berenice and Clive - A Scuffle in Town

Rogue: I will not forget this!

Berenice: Keep walking if you know what is good for you.

Clive: Berenice! What is going on here?

Berenice: That? Just a little scuffle, is all.

Clive: You stepped in to assist that girl. A noble deed, marred by a most ignoble methodology.

Clive: Perhaps so, yes.

### Berenice and Jeremy

#### Berenice and Jeremy - The Gambling Den

Berenice: What? But you are...

Jeremy: Trust me, I could tell. Nobody bets like that if they have got their eye on actually winning.

Jeremy: Come on, do not be like that. I was just having a little fun.

Berenice: Fun? You were cheating and dragged me into your mess because of it.

Jeremy: Seems you should be thanking me, do you not think?

Berenice: If that is how you are going to do things here, you will be out on the streets before you know it. That is a promise.

Jeremy: Better looking after yourself than dying to help a guy like me.

Berenice: Well, look who is trying to be selfless.

Jeremy: And if you do not like the sound of that, you are better off leaving me behind.

Berenice: I do not mind letting the past stay in the past. Just know you will not get off easy if it happens again.

Jeremy: Whatever you say.

### Berenice and Kitra

Kitra: I would like that very much, Berenice.

Berenice: That is the spirit. Come on. I will have you stronger before you know it.

### Bertrand and Govil

#### Govil and Bertrand - Scars

**Govil:** Some scar you have got there, Bertrand.

**Bertrand:** I earned it back when Zenoira first invaded our lands.

**Govil:** Kinda hard to imagine how, with a shield as massive as yours.

**Bertrand:** No matter how large or sturdy a shield you hold, it may as well not exist if you cannot even make use of it. I was lucky to escape with my life. Or cursed, you could say.

**Bertrand:** Apologies if I frightened you.

**Govil:** That is not it. I am just surprised a guy as tough as you could get beat like that. Anyway, where is he now? I wanna get a good swing at him myself.

**Bertrand:** We had our revenge, yes, though we could do nothing to stem Zenoira's vile onslaught.

**Govil:** Same goes for my dream of avenging you.

**Bertrand:** That is why I am here, to make sure I never have to lose anyone else again.

**Govil:** Hold on. Did you just call me your friend?

**Bertrand:** We are fighting for the same army, bleeding the same blood.

**Govil:** Then I will try not to go running off too much.

#### Govil and Bertrand - The Tavern

**Govil:** Heh. Look at us, sharing drinks like a couple of old pals.

**Bertrand:** Though I cannot say I ever expected it. Unlike you, this is water I have, not alcohol.

**Govil:** Never met a guy who does not like his liquor, but do not worry. I will not push it. What are you thinking you will do once this war is all finished?

**Bertrand:** First, I plan to help my village rebuild. After that, I am not entirely sure.

**Govil:** Yep, that sounds like you. Me, I am gonna pick up where my grandpa left off before he died: running a tavern in one of the local towns.

**Bertrand:** I had no idea you had tradesman blood in your family.

**Govil:** Good news is, I will not even have to fix up the building. It is still standing just as tall as I remember it. It is not easy, but my grandpa taught me everything he knew back when the world was a bit calmer.

**Govil:** Just got one problem.

**Bertrand:** What is it?

**Govil:** The old man had some real trouble with thieves, too. Feel free to say no to this if you want, but what do you think about being my shield?

**Bertrand:** I would expect you are more than capable of handling such undertakings yourself.

**Govil:** You know this is me you are talking about, right? I start fights, not prevent them. But with a big guy like you keeping watch, nobody will even think about stealing from us. That solves the problem way better than my sword does, if you ask me. More peacefully, too.

**Bertrand:** I would not be guarding the tavern so much as the people who frequent it. And I could use something to motivate me once the war comes to a close. Very well, Govil. I will pay you a visit once my village is restored.

**Govil:** You will? Of course you will. I mean, yeah. I cannot wait.

### Bertrand and Ochlys

#### Ochlys and Bertrand - The Sky

**Ochlys:** Excuse the question, Bertrand, but I have noticed you gazing at the sky quite often of late. What is it you are hoping to catch a glimpse of?

**Bertrand:** In this holy nation, the great expanse is rife with angels such as yourself flying one way or the other. I cannot help but wonder if one of them may deliver my son from the heavens he now calls home.

**Ochlys:** I fear that only applies to those still among the living.

**Bertrand:** It is a boon I am truly grateful for.

**Ochlys:** Whatever must be done for the sake of victory, our Holiness Pontifex Arant, slain at the hand of those accursed Zenoirans...

**Ochlys:** Forgive me the outburst. Perhaps I could have taken to the sky myself, swept him to safety before it was too late. But I suppose such fantasy only exists in the pages of faerie tales.

**Bertrand:** And my shield is the steadfast wall to ensure none will suffer our agony again.

**Ochlys:** Mine as well.

### Bertrand and Yunifi

#### Yunifi and Bertrand - Battle Strategies

**Yunifi:** Hey, Bertrand! Want to hear some new battle strategies I have been working on? You have been doing this whole war thing for years now, so I thought maybe you would have some good insight.

**Bertrand:** I would be glad to. An elder like me could never turn down the opportunity to instruct his younger generations.

**Yunifi:** Maybe if we just threw some water on the enemy, they would get frozen in place and would not be able to move.

**Bertrand:** I fear preventing the water from freezing before battle will prove far too difficult a task.

**Yunifi:** Huh. You are right. And there is no point just carrying around buckets of ice.

**Bertrand:** If you wish to freeze our enemies, it would be much more realistic to do so using a sorcerer's ice magick.

**Yunifi:** Good point. No buckets weighing us down that way, too.

**Yunifi:** Then why don't we just slip a scrap of our clothes into their pocket and follow the scent all the way back?

**Bertrand:** Another fascinating tactic.

**Yunifi:** Is it not? I got the idea from a book I was reading, though that was actually about dogs tracking smells, not bestrals.

**Bertrand:** Trying to use it against an enemy with noses as keen as ours would only risk our own safety in return.

**Yunifi:** Urgh. This strategy stuff is impossible.

**Bertrand:** More than anything, I think it is truly amazing just how much thought you have put into this.

**Yunifi:** You mind if we do this again once I think of more ideas?

**Bertrand:** Of course. I will be here any time you need me.

### Bruno and Bryce

#### Bruno and Bryce - Cargo Race

Bryce: How's the cargo looking there, Bruno?

Bryce: Seems like a lot for just one guy. Here, let me give you a hand.

Bruno: Nah, I'm good. I can carry this stuff in my sleep and still have room left for dreamin'.

Bryce: Maybe, but it'll still take you all day if you do it alone. Now let me-

Bruno: I said no. This here's my job, and dammit, I'm gonna do it.

Bryce: Look, you can still-

Bruno: Fine. If you're not gonna listen, I'll hafta work so fast ya can't even lay a finger on 'em.

Bryce: A race, is it? Not a bad idea.

Bruno: Alain said I'd get a triple servin' at dinner for this, and now some rat keeps cuttin' into my earnin's.

Bryce: Just one box left, huh?

Bruno: Hands off, it's mine.

Bryce: Oh, quit your complaining. Why don't we just carry it together?

Bruno: Like hell that's gonna happen. I'm done takin' your damn help.

Bryce: C'mon, Bruno. What good are friends for if we don't come running for stuff like this?

Bruno: So tired...

Bryce: Can't believe we managed to move all that before noon.

Bryce: Though, it wasn't really a "we" operation. You must've carried three times as much as I did.

#### Bruno and Bryce - Cargo Race

Bryce: Need a hand with that cargo?

Bruno: No. Alain promised me a triple serving at dinner if I hauled it myself.

Bryce: Then I should help. We can finish faster.

Bruno: That defeats the point.

Bryce: Then let us make it a contest.

Bruno: Now you are talking.

Bryce: How did you carry that much?

Bruno: Hunger.

Alain: What happened to the cargo?

Bruno: It arrived. Mostly.

### Bruno and Selvie

#### Bruno and Selvie - Anatomical Interest

Bruno: Evenin', Selvie. What're ya thinkin' about over there?

Selvie: But alas, this incessant rubble seems determined to bar my path.

Bruno: What, that? Lemme try helpin'.

Bruno: Just gotta move a few things, and done.

Bruno: If ya wanna pay me back, a nice bottle o' ale'll do just fine. Sorry, what're ya starin' at me like that for?

Selvie: The beauty of your form has me rather entranced, frankly.

Bruno: Well, thanks. This is what ya get when ya put in years o' hard work.

Selvie: According to the tomes I've read on human anatomy, I'm particularly drawn to the shape of your trapezius, I believe it's called.

Selvie: Though the contours of your external oblique and infraspinatus muscles are quite fetching as well.

Bruno: Heh. If ya say so.

Selvie: But nothing compares to your sturdy flexor carpi radialis. Why, I can feel my scientific interest piqued just looking at it.

Bruno: Uh, weren't you gonna go studyin' these ruins or somethin'?

Selvie: Ah, yes. I fear I grew a little distracted for a moment there.

Bruno: Ya sure did. Now let's talk about a reward, yeah?

Selvie: Wait, Bruno. Your serratus anterior and your latissimus dorsi just moved in the most perfect harmony.

Bruno: Y'know what, forget the reward. I'm outta here.

Selvie: And what a majestic gluteus maximus. Truly a fascinating specimen.

#### Bruno and Selvie - Anatomical Interest

Selvie: This rubble is blocking the path.

Bruno: stand back.

Selvie: Impressive.

Bruno: That worth a cup of ale?

Selvie: External oblique, infraspinatus, flexor carpi radialis...

Bruno: What?

Selvie: Serratus anterior, latissimus dorsi, gluteus maximus. Fascinating.

Bruno: I am leaving.

Selvie: But I have not finished observing.

Bruno: Keep the ale.

### Bruno and Sharon

#### Bruno and Sharon - The Injured Cat

Sharon: Another fine morning, blessed by the Father's divine grace.

Sharon: I think a short rest is in order to celebrate the occasion. Perhaps on that boulder over there?

Sharon: Ah... How lovely.

Bruno: The hell do ya think you're doin'?

Sharon: My word. Did the boulder just speak to me?

Bruno: Who're you callin' a boulder?

Sharon: Is that Bruno? Wait, you...

Bruno: 'Course it is. But I get the feelin' ya thought otherwise.

Sharon: What? No, I would never confuse your muscular back for mere stone.

Sharon: Well, I suppose there's no point attempting to hide it. Forgive me for leaning on you.

Bruno: Eh, it's fine. It was kinda my fault too, for crouchin' down like that.

Bruno: Sorry for scarin' ya, Sharon.

Sharon: And what were you doing over there, if you don't mind me asking?

Bruno: I found a cat, okay? Poor thing was hurtin' real bad, so I figured I'd try to fix him up.

Sharon: With my help, your friend here will be back on his paws in no time.

Bruno: I, uh... yeah. Go right ahead.

Sharon: Thank you, Bruno. It'll just be a minute.

Bruno: Is he gonna be okay, Sharon?

#### Bruno and Sharon - The Goat

Bruno: Well, I was makin' my way over to...

Bruno: That's when I caught sight of that goat gettin' mauled by a wolf.

Bruno: So I grabbed the goat and ran as fast as I could. Kept him safe while those wolves were bitin' at my legs.

Bruno: 'Course, who knows what'll happen to him once he's back out in the wild.

Bruno: But at least for today, he's okay.

Sharon: Then let me make certain you are okay as well.

#### Sharon and Bruno - The Injured Cat

Sharon: Why is there a boulder in the road?

Bruno: I am not a boulder.

Sharon: Bruno?

Bruno: Quiet. There is an injured cat here.

Sharon: Let me see.

Bruno: Can you heal it?

Sharon: I can. Hold still.

Bruno: Me or the cat?

Sharon: Both.

#### Sharon and Bruno - The Goat

Sharon: Bruno, you are injured.

Bruno: Wolves came after a goat. I got in the way.

Sharon: You should worry about yourself first.

Bruno: Will the goat be okay?

Sharon: Yes. And so will you, if you let me treat that wound.

Bruno: Good. At least for today, it is okay.

Sharon: And so are you.

### Bruno and Travis

#### Bruno and Travis - Firewood

Travis: That's some good chopping you're doing there, big guy.

Bruno: If you're here to make fun of me, ya can go straight to hell.

Travis: Easy. I know how much you hate this kind of busywork.

Bruno: I'll take that kinda trainin' any day.

Bruno: Ya got somethin' to say to me?

Travis: Not really. Though if you're gonna sneak food from the stores, maybe try not to get caught next time.

Bruno: Put that book down for a sec and let's have ourselves a good old-fashioned fistfight, yeah?

Travis: I don't know. You're not so good at pulling your punches, Bruno.

Bruno: Like that matters. I barely ever hit ya.

Travis: I guess those swings of yours are pretty easy to dodge.

Bruno: Think how good it'll feel when I finally land one, though.

Travis: That's not quite my idea of fun.

Bruno: Oh, you wouldn't know fun if it smacked ya 'cross the face.

Bruno: Maybe I'll go ask Alain instead. He'll spar with me.

Travis: I've got an idea. Why don't you read a book?

Bruno: Just lookin' at the thing makes my damn head hurt.

Travis: That's exactly what all the other Tricorns used to say, too.

Bruno: If it's not sharp and pointy, we're not interested.

#### Travis and Bruno - Books and Fistfights

Bruno: Put that book down for a sec and let's have ourselves a good ol' fashioned fistfight, yeah?

Travis: I don't know. You're not so good at pulling your punches, Bruno.

Bruno: Like that matters. I barely ever hit ya!

Travis: Guess those swings of yours are pretty easy to dodge.

Bruno: Think how good it'll feel when I finally land one, though!

Travis: That's not quite my idea of fun.

Bruno: Oh, you wouldn't know fun if it smacked ya across the face. Maybe I'll go ask Alain instead. He'll spar with me.

Travis: I've got an idea. Why don't you read a book?

Bruno: Ya mean with all them wiggly little letters and stuff? Just lookin' at the thing makes my damn head hurt.

Travis: That's exactly what all the other Tricorns used to say, too.

Bruno: If it's not sharp n' pointy, we're not interested.

#### Bruno and Travis - After the War

Travis: You okay there, big guy? It's weird seeing you lost in thought like that.

Bruno: What're ya gonna do once this war's done with?

Travis: straight into the heavy questions, huh?

Travis: Maybe Alain'll bring me on as his personal scout or something.

Bruno: But if we can get the whole world talkin' about us again, they just might.

Travis: Hm.

Bruno: Though no way I'm convincin' the boss with you outta the picture.

Travis: So what, you're planning on getting the gang back together all by yourself?

Travis: Pretty good joke, that.

Bruno: What'd you say?

Travis: Which was always my job, of course.

Travis: And it's like I said before. Those days spent playing the fool were some of the happiest I've ever known.

Bruno: What're ya gettin' at?

Travis: I'll convince Ren too, one way or another.

Bruno: Heh. Ya mean you knew I'd come around.

Travis: But let's focus on ending this war first, okay?

Bruno: Anythin' ya say, Travis.

Bruno: C'mon. We got an empire to stomp.

#### Bruno and Travis - Firewood

Travis: You are chopping enough wood for three camps.

Bruno: Gives the arms something to do.

Travis: You could rest once in a while.

Bruno: So could you. Yet here you are watching me like I will fall over if you blink.

Travis: Old habits.

Bruno: Then get a new one. Pick up an axe.

Travis: Fine, fine. But I am taking the smaller one.

#### Bruno and Travis - Books and Fists

Travis: You ever consider reading something that is not a wanted poster?

Bruno: You ever consider solving an argument without that mouth of yours?

Travis: That is what makes it an argument.

Bruno: Hah. I missed this.

Travis: Missed me annoying you?

Bruno: Missed having someone worth punching after.

Travis: I will take that as affection.

#### Bruno and Travis - After the War

Bruno: When this is over, what happens to the Tricorns?

Travis: We see who is left standing, then decide.

Bruno: Sounds like you.

Travis: You have an idea?

Bruno: Maybe we keep helping people. Maybe we find work that does not start with theft and end with a tavern brawl.

Travis: Ambitious.

Bruno: Coming from you, that hurts.

### Bryce and Fodoquia

#### Fodoquia and Bryce - A Family Technique

**Fodoquia:** Hmph. A mere thief, training as though he were a true soldier? Ridiculous.

**Bryce:** You got that right, but I am part of the Liberation, same as you. Have to do whatever it takes to prove I am worth keeping around.

**Fodoquia:** What admirable mentality. It would seem I will have to revise my assessment of you.

**Bryce:** No need. You were right, you know. Now just do me a favor and leave me to it, yeah?

**Fodoquia:** Apologies, but I will not acquiesce so easily. Perhaps I could teach you an old family technique to offset my earlier incivility.

**Bryce:** Now you are talking my language.

**Fodoquia:** Heed well. Now, bear witness to the Radiant Light Which Shelters All!

**Bryce:** That is not seriously what it is called, is it? Holy...

**Fodoquia:** Well? With such a technique amidst your arsenal, none shall ever harm you or your allies again.

**Bryce:** Yeah, I dunno. I felt like I was about to pass out just watching you.

**Fodoquia:** From but a moment's use? Yet true mastery can only come after half an hour of uninterrupted practice.

**Fodoquia:** Ngh. Perhaps I have grown weak behind the invulnerable walls of Peyston.

**Bryce:** Maybe you are better off just letting people fend for themselves, then. They really cannot attack while you are fluttering around them.

**Fodoquia:** Hmph. I will show you.

### Bryce and Nina

#### Nina and Bryce - A Sandwich

Bryce: Hey there, Nina. You been doing okay?

Nina: Captain Bryce.

Bryce: Easy there. I am just a regular soldier, same as you.

Bryce: Life sure is a funny thing. Now here we are, both flying the Liberation flag.

Nina: It is an honor to stand beside you once more.

Nina: Are the others doing all right?

Bryce: If all this snow did not break their spirits, nothing will.

Nina: I suppose you are right.

Bryce: Almost forgot. I brought you something.

Nina: What is it?

Bryce: Nothing special. Just some meat and egg shoved between two halves of bread.

Nina: How have I never heard of this before?

Bryce: Guess I never got the chance to make you one. Go on, eat.

Nina: Hold a moment. You want me to eat it here? With my hands?

Bryce: I know you are more of a knife and fork girl, but sometimes you have just got to sink your teeth into a good sandwich.

Nina: Here goes nothing.

Nina: The oozing yolk, the tender meat, and slightly sweet bread. It is simple, yet...

Bryce: The guy was real nice about sharing his recipes.

Nina: I will have to compliment him the next time I see him.

Bryce: Slow down, kid. You are going to choke if you keep talking with your mouth full like that.

Nina: I cannot breathe.

Bryce: I have got you, Nina. Just one push.

#### Nina and Bryce - The Knight

Nina: Unhand her this instant!

Kidnapper: Rgh!

Girl: Thank you for saving me, brave knight.

Nina: Knight? But I am not...

Nina: The blackguard would have succeeded if not for a valiant knight who rode up to fight him off.

Bryce: Glad he did.

Nina: Mille, always the more adaptable of us, quickly grew close to our new stepmother.

Nina: Yet no amount of kindness could ever replace our mother.

Bryce: So that is why you ran. Found yourself throwing in with the Rock Rats.

Nina: More or less, yes.

Nina: In any case, I think that is quite enough for now. We should return to camp and make ready for our next battle.

Bryce: Suppose we should.

#### Nina and Bryce - The Rock Rats Name

Nina: I have been wondering, Captain. Where did you come up with the name "Rock Rats"?

Bryce: Makes sense you never heard.

Bryce: There is an old saying. "Cling to life with all the tenacity of a wounded rat." Sounds just like us, right?

Bryce: A long time ago, there was a family over in Drakenhold. One day, a noble in town had his house picked clean by thieves.

Bryce: His wife, racked with grief for her lost love, tried to end it all. Kill herself and her son, too.

Bryce: But the kid made it out. He went from town to town and clung to life with all the tenacity of a wounded rat.

Bryce: He could never get over his hatred for nobility, though.

Nina: Captain...

Bryce: It was greed, plain and simple. If you did not want to be taken advantage of, you had to get stronger.

Bryce: Makes it a fitting moniker for a band of thieves who ply the same trade.

Nina: But I am nobility. Daughter of a Cornian lord.

Bryce: I already knew. It was obvious.

Nina: Then why did you permit me to join? I thought you hated nobles like me.

Bryce: We are both out here trying to protect those who cannot lift a sword for themselves. That is good enough for me.

Bryce: Anyway, I did not mean to give you my whole life story. Come on. Last I checked, you are on cooking duty tonight.

### Celeste and Fran

#### Fran and Celeste - Laundry Trouble

Celeste: Fran? What seems to be the matter?

Fran: Everything is soaked. Even if I wash it all again, our clothes will never be dry by the time we set off from camp.

Celeste: That is some afternoon, yes.

Celeste: We can have our gryphons fan the heat across the clothes. They will be dry before you know it.

Fran: I am not sure my luck can handle fire today. Honestly, we would be more likely to torch the entire garrison.

Celeste: The others might lend a hand if they see how hard we are working here.

Fran: You would really do that for me?

Celeste: Of course. I have been hoping the four of us could become friends someday anyway, so let us get to work.

### Celeste and Gammel

#### Gammel and Celeste - Pride

**Gammel:** Only things I have ever been good for are stealin' and murderin'. But here I am, fightin' some kinda righteous war, hopin' to save the whole damn world. I would have lost everything: my sister, my life, and myself. But here I am, alive and breathin'.

**Gammel:** I bet we can do the same for that friend of yours, too.

**Celeste:** And I am glad I was able to help your sister. I just pray...

**Gammel:** Hey, this is no time for beggin' the Father. We will find him.

**Celeste:** So we will. Thank you, Gammel. It was good to see you. Take care of yourself, okay?

**Celeste:** I never would have expected my friend once worked for you. You have given me more than I ever could have asked for, Gammel. My friend said you were some leader, by the sounds of it.

**Celeste:** He said you would always divide up the spoils so that none of the younger thieves would get cheated out of their fair share, and that you would always lure away the guards whenever a job was getting too dangerous.

**Celeste:** You saved their lives so many times, Gammel, and I could not be more thankful that you did. So please, stop demeaning yourself like this.

**Celeste:** Do you want to know what I think? I think you need to be a little prouder of what you have accomplished. "I, Gammel, am proud to have saved Celeste's friend."

**Gammel:** Well, all right then. I, Gammel, am proud...

**Celeste:** Proud of what, exactly?

**Gammel:** To have saved Celeste's friend.

**Celeste:** That was not so hard, now was it?

### Celeste and Mandrin

#### Mandrin and Celeste - Pheasants

**Celeste:** What lovely birds.

**Mandrin:** Sorry, you say something?

**Celeste:** Oh, just admiring the pheasants. They look absolutely delectable.

**Mandrin:** Don't tell me you forgot to eat breakfast again.

**Celeste:** It is forbidden to even hunt birds, let alone eat them.

**Mandrin:** Guess there is no ignoring tradition, huh? Good news is, we are nowhere near your home, so how about you go shoot a few of them down for us?

**Celeste:** You would really do that?

**Mandrin:** Besides, now my mind is set on pheasant stew for dinner.

**Celeste:** Oh, perfect. Just let me get closer first so I can catch any of the ones you hit.

**Mandrin:** You outta your damn mind? That is right where I'm aiming.

**Celeste:** Let us just hope you hit the right bird, then.

#### Mandrin and Celeste - Acting Harsh

**Celeste:** stop right there, vile rogue! Did you forget we agreed to stroll through the woods today?

**Mandrin:** Uh...

**Celeste:** Sorry. I think that might have been a bit too much.

**Mandrin:** Don't worry about it. But I have gotta ask, why are you talking like that damn angel does?

**Celeste:** I thought maybe her irritability was the key to that friendship somehow.

**Mandrin:** First off, me and that angel aren't friends. Not even close. Would not be surprised if she was around here now, ready to put a sword in my back at any moment.

**Mandrin:** Things go sideways, you might end up fighting for real.

**Celeste:** Hm. I guess there are just some things you should not say to people.

**Mandrin:** And for what it is worth, I think we are friends enough as it is. No changes needed.

**Celeste:** Oh. In that case, I will treat you just the same as I did before?

**Mandrin:** Appreciate it. Now, what was that about a stroll?

**Celeste:** Well, let us just forget it, okay? This whole situation has gotten a bit too embarrassing for my liking.

**Mandrin:** Nice try, but no take-backs. Come on, out with it.

**Celeste:** Urgh. Who is being the mean one now?

### Chloe and Clive

#### Chloe and Clive - Shopping

Clive: I must say, Chloe, it always pains me to see you burdened by dinner preparations. I may not have much skill in the art of cookery, yet I would love to aid you in procuring ingredients, if that's all right.

Chloe: Though I have to wonder, how often have you actually bought food for yourself?

Clive: Tell me, do you fear I would impede your work rather than expedite it?

Chloe: Oh, not at all. Now come, let's work on your shopping list.

Clive: Forgive me the wait, my lady. I've purchased everything you requested.

Chloe: Erm, Clive? What's in the giant saddlebag?

Clive: I performed my own calculations based on the recipe you provided, and believe this should be a sufficient amount.

Chloe: Sufficient for the next ten years, maybe.

Clive: I've bought too much, you mean? Ah, 'tis a failure which brings shame to the very notion of knighthood.

Chloe: Here, why don't we get the next set of ingredients together?

Clive: Thank you for the kindness, Chloe. And I promise, I'll not fail you again.

### Chloe and Hodrick

#### Chloe and Hodrick - Garlic

Chloe: With all this, I could do what I did two days ago... no.

Hodrick: Is something wrong?

Chloe: There are only so many ingredients we can keep around in wartime, but I'd still like to include some variety if I can.

Hodrick: After all, your cooking is one of the few respites we have from the ceaseless toils of this brutal war.

Chloe: And I'm honored to help, truly. If only I had a new ingredient to work with.

Hodrick: Now that you mention it, I have heard tell of garlic being grown in the nearby town.

Chloe: Oh, we haven't had garlic in ages! That's sure to provide a different enough flavor, even if everything else stays the same.

Hodrick: In that case, wait right here. I'll fetch some.

Chloe: I couldn't dare ask that of you, ser.

Hodrick: Please, 'tis no trouble at all. I happen to love garlic myself, so I'll be looking forward to tonight's dinner even more than usual.

Chloe: I can't tell if he really loves it, or if he's just being nice.

### Chloe and Josef

#### Josef and Chloe

Josef: I believe it best that we investigate, my prince, to be truly certain, if nothing else. It shall be done, Your Highness.

Josef: Might I help you with something, Chloe? You seem to have been studying our conversation with some intrigue.

Josef: I hardly consider our appearances comparable. I can't say I've noticed such parallels. Indeed, I've endeavored to guide him in every manner possible these past ten years. Should that be the case, I pray he's not inherited my flaws as well.

Josef: I should think you'd have more important things to focus on amidst our war councils. Forgive me, Chloe. 'Twas merely a joke. Take it as a symbol of trust, if you wish. But do be careful not to grow complacent in our councils, hm?

#### Chloe and Josef - Training

Chloe: Oh, Ser Josef. I was so pleased the day my father gave me one. I even cradled it in my sleep.

Chloe: I appreciate that, ser, but I do not believe it for a second. Not as one of his many subjects, but as his friend.

Chloe: I cannot ride a horse into battle, and I do not have the strength to carry a greatshield.

Chloe: After all, I cannot just sit back and watch while His Majesty gets hurt.

Chloe: I cannot turn defense into attack with the same fluidity that you do.

Chloe: And for all my obstinance, I am not sure I will ever have what it takes to really be there for His Majesty.

Josef: If you wish it, I would be more than glad to convey the knowledge I have mustered over my many years of knighthood.

Josef: Beyond certain. Now then, let us learn how deep this loyalty of yours runs.

### Chloe and Lex

#### Lex and Chloe - Rations

Chloe: Can I ask you something, Lex? Why do you only sneak food out when I'm on cooking duty?

Lex: We never have enough for seconds, so this is my one shot at getting a few extra bites in.

Chloe: Well, maybe we would have enough if someone wasn't stealing rations before we even sat at the table.

Lex: Oh. I, uh, never thought about it like that.

Chloe: And while I'm glad you think I'm a good cook...

Lex: I really do mean it, though. I don't know what we'd do without you!

Chloe: You didn't let me finish. What I was going to say is, all the flattery in the world doesn't excuse theft.

Lex: Listen, I'm sorry, all right?

Chloe: Then help me prepare meals. And in return, I'll look the other way while you sneak a couple early bites.

Lex: Works for me. Mm, so good.

Chloe: That's far more than a couple bites!

Lex: Urp, sorry!

#### Lex and Chloe - Formality

Lex: Dammit! I don't think I'm ever gonna beat Alain at this rate. Times like these call for a bit of stress eating, though. You got anything good for me, Chloe?

Chloe: You never learn, do you?

Lex: What're you talking about?

Chloe: Your behavior toward His Majesty. Can't you try being at least somewhat formal with him?

Lex: Look, I know you really focus on getting that stuff right. But I dunno. I think I'd rather just keep doing things the same way I always have.

Chloe: If you speak to him like that after he's ascended the throne, you could easily find yourself tossed in gaol, or worse.

Lex: It's already sad enough seeing how much Alain's changed since we were kids, y'know? But I'm glad you're still the same as ever, Chloe. Kinda relieved, to be honest.

Chloe: Lex, I...

Lex: If you ask me, I'm better off not doing a damn thing different. Oh, and don't you go changing on me either, Chloe. I wanna keep our friendship just the way it is.

Lex: By the way, what'd I come here for again?

Chloe: You were looking for a snack after His Majesty bested you, remember? Here, there's plenty of leftover bread you can have.

Lex: Oh yeah! Totally forgot about that.

Chloe: I doubt I'd like it very much if you started being all formal out of the blue.

Lex: Now you're talking! I'd hate it too.

### Chloe and Ridiel

#### Ridiel and Chloe - Training Too Hard

Chloe: still training, Ridiel? It is getting late.

Ridiel: It is the only way I can make up for selling you out to Zenoira.

Chloe: That does not mean you need to work yourself to the bone.

Ridiel: I do not remember asking your opinion.

Chloe: I am surprised you can even hold your bow through all the pain.

Ridiel: I do not have a choice. You know that just as well as I do.

Chloe: You are wrong, Ridiel.

Chloe: The only thing that would prove is that he cannot trust you to be there when he needs you.

Ridiel: But...

Chloe: Take it slow, okay? You will get there, even if it is not as fast as you might want.

Ridiel: Now that you mention it, I guess I was getting a little impatient.

Chloe: Here. Put some balm on your hands. And I had better not catch you training like this again.

Ridiel: I will not let you down. I promise.

#### Ridiel and Chloe - Cooking

Chloe: You really never stop improving, Ridiel.

Ridiel: I appreciate that. Here, I will not be needing this balm anymore.

Chloe: Let me see your hands. It must have taken weeks to get to that point.

Chloe: I cannot say I am surprised. Nor would your mom be, I am sure.

Ridiel: I still have a long way to go until I get there.

Chloe: She must have really been special, huh?

Ridiel: She was amazing, at least at most things.

Chloe: What did she struggle with?

Ridiel: Cooking. I never ended up doing it much myself because of that.

Chloe: That explains why you always disappear when we need help with dinner.

Ridiel: I have been thinking maybe you could teach me.

Chloe: I would love to. Come on.

Chloe: Besides, I am sure you are starving after all that archery, so let us get going already.

Ridiel: Hey, stop pulling.

Ridiel: I guess I am just not meant for this stuff.

Chloe: Cooking is no different from training. If you want to get better, you have to keep practicing.

Chloe: Just so you know, everyone loved the dish you made.

Ridiel: They did? Then I will not give up on this. I promise you that.

Chloe: Glad to hear it.

#### Ridiel and Chloe - Ending

Ridiel: I always thought she was a fool for falling in love with a human.

Ridiel: But here I have done just that, and it is all your fault.

Ridiel: Oh, wipe that smile off your face.

Ridiel: I would love to find a little something for my friends back in Elheim. Any ideas, Chloe?

Chloe: Maybe a honey apple? They are almost impossible to get anywhere else, and they are delicious too.

### Chloe and Rolf

#### Chloe and Rolf

Rolf: It's grown late, Chloe.

Chloe: I mean, it was quick enough liberating that town, but I never thought they would throw us a feast afterward.

Rolf: Fair enough point. The food was rather impressive as well, yet I worry the snack I prepared this morning will have to be thrown away.

Chloe: So that's what you were doing crouched around the fire. What was it you made?

Rolf: Roasted yams. Not only are they delicious, but they give me all the energy I need to endure through the day.

Chloe: Although, it might not be the best idea to have a whole snack right before dinner.

Rolf: Perhaps we can share them, then. Better that than let them go to waste.

Chloe: Well, as long as you're sure. Is something wrong? Oh. I don't think we can eat those.

Rolf: Forgive me for allowing your yams to spoil in such a careless manner.

Chloe: How about next time we cool them off first? Or maybe we can forage for food after our assignment instead of before.

Rolf: Indeed.

Chloe: Is that really all you have to say to me? Come on, cheer up already.

#### Rolf and Chloe - Roasted Yams

Chloe: Rolf, it is almost dinner. Why are you still carrying those roasted yams?

Rolf: I was saving them as a snack, but I fear they may spoil if I wait until morning.

Chloe: A whole snack before dinner is a bit much. Why do we not share them?

Rolf: A fine idea.

Chloe: Oh. They have already gone bad.

Rolf: My apologies. I should have thought of this sooner.

Chloe: Next time, let them cool before you pack them away. Or we can forage after the assignment and eat them fresh.

Rolf: Thank you, Chloe. I will remember that.

### Chloe and Scarlett

#### Scarlett and Chloe

Chloe: It's gorgeous, isn't it? I almost forget we're at war, staring out at the water like this.

Scarlett: Me too.

Chloe: It's been too long since we've had the chance to breathe, you know?

Scarlett: It has.

Chloe: Listen, Scarlett. You don't need to spend the entire time pouting just because His Majesty declined your invitation.

Scarlett: That's not...

Chloe: Would you like me to yell at him for you?

Scarlett: You don't need to do that, Chloe. Though I do appreciate the offer.

Chloe: Understandably so. Things are nothing like how they used to be on Palevia.

Scarlett: Life was so easy then. So fun. But now here he is, marching us on to a brighter future, while I'm struggling just to follow in his wake.

Chloe: And one of these days, His Majesty is going to realize that.

Scarlett: If we're talking beauty, I think you have me beat, Chloe.

Chloe: Huh? Anyway, care to eat something? I packed a nice, big lunch for us before we left.

Scarlett: That would be lovely!

#### Scarlett and Chloe

Chloe: Wow. So this is the Valleyshallow, huh?

Scarlett: Just as I remember it from all those years ago, yes.

Chloe: Did you spend a lot of time here? When you were young, I mean.

Scarlett: And in the summer months, we'd leap from the balustrade and cool ourselves down in the river.

Chloe: I can picture it now, plain as day.

Scarlett: Chloe?

Chloe: When I first found out you were the pontifex's daughter, it came as a real shock, you know.

Scarlett: I'm sorry for keeping it from you.

Chloe: I don't think I would have told anyone either, if I was in your position. But it still hurts, knowing I was oblivious to such an important part of you. That's not the kind of friend I want to be.

Scarlett: I didn't realize you were so taken with me, Chloe.

Chloe: This isn't a joke!

Scarlett: Sorry, I couldn't help it. And I really am happy to hear you say that.

Chloe: Then maybe you can tell me some more about your life here in Albion.

Scarlett: I'd be glad to.

Chloe: Good. Now come with me.

Scarlett: Hm? Where to?

Chloe: I was thinking you could share those stories of yours over a little snack on the bridge.

Scarlett: That sounds perfect, Chloe. Just when I was getting hungry, too!

Chloe: I knew you'd say that.

Scarlett: Am I really that predictable?

### Chloe and Travis

#### Chloe and Travis

Chloe: Travis? Oh, sorry. I didn't realize you were reading there.

Travis: It's more than all right. Did you need something?

Chloe: I did, but... is that a new book you have? I can't say I recognize the cover.

Travis: I can't exactly haul a library around, though, so I always end up selling my old books to fund the new purchases.

Chloe: My sister never parts ways with a book herself, even if she doesn't have room on the shelf for it.

Travis: Heh. Once the war's over, maybe I can start actually building a collection again.

Chloe: I didn't realize they were that important to you, Travis.

Travis: Anyway, what was it you wanted to talk about?

Chloe: Oh, right. Dinner will be ready any minute now.

Travis: Perfect, thanks. Just let me finish this chapter, and I'll be right there.

### Chloe and Yahna

#### Chloe and Yahna

Yahna: Hm. This is quite a quandary.

Chloe: What's wrong, Yahna?

Yahna: Here I am, stuck with an outfit I can't wear, and no one to give it to.

Chloe: In that case, do you mind if I take a look?

Yahna: Be my guest. You can even try it on if you'd like.

Chloe: Maybe I can be just as charming and mature as she is. Oh... I'm not sure if size can really be an issue when there's barely any clothing here to begin with.

Yahna: A slender girl like you should have no problem with that. Go on, try it.

Chloe: If you say so.

Lex: Don't do this, Chloe! There are some things the world's not meant to see!

Chloe: What's that supposed to mean?

Chloe: You too, Scarlett?

#### Yahna and Chloe - A New Outfit

Chloe: Yahna, have you ever thought of trying a different outfit?

Yahna: Many have thought about my outfit on my behalf.

Chloe: I only mean something warmer. Or sturdier.

Yahna: You are kind to worry. But a witch knows what she is comfortable casting in.

Chloe: Then maybe just a cloak?

Yahna: That I might accept.

### Clive and Hodrick

#### Hodrick and Clive

Hodrick: Your spear work is excellent, Clive. I see now why Josef has placed his trust in you.

Clive: 'Tis a great honor to earn such praise from a distinguished member of the royal guard.

Hodrick: Former member, you mean. You and I stand as equals now, nothing more.

Clive: In that case, might you permit me a minor request?

Hodrick: What is it?

Clive: I should love to see that mastery in action, if you wouldn't mind. Such is the only way I shall surpass my father and see that the tragedy which befell my family never again comes to pass.

Hodrick: Now then. The greatest mentor teaches not through words, but action.

Clive: Precisely what I hoped to hear. Let us spar, Ser Hodrick!

Hodrick: I only pray you're ready for the storm which approaches.

### Clive and Josef

#### Clive and Josef - The Ashen Blue Returns

Josef: Here we are. The Province of the Ashen Blue.

Clive: Ten long years have passed since that fateful day, yet I've finally returned.

Josef: Had you not persevered in pursuing my foolish dream, this moment would ever have remained mere fantasy.

Clive: The day Zenoira seized these lands, I lost everything. Zenoira slaughtered the entire house as punishment: my mother, my sister, and even our retainers were put to the sword. The only soul spared was me. Not only was our family slain, but the very province he sought to protect fell to Zenoira in a matter of days.

Josef: Without your father's bold defiance, I wager you would not be standing here now. Even so, I would not see you held prisoner to your past. They shall see you save a great many more before this war has concluded. Do you understand, Clive?

Clive: I do. Thank you, Ser Josef.

#### Clive and Josef - Tavern

Rogue: I'm working for the Liberation, and I'm not paying a single damned gold!

Tavernkeep: But, ser...

Clive: Quite the conversation you're having here.

Rogue: Yeah? And who the hell're you?

Josef: Soldiers of the Liberation in earnest, unlike yourself.

Rogue: Oh, uh... I was just kiddin' about that! Pretty funny, right?

Clive: The wine up here in northeast Cornia is simply to die for, wouldn't you say?

Josef: Perhaps, if I was able to hold my liquor better. Yet I fear age has begun to get the better of me.

Clive: Do you remember our previous occasion, Ser Josef?

Josef: But of course. You practically drank the entire tavern dry, and grew rather unruly as a result.

Clive: 'Tis an embarrassing memory. For countless days, I awaited orders to commence the final assault against Zenoira. All the while, my mind was flooded with thoughts of the fallen. Did their sacrifice mean nothing? I had become an empty shell of my former self.

Josef: I suppose it's fate, in a way. We never would have met if not for that quarrel.

Clive: It wasn't much of a fight, of course. You knocked me flat into the wall, and in so doing returned me to my senses. I suppose it worked to my benefit in the end, both in my actions and in my finding a mentor as unfailing as you.

Josef: In any case, the shadows which once engulfed you have long since lifted.

Clive: Despite my being older than her, Monica always treated me as if I was years her junior. Yet to know she once thought of me... that she still does to this day... what a callous fool I was.

Josef: Perhaps an apology is in order, then?

Clive: You mean, after all these years? I couldn't bear the thought.

Josef: Simply tell her everything you just told me.

### Clive and Lex

#### Clive and Lex

Lex: Hey, Clive. You mind lending me your horse for a sec?

Clive: I would, in fact. The humble steed is an extension of a knight's very spirit, and not something to loan out without good reason.

Lex: Yeah, figured you'd say that.

Clive: Why do you want it, exactly?

Lex: I was a real handful as a kid. Never helped my dad with the fishing, and the only thing I ever talked about was becoming a knight. Thing is, I doubt they'll believe a word of it if I don't have a horse to march in on.

Clive: Your unwavering dedication to the crown is more than proof enough of your chivalrous deeds.

Lex: C'mon, I'm begging you!

Clive: Hm. In that case, sit here in front of me. I shall take you to your parents myself.

Lex: Yeah... I'll just walk. Think I'd look more like a noblewoman than a knight at that point.

### Clive and Liza

#### Clive and Liza

Clive: Hm. I managed to find everything I was looking for, yet I admit it was all rather pricier than usual.

Liza: Yeah, that's 'cause you got swindled.

Clive: I'm not sure I understand.

Liza: There's not a whetstone in the world worth five times the goin' price. I watched the whole damn thing go down, after all.

Clive: You mean to say you witnessed me falling victim to his deceit, and you did nothing to stop it?

Liza: That's enough for another four whole whetstones.

Clive: My thanks, both for retrieving my gold and for alerting me to the myriad dangers of this desert.

Liza: How 'bout you pay me back for it, then? Maybe we can spend that extra coin on a fancy little meal in town.

Clive: As you wish. Though let's be sure to choose a reputable establishment this time, hm?

### Clive and Monica

#### Clive and Monica

Monica: Evening, Clive. Do you always stare at the ground when you're speaking to someone? It's rude, you know.

Clive: It's not that I don't wish to meet your gaze, of course. It's merely...

Monica: Enough, Clive. I know you had your reasons for deceiving me, as did my grandfather. What's done is done.

Clive: Be that as it may, it doesn't change the manner in which I wronged you.

Monica: Bearing a grudge does me little good, knowing you only did what you thought was best. Unless there's something else you feel guilty about, of course. Should I be worried?

Clive: Even now, your iron will is as apparent in your eyes as it always has been.

Monica: I don't know what to say, Clive. You've changed as well. Years past, I could never have foreseen you standing tall against the might of Zenoira like this.

#### Clive and Monica - Sweets

Clive: Do you mind if we spoke for a moment, Monica?

Monica: Well, this is convenient. You're just the man I was looking for. You started this conversation. You first.

Clive: Of course. I'm not certain if it's still to your liking, but I bought some for you, if you would accept it.

Monica: Worry not, my tastes don't change that easily.

Clive: 'Tis a relief to hear.

Monica: Actually, perhaps we should discuss my business first. While inspecting the marketplace myself, I happened to purchase your favorite flavor of sweet bun.

Clive: Do you mean to say that bun is for me?

Monica: Who else would it be for? Strange how the stars seem to align sometimes. Perhaps we could take tea together?

Clive: Are you certain you don't mind?

Monica: I wouldn't have suggested it if I did.

Clive: Forgive me for dithering. I shall prepare for our meal at once.

Monica: I wonder, how long has it been since we've dined together like this?

Clive: Far too long, by my estimations. Thank you, Monica.

### Clive and Mordon

#### Clive and Mordon

Mordon: You there, kid. You notice you've got a nice, big chip on that lance of yours?

Clive: It would seem I'll need to procure a new one when next we're in town.

Mordon: Should be an easy fix, and if anyone can do it, it's an old stonemason like me.

Clive: I'd much appreciate that, thank you. Go right ahead.

Mordon: There you are, good as new.

Clive: What craftsmanship. You've done finer work than even my preferred blacksmith.

Mordon: Heh, glad to hear it. Now let's talk fees.

Clive: Hold a moment. You mean to demand gold from me?

Mordon: When you really think about it, this is still plenty cheaper than buying a whole new weapon.

Clive: Urgh. Just mind you keep your wits about you, hm?

Mordon: Hah! No need to worry about me, kid. I've been swimming in ale since before you were born.

#### Mordon and Clive - Lance Repair

Clive: Mordon, could you take a look at this lance?

Mordon: Bent clean out of shape. You do not do things by halves, do you?

Clive: I would prefer it restored before the next battle.

Mordon: I can manage that. Good metal, this.

Clive: I am grateful.

Mordon: Thank me after it stops trying to twist out of my hands.

### Clive and Renault

#### Renault and Clive - Redemption

Clive: 'Tis a great honor to take arms with you once more, Ser Renault.

Renault: Indeed it is, and the innocent boy I once knew has now grown into a gallant young man.

Clive: It was either that or perish in despair. I've witnessed great horrors these last ten years, ser.

Clive: At times I've wondered what right I have to survive amidst so many dead. The thought alone has nearly consumed me whole.

Renault: Yet before me stands a man of great virtue. A knight, bold and courageous in defense of his people.

Clive: Is that not what drives you as well, Ser Renault? Redemption for those you failed to save.

Renault: Quite right. Though I owe my awareness of that entirely to you.

Clive: Thank you, ser. Both for then, and for now.

Renault: It is peculiar. I had once thought to abandon this march, should my presence ever prove too great a burden.

Renault: No. I shall not complain. I'll meet this newfound esteem with conviction and pride of my own.

Clive: And I shall see you never feel troubled again.

### Colm and Lex

#### Colm and Lex - Advice from Another Retainer

Colm: Oh, Lady Melisandre. Ah, it appears I have spilled my tea.

Colm: Alas, Lady Melisandre has spurned my advice at every opportunity.

Lex: Rough day?

Colm: Actually, I was just thinking I might make that up to you.

Colm: My word. It would seem I owe you yet another apology now.

Lex: You worry about her a lot, do you not?

Colm: Perhaps so. Though as her aide, I shall gladly abide by any decision Lady Melisandre makes.

Colm: I only pray her choice leads her toward happiness, not rejection.

Colm: Before that day, my work with House Meillet was no different from any other profession.

Colm: Such marvels have brought me greater pride and greater joy than I ever thought imaginable.

Colm: I hope this conversation helps you excuse my worry, even somewhat.

### Colm and Melisandre

#### Melisandre and Colm - Lineage and Beauty

Colm: It is a sad state of affairs, my lady. He is a cruel man indeed to toy with your heart in such a manner.

Colm: Perhaps the queenship Lady Melisandre desires is not as distant as it appears to be.

Colm: Though should she marry into the royal family, none would remain to assume leadership of House Meillet.

Melisandre: What are you mumbling about over there, Colm? It is almost time we head off to bed.

Colm: Have you ever considered the impending existential danger to your lineage, my lady?

Melisandre: For now, I wish to fight at Alain's side. Even at the risk of my own demise.

Colm: I suppose you make a fair point.

Melisandre: I cannot bear the thought of Alain seeing my hair a mess, and my unblemished skin covered in disgusting sweat.

Colm: merely say the word in the midst of combat and I shall ensure you appear as fair as the light of dawn.

Colm: Thus, Prince Alain shall only ever gaze upon you at your absolute best.

Melisandre: Colm, please. If you attempted such a thing on the battlefield, neither of us would live to tell the tale.
